And the mention of father and son in the author's speech is coincidental; because the ruling is not specific to them but includes all relating by birth, for they enter into his kitaba as dependents. The closest entering is the child born during kitaba, then the purchased child, then the parents. And accordingly they differ in rulings: the child born during kitaba has the same ruling as his father, so if his father dies without leaving payment, he works for his father's installments; the purchased child pays the kitaba price immediately, otherwise he is returned to slavery; and the parents are returned to the market when the mukatib dies, and they do not pay either immediately or on credit. Rumor al-Haqa'iq: 2/294. And he only said 'becomes a mukatib' and did not say 'becomes a mukatib originally' because if he were a mukatib originally, his kitaba would remain after the original mukatib's inability, but it is not so, until if the mukatib becomes unable, the father follows him. (Mulla Miskin) And if he bought his brother, i.e. the brother by lineage who is a mahram without birth between them. (Mulla Miskin) Means if he bought his brother or others of his mahram such as his nephew, uncle, and cousin, he does not become a mukatib due to him according to Abu Hanifa in his view, so it is permissible for him to sell him; because he did not own him to prevent his sale, but if the mukatib pays, he is freed; because the earning of the mukatib is suspended between his paying so it is established for him, and his inability so it is established for the master, and here it is established for him so he is freed, and there is no sa'aya upon him; because it became like purchasing a relative from the beginning. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the brother and the like enter into the kitaba; because obligatory connection includes the mahram relatives by marriage, and therefore every mahram relative is freed upon a free person, and their maintenance is obligatory, and the mukatib has earnings but he does not have actual ownership; because of the existence of what negates it, which is slavery. And therefore if he bought his wife, his marriage is not invalidated, but the earning suffices for connection in wala'. Do you not see that the one capable of earning is addressed with the maintenance of parents, but it does not suffice for others, so the brother is not addressed with the maintenance of his brother unless he is wealthy. And know that the fruit of the disagreement in this issue between the Imam and his two companions appears in the permissibility of sale and its absence. According to him (Imam), the mukatib may sell him; according to them, no. And if the mukatib dies without payment, according to them the brother and the like take his place and work for his installments; according to Imam, he does not take his place except when the mukatib pays or dies with payment, then he is freed without dispute. (Compiled from the commentaries) 'It is not permissible to sell her' etc.: i.e. if the mukatib bought his wife with her child from him, it is not permissible for him to sell her; because the child entered into the kitaba, so his sale is prevented as we mentioned, so his mother follows him, so her sale is prevented; because she is dependent on him. 'Ali said: 'her child frees her' and she does not enter into his kitaba, so she is not freed by his freedom, and the marriage is not annulled; because he did not own her, so it is permissible for him to have intercourse with her by the right of marriage. Likewise the female mukatib if she bought her husband, except that she may sell him in any case; because the dependent part is not established from her side. Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 8/97. And if he owned her without the child and the birth was before the kitaba, it is permissible for him to sell her according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and the face of their statement: she is his umm walad.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage covers three related rulings: (1) If a mukatib buys his father or son, they automatically become mukatib like him (takatub). This is because the mukatib cannot free them (since he doesn't own the neck), but the relationship demands connection, so they enter his kitaba as dependents. The commentary details the gradation: children born during kitaba are closest, then purchased children, then parents, and each has different obligations regarding payment or return to slavery. (2) For a brother or other mahram relative (except parents/children), there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds they do NOT become mukatib, so the mukatib can sell them; but if he pays his kitaba, they are freed without sa'aya (work). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold they DO enter kitaba, cannot be sold, and if the mukatib dies insolvent, they must work for his installments. The practical difference (thamara) is highlighted: ability to sell and obligations upon death. (3) If the mukatib buys his wife with her child from him, the child enters kitaba, so the wife cannot be sold because she follows the child. The marriage remains valid. If he buys the wife without the child, and the child was born before kitaba, then Abu Hanifa allows selling her, but the two companions prohibit because she is an umm walad. The commentary follows the author's order by first discussing the father/son (agreed ruling), then the disputed brother case, then the wife/child case.

Key Terms
السعاية (al-sa'aya): The requirement for a freed slave to work to pay off the kitaba installments of his former master.
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master.
محرم (mahram): A relative with whom marriage is permanently forbidden due to blood, suckling, or marriage affinity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of the disagreement between Imam and Sahibayn on the brother?
A) The brother is freed immediately in both views.
B) The brother can be sold according to Imam but not according to Sahibayn.
C) The brother must pay the kitaba price immediately in both views.
D) The brother does not enter the kitaba according to both.

Key Takeaway
Imam and Sahibayn disagree on whether a brother enters a mukatib's kitaba, with the practical difference being the ability to sell the brother and the obligation to work if the mukatib dies insolvent.

The Ruling on a Mukatab Purchasing a Close Relative
Explains the legal status of a purchased relative of a mukatab, distinguishing types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a mukatab purchases a close blood relative, explain the reasoning based on the mukatab's lack of ownership, and distinguish the legal treatment of different categories of relatives.

Core Idea
A purchased relative of a mukatab becomes a subsidiary mukatab, not free, because the mukatab does not own his own person.

When a slave in a kitabah contract (a mukatab) purchases his own father or son, one might assume the relative becomes free due to the relationship. However, the Hanafi school rules that the relative enters into a subsidiary kitabah, becoming a mukatab tiba'an. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this ruling and the distinctions between different relatives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is a mukatab purchasing his father or son. The ruling is that the relative becomes a subsidiary mukatab, not free.
This is the established Hanafi position.
2
Examine the illah (legal cause)
The illah is that the mukatab does not own his own person (رقبته), so he cannot directly free the relative. The relative is therefore made a mukatab to actualize the cause as far as possible.
This reasoning distinguishes the mukatab from a free person.
3
Compare with the free person
If the purchaser were free, the relative would be freed immediately because a free person can own and manumit others. The free person's ability to emancipate is not precluded.
This contrast highlights the mukatab's limited capacity.
4
Distinguish between categories of relatives
The text classifies relatives into three: child born during kitabah (follows father's status fully), purchased child (must pay immediately or be returned), and parents (returned to market if mukatab dies).
The hierarchy determines the practical outcome.
5
Reflect on the precise wording
The original matn uses 'tukatib' (he makes a kitabah) rather than 'sara mukataban' (he becomes a mukatab) to indicate that this subsidiary kitabah does not survive the original mukatab's inability.
The commentator highlights this precision.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تكاتب عليه، ولو اشترى أخاه ونحوه ،لا ولو اشترى أم ولده معه لم يجز بيعها . 
المكاتب
أي مع ولده منها
تكاتب عليه لأن المكاتب من أهل أن يكاتب، فيجعل مكاتبا تحقيقا للعلة بقدر الإمكان؛ لأن المكاتب ليس بمالك رقبته، والعتق يختص بمن يملك الرقبة، فإذا تعذر الإعتاق صار مكاتبا مثله، بخلاف الحر؛ فإنه لا يتعذر الإعتاق في حقه، فيعتق عليه سواء كان أهلا للإعتاق بأن كان عاقلا بالغا أو لم يكن بأن كان صغيرا أو مجنونا، وذكر الأب والابن في كلام المصنف اتفاقي؛ لأن الحكم لا يختص . بهما بل يجميع من له قرابة ،الولادة، فإنهم يدخلون في كتابته تبعا له، وأقربهم دخولا الولد المولود في الكتابة، ثم الولد المشترى ثم الوالدان، وعلى هذا يتفاوتون في الأحكام، فإن الولد المولود في الكتابة يكون حكمه كحكم أبيه حتى إذا مات أبوه ولم يترك وفاء، يسعى على نجوم أبيه، والولد المشترى يؤدي بدل الكتابة حالا، وإلا يرد في الرق والوالدان يردان في السوق كما مات المكاتب ولا يؤديان لا حالا ولا مؤجلا. رمز الحقائق: ٢٩٤/٢]
أن
وإنما قال "تكاتب" ولم يقل: "صار مكاتبا؛ لأنه لو كان مكاتبا أصالة لبقيت كتابته بعد عجز المكاتب الأصلي، وليس كذلك، حتى إذا عجز المكاتب تبعه الأب. (ملا مسكين)
He makes them a mukatab upon himself, and if he buys his brother or the like, no [?], and if he buys his umm walad with him, it is not permissible to sell her. The mukatab's child from her? He makes them a mukatab upon himself because the mukatab is among those who can make a kitabah, so he is made a mukatab actualizing the cause as much as possible; because the mukatab does not own his own person, and manumission is specific to one who owns the person, so when manumission is not possible, he becomes a mukatab like him, unlike the free person; for manumission is not precluded in his case, so he becomes free upon him whether he is eligible for manumission by being sane and adult or not, by being a minor or insane. And the mention of father and son in the author's words is accidental; because the ruling is not restricted to them but includes all blood relatives, for they enter into his kitabah as followers. The closest of them in entry is the child born during the kitabah, then the purchased child, then the parents. And accordingly they differ in rulings: the child born during kitabah is like his father, so when his father dies leaving no assets, he works for his father's installments; the purchased child pays the kitabah price immediately, otherwise he is returned to slavery; the parents are returned to the market when the mukatab dies and they do not pay, neither immediately nor deferred. [2/294 رمز الحقائق]. That he said 'tukatibu' and did not say 'he becomes a mukatab'; because if he were originally a mukatab, his kitabah would remain after the original mukatab's inability, but it is not so; rather when the mukatab becomes unable, the father follows him. (Mulla Miskin)
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling that when a mukatab (a slave in a contract of manumission) purchases a close blood relative such as his father or son, that relative does not become free but instead becomes a mukatab tiba'an (subsidiary mukatab). The reasoning is that the mukatab does not own his own person, so he cannot manumit directly; instead, the relative is placed in a similar contract. The passage distinguishes between types of relatives: a child born during the kitabah follows the father's status entirely, working for the installments if the father dies without asset; a purchased child must pay the kitabah price immediately or be returned to slavery; parents are simply returned to the slave market upon the mukatab's death. The commentator also notes the precise wording of the original text, explaining why 'tukatibu' is used instead of 'sara mukataban' to indicate that the subsidiary kitabah does not survive the original mukatab's inability.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of kitabah with his master, working to earn his freedom by paying fixed installments.
تكاتب (tukatib): The act of making a purchased relative a mukatab (subsidiary kitabah), not freeing him directly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The father becomes free immediately.
B) The father becomes a subsidiary mukatab.
C) The father remains a slave and is returned to the market.
D) The father must pay the kitabah price immediately.

Key Takeaway
When a mukatab purchases a close blood relative, the relative enters a subsidiary kitabah, and the exact rulings vary depending on whether the relative was born during kitabah, purchased, or is a parent.

Mukatab Purchasing a Brother: The Kitabah Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on kitabah for non-lineal mahram relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a mukatab's purchase of a non-lineal mahram relative and identify the practical consequences of each position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa says the brother does not enter kitabah; Sahibayn say he does — the difference affects sale rights and death scenarios.

Imagine a mukatab (a slave under contract to earn his freedom) purchases his brother or another close relative who is a mahram. Does that relative automatically enter the kitabah and become bound to work alongside him? The Hanafi school has a well-known internal disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. This lesson unpacks that dispute and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Dispute
Recognize the scenario: a mukatab buys a mahram relative (brother, nephew, uncle, cousin). The core question is whether that relative becomes a subsidiary mukatab (enters the kitabah) or remains a regular slave that the mukatab may sell.
The relatives in question are those with whom marriage is permanently prohibited (mahram) but who are not lineal descendants.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position and Its Proof
Abu Hanifa holds that the relative does NOT enter the kitabah. His reasoning: the mukatab's earnings are suspended (not full ownership), so the purchase is like a free person buying a relative initially—the relative becomes free upon payment without needing to separately work.
The key principle: the mukatab lacks full ownership (malikiyyah) due to his own slavery, so the purchase does not trigger automatic kitabah.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position and Its Proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the relative DOES enter the kitabah. Their reasoning: the duty of maintaining family ties (silat al-rahim) applies to all mahram relatives. For a free person, such relatives become free and require maintenance; for a mukatab, his earnings are sufficient to establish this connection, even if he lacks full ownership.
They analogize to the rule that a free person's mahram relative automatically becomes free and owes no compensation.
4
Determine the Practical Consequences (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
The difference matters in two cases: (1) Sale: Abu Hanifa allows the mukatab to sell the brother; Sahibayn forbid it. (2) Death of the mukatab without assets: Sahibayn require the brother to work for the installments; Abu Hanifa only requires this if the mukatab died with assets or had paid.
This is the fruit of the ikhtilaf—the real-world application that affects rights and obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اشترى أخاه [ أي الأخ في القرابة وهو كل ذي رحم محرم لا ولاد بينهما. ملا مسكين)] يعني لو اشترى أخاه أو غيره من محارمه مثل ابن أخيه وعمه وابن عمه لا يتكاتب عليه عند أبي حنيفة محله حتى يجوز له بيعه؛ لأنه لم يملكه ليمتنع بيعه، لكنه إذا أدى المكاتب عتق؛ لأن كسب المكاتب موقوف بين أن يؤدي فيتقرر له، وبين يعجز ويتقرر للمولى وههنا تقرر له فعتق عليه، ولا سعاية عليه؛ لأنه صار كشراء القريب ابتداء، وعندهما: يدخل الأخ ونحوه في الكتابة؛ لأن وجوب الصلة يشمل القرابة المحرمة للنكاح ، ولهذا يعتق على الحر كل ذي رحم محرم وتجب نفقتهم وله أن للمكاتب كسبا وليس له ملك حقيقة؛ لوجود ما ينافيه وهو الرق، ولهذا لو اشترى امرأته لا يفسد نكاحه غير أن الكسب يكفي للصلة في الولاء، ألا ترى أن القادر على الكسب يخاطب بنفقة الأبوين، ولا يكفي في غيرها حتى لا يخاطب الأخ بنفقة أخيه إلا إذا كان موسرا. واعلم أن ثمرة الخلاف في هذه المسألة بين الإمام وصاحبيه تظهر في جواز البيع وعدمه، فعنده: للمكاتب بيعه، وعندهما لا، وفيما إذا مات المكاتب لا عن وفاء فعندهما يقوم الأخ ونحوه مقامه، ويسعى على نجومه؛ وعند الإمام: لا يقوم مقامه إلا فيما إذا أدى المكاتب أو مات عن وفاء، فإنه يعتق عليه بلا خلاف. (ملتقط من الشروح)
And if he buys his brother [i.e., the brother in kinship, which is every mahram relative not connected by birth. Mulla Miskin)] meaning if he buys his brother or other mahram relatives like his nephew, paternal uncle, and cousin, he does not become a mukatab upon him according to Abu Hanifa in his view, so it is permissible for him to sell him; because he did not own him so as to prevent his sale. But if the mukatab pays (the kitabah), he becomes free, because the earnings of the mukatab are suspended: if he pays it is established for him, if he becomes unable it is established for the master, and here it is established for him so he becomes free upon him, and no work (for the master) is required; because it becomes like the initial purchase of a relative. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the brother and similar enter the kitabah; because the obligation of connection includes mahram relatives, and for this reason every mahram relative becomes free upon a free person and their maintenance is obligatory, and he (the mukatab) has earnings but does not have real ownership; due to the presence of what contradicts it, which is slavery. For this reason if he buys his wife, his marriage is not invalidated, but earnings are sufficient for connection in patronage. Do you not see that the one capable of earning is addressed for the maintenance of parents, but it is not sufficient for others, so a brother is not addressed for the maintenance of his brother unless he is well-off. And know that the fruit of the difference in this issue between the Imam and his two companions appears in the permissibility of sale and its non-permissibility. According to him: the mukatab may sell him; according to them: no. And if the mukatab dies without assets, according to them the brother and similar stand in his place and work for his installments; according to the Imam: he does not stand in his place except if the mukatab paid or died with assets, then he becomes free upon him without dispute. (Selected from the commentaries)
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the purchase of a brother or similar non-lineal mahram relative by a mukatab. According to Abu Hanifa, the purchased relative does not become a subsidiary mukatab; thus the mukatab may sell him. However, if the mukatab eventually completes his kitabah payments, the brother becomes free as a result of the mukatab's earnings being established for him, and no compensation (sa'i) is required. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), the brother does enter the kitabah, because the duty of maintaining connection (silat al-rahim) applies to all mahram relatives. For a free person, such relatives become free and are entitled to maintenance. For a mukatab, though he lacks full ownership, his earnings are sufficient to establish the connection (patronage). The practical consequence (thamarah) of this difference is that Abu Hanifa allows the mukatab to sell the brother, while the Sahibayn do not. Additionally, if the mukatab dies without assets, the Sahibayn say the brother must work to pay off the installments, whereas Abu Hanifa says the brother only stands in place if the mukatab had paid or died with assets.

Key Terms
قرابة محرم (qarabah muharramah): A mahram relative, one whom one cannot marry due to blood relationship.
سعاية (sa'y): Work (or earning) that a slave must do to pay off a debt or kitabah; here, required from the brother to pay installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The brother becomes a subsidiary mukatab.
B) The mukatab may sell the brother.
C) The brother becomes free immediately.
D) The mukatab must free the brother upon payment.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on a mukatab purchasing a non-lineal mahram relative hinges on the nature of the mukatab's ownership and the duty of silat al-rahim, with practical consequences for sale and death.

Child Born to Mukatab's Slave Woman Enters Kitabah
Ruling on the child of a mukatab's slave woman becoming a subsidiary mukatab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the child of a mukatab born from his slave woman and explain the legal reasoning, including the response to the objection based on the prohibition of tassari.

Core Idea
The child enters the kitabah as a subsidiary, its earnings for the mukatab, even though intercourse is prohibited.

This passage addresses the status of a child born to a mukatab from his own slave woman. The mukatab is a slave who has contracted to purchase his freedom, and his right to concubinage (tassari) is restricted. The author presents the ruling that the child enters the kitabah and explains the underlying rationale, then raises and resolves a critical objection: if the mukatab cannot lawfully have intercourse, how can paternity be established and the child attached to his kitabah?

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The child of a mukatab from his slave woman enters the mukatab's kitabah contract as a subsidiary. The child's earnings belong to the mukatab.
The same rule applies if a female mukatab gives birth.
2
Trace the Reasoning
The basis is that paternity is established by the mukatab's claim (da'wa). Once lineage is fixed, the child follows the father in the kitabah, and since the child is effectively the mukatab's property, its earnings are his.
The child is considered legally akin to the mukatab's property for the purposes of the contract.
3
Examine the Objection
An objector argues that a mukatab does not own the right to concubinage (tassari), so he is not permitted to have intercourse with his slave woman. How then can he have a child that enters his kitabah?
This objection is based on the prohibition of unlawful intercourse.
4
Analyze the Response
The answer distinguishes between the permissibility of the act and its legal consequences. Although intercourse is not permissible, if it occurs and the mukatab claims the child, paternity is nevertheless legally established. Thus, the child enters the kitabah.
The ruling is based on the establishment of lineage, not on the lawfulness of the act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن ولد له إلخ : يعني إن ولد للمكاتب من أمته ولد دخل الولد في كتابته؛ لأنه بالدعوة تثبت النسب له، فيتبعه في الكتابة، ويكون كسب الولد للمكاتب؛ لأنه في حكم مملوكه ، فكان كسبه له وكذا لو ولدت المكاتبة ولدا دخل في كتابتها كما سنذكره، قال في "العناية : واعترض عليه بأن المكاتب لا يملك التسري فمن أين له ولد الأمة حتى يدخل في الكتابة؟ وأجيب بأن معنى قولنا: "لا يملك" لا يحل له وطء أمته ولكن إن وطئ وادعى النسب ثبت تكملة البحر الرائق: ۹۸/۸]
And if a child is born to him etc.: meaning if a child is born to the mukatab from his slave woman, the child enters his kitabah; because by his claim (of paternity) the lineage is established for him, so the child follows him in the kitabah, and the earnings of the child are for the mukatab; because the child is in the ruling of his property, so its earnings are his. Similarly, if a female mukatab gives birth to a child, it enters her kitabah as we will mention. He said in al-'Inayah: An objection was raised that the mukatab does not own the right of tassari (taking concubines), so how can he have a child from his slave woman to enter the kitabah? And it was answered: The meaning of our statement 'he does not own' is that it is not permissible for him to have intercourse with his slave woman, but if he does have intercourse and claims paternity, the lineage is established. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/98)
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage states that if a mukatab's slave woman gives birth to his child, the child becomes a subsidiary mukatab (tiba'an) and its earnings belong to the mukatab. The child follows the father in the kitabah because the father establishes paternity by claiming the child. An objection is raised: the mukatab is not permitted to have concubinage (tassari) with his slave woman—meaning he is not allowed to have sexual relations with her—so how can paternity be established? The answer is that although it is not permissible for him to have intercourse, if he does so and claims the child, the lineage is nevertheless established legally. Thus the child enters the kitabah. The same rule applies if a female mukatab gives birth: the child enters her kitabah.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a kitabah contract to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
كتابة (kitabah): A contract of manumission by which a slave agrees to pay a sum to the master in exchange for freedom.
أمة (amah): A female slave.
تسري (tassari): The right of a master to take his slave woman as a concubine for sexual relations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the child of a mukatab born from his slave woman according to the Hanafi school?
A) The child is free immediately because the mukatab is the father.
B) The child becomes a slave of the original master (the mukatab's master).
C) The child enters the mukatab's kitabah and its earnings go to the mukatab.
D) The child remains a slave of the mukatab but does not enter the kitabah.

Key Takeaway
The child of a mukatab from his slave woman enters the kitabah contract as a subsidiary, and its earnings belong to the mukatab, even though the mukatab is prohibited from concubinage.

advanced
12 min
Kitabah of Umm Walad and Mudabbar with Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Sa'y
Validates kitabah for umm walad and mudabbar and explains the intra-Hanafi sa'y dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of kitabah for umm walad and mudabbar, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on sa'y upon the master's death, including the basis in the divisibility of emancipation.

Core Idea
Kitabah is valid for umm walad and mudabbar, but the sa'y obligation upon death reveals a deep intra-Hanafi split on divisibility of emancipation.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq covers two related issues: the permissibility of contracting kitabah with an umm walad or mudabbar, and the subsequent dispute among the Hanafi imams on what the mudabbar owes when the master dies poor. While the master's ownership supports the kitabah, the combined status of tadbir and kitabah at death sparks a famous three-way disagreement. Understanding the root cause — whether emancipation is divisible — is key to mastering this discussion.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling on kitabah validity
Identify that kitabah is valid for umm walad and mudabbar because the master owns them, even though umm walad is not a commodity. Note the purpose: providing a path to freedom.
Umm walad requires freedom before master's death; kitabah fulfills this.
2
Identify consequences at master's death
For umm walad: she becomes free without payment and kitabah debt is cancelled. For mudabbar: if master dies poor, he must perform sa'y (work to pay) either two-thirds value or the entire substitute, with a dispute.
If master has other assets, mudabbar is freed from those assets and no sa'y.
3
List the three intra-Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa gives choice between two-thirds value (immediate) or full substitute (deferred). Abu Yusuf: lesser of two-thirds value or full substitute, no choice. Muhammad: lesser of two-thirds value or two-thirds substitute, no choice.
Disagreement on both choice (takhyir) and quantum (miqdar).
4
Analyse the basis of the dispute
The root is whether emancipation is divisible (tajazzu' al-i'taq). Abu Hanifa: only one-third freed by tadbir, so remaining two-thirds still under kitabah, creating two obligations. Sahibayn: emancipation of one-third frees the whole, dissolving kitabah, so only one amount due.
Abu Hanifa's view aligns with qiyas on partial emancipation; Sahibayn see tadbir as indivisible.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical difference
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's, giving the slave a beneficial choice between immediate smaller payment or deferred larger payment. This benefits the slave. The thamarah is that the slave can choose the easier option.
Tarjih by later scholars like Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir.

وإن كاتب أم ولده إلخ: يعني صح أن يكاتب المولى أم ولده أو مدبره؛ لأن ملكه ثابت في كل واحد منهما، وإن كانت أم الولد غير متقومة عند الإمام فإنها تحتاج إلى استفادة الحرية قبل موت المولى، وذلك بالكتابة، ولا تنافي بينهما؛ لأنه تلقته جهتا حرية. (ملتقط) كتاب المكاتب ١٩٩ كتابة أم ولد والمدبر صح، وعتقت مجانا بموته، وسعى المدبر في ثلثي قيمته أو كل البدل بموته فقيرا، أم الولد المكاتبة أي موت المولى وإن دبر مکاتبه المولى المكاتب صح، فإن عجز بقي مدبرا، التدبير نفسه أي اعترف بعجزه حال كونه يسعى في صح: عقد الكتابة حتى لو أديا بدل الكتابة قبل موت المولى عتقا بالكتابة. (مسكين) وعتقت مجانا إلخ: أي عتقت أم الولد بموت المولى بغير شيء يلزمها وسقط عنها بدل الكتابة؛ لأنها عتقت بالاستيلاد، وتسلم لها الأكساب والأولاد ؛ لأنها عتقت وهي مكاتبة وملكها يمنع من ثبوت ملك الغير فيه، فصار كما إذا أعتقها المولى في حال حياته، ولئن انفسخت الكتابة في حقها بقيت الحرية في حق الأولاد والأكساب؛ لأن الفسخ للنظر، والنظر فيما ذكرنا، ولو أدت البدل قبل موت المولى عتقت بالكتابة كبقائها إلى وقت الأداء، وبالأداء تقرر، ولا يبطل. تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٠٣/٨] (عيني) وسعى المدبر إلخ: أي إن مات المولى فقيرا لا مال له سوى عبده المدبر ثم المكاتب، فهو مخير بين أن أن ثلثي قيمته، وبين في كل البدل عند أبي حنيفة لله، وعند أبي يوسف يسعى في الأقل من ثلثي القيمة يسعى وكل البدل، وعند محمد الله: يسعى في الأقل من ثلثي القيمة وثلثي البدل فالخلاف في موضعين في التخيير وفي المقدار، فأبو يوسف محليه محمد في عدم التخيير ومع أبي حنيفة حاله في المقدار، والكلام في الخيار ونفيه مبني على تجزئ الإعتاق ،وعدمه، فعنده لما كان متجزئا بقي ما وراء الثلث عبدا وبقيت الكتابة فيه كما كانت قبل عتق الثلث، فتوجه لعتقه :جهتان كتابة مؤجلة وسعاية معجلة فيخير وعندهما لما عتق كله بعتق ثلثه بطلت الكتابة وبطل الأجل، ووجب عليه أحد المالين فيختار الأقل، فلا معنى للتخيير. مع وأما في المقدار فلمحمد أنه قابل البدل بالكل، وقد سلم الثلث بالتدبير، فمن المحال أن يجب البدل؛ لأن الكتابة صادفت كله، وقد عتق الثلث بالتدبير، فيبطل ما بإزائه من البدل ولهما أن جميع بدل الكتابة مقابل بثلثي رقبته، فلا يسقط منه شيء، ثم في التخيير عند أبي حنيفة محله فائدة؛ الجواز أن أكثر المالين أيسر باعتبار الأجل، وأقلهما أعسر أداء؛ لكونه حالا، فكان في التخيير فائدة وإن كان جنس المال متحدا، كذا في "الفتح" عن "الزيلعي"، واستفيد منه أنه يسعى في ثلثي قيمته حال أداء كل البدل موجلا، فافهم، وإنما قيد بقوله : "فقيرا"؛ لأنه لو مات وترك أن بالخيار بين الثلث، عتق مالا يخرج المدبر من وسقط بدل الكتابة. ملتقط من العيني والفتح وملا مسكين بالتدبير، وإن دبر مكاتبه إلخ: أي أن يدبر المولى مكاتبه؛ لأنه يملك تنجيز العتق بعد الكتابة، فيملك التعليق يصح بشرط، وهذا التصرف نافع له؛ لاحتمال أن يموت المولى قبل أداء بدل الكتابة، فيعتق مجانا أو يعجز عن أداء بدل الكتابة، فيبقى مدبرا تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٠٤/٨] فإن عجز إلخ إما من التعجيز أي عجز نفسه بمعنى اعترف بعجزه، أو من العجز أي عجز عن الكتابة، والحاصل: المكاتب الذي دبره المولى إن عجز عن الكتابة بقي مدبرا؛ لوجود السبب الموجب له. (محشي)
And if he made kitabah of his umm walad etc.: That is, it is valid for the master to make kitabah of his umm walad or his mudabbar, because his ownership is established over each of them, even though the umm walad is not a commodity (muttaqawwama) according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa), she needs to obtain freedom before the master's death, and that is by kitabah, and there is no contradiction between them because two directions of freedom have come to her. (Multaqat) Kitab al-Mukatab 199: Kitabah of umm walad and mudabbar is valid, and she becomes free without payment (majjānan) upon his death, and the mudabbar must seek (sa'y) in two-thirds of his value or the entire substitute upon his death if he dies poor. The mukatabah umm walad means upon the master's death. And if he made tadbir of his mukatab, the master's tadbir of the mukatab is valid; if he becomes incapable, he remains mudabbar; tadbir itself means he admits his incapacity while he seeks to fulfill the kitabah contract. Even if they paid the kitabah substitute before the master's death, they become free by kitabah. (Miskin) 'And she becomes free without payment etc.': That is, the umm walad becomes free upon the master's death without anything incumbent upon her, and the kitabah substitute falls from her because she becomes free by istilad, and her earnings and children are secured to her because she became free while she was a mukatabah, and her ownership prevents the establishment of any other's ownership over it, so it is as if the master had freed her during his lifetime. Even if the kitabah is dissolved in her regard, freedom remains for the children and earnings because the dissolution is for her benefit. If she paid the substitute before the master's death, she becomes free by kitabah as if she remained until the time of payment, and by payment it is confirmed and is not void. [Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 103/8] ('Ayni) 'And the mudabbar must seek etc.': That is, if the master dies poor with no property except his mudabbar slave and then the mukatab, he (the mudabbar) has the choice between two-thirds of his value and the entire substitute according to Abu Hanifa. According to Abu Yusuf, he must seek the lesser of two-thirds of the value or the entire substitute. According to Muhammad, he must seek the lesser of two-thirds of the value or two-thirds of the substitute. So the disagreement is in two points: in the choice and in the amount. Abu Yusuf is with Muhammad on the absence of choice and with Abu Hanifa on the amount. The discussion on choice and its negation is based on the divisibility of emancipation and its absence. According to Abu Hanifa, since emancipation is divisible, what remains beyond one-third remains a slave, and the kitabah remains in it as before the emancipation of one-third, so he faces two directions: a deferred kitabah and an immediate sa'y, so he is given a choice. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), since the entire slave is emancipated by the emancipation of one-third, the kitabah is invalidated and the deferment is invalidated, so one of the two amounts is incumbent upon him, so he chooses the lesser, thus no choice. As for the amount, according to Muhammad, he compares the substitute to the entire, and one-third is secured by tadbir, so it is impossible for the entire substitute to be required because the kitabah encompassed all of him, and one-third was emancipated by tadbir, so the portion of the substitute corresponding to it is void. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa), all of the kitabah substitute is in exchange for two-thirds of his slave-body, so nothing falls. Then in the choice according to Abu Hanifa there is a benefit because the larger of the two amounts is easier due to deferment, and the smaller is harder to pay because it is immediate, so the choice has a benefit even if the type of property is the same. As in al-Fath from al-Zayla'i. From this it is understood that he seeks two-thirds of his value immediately or the whole substitute deferred, so understand. He restricted it by saying 'poor' because if he died leaving property that covers the mudabbar, he is freed and the kitabah substitute falls. (Multaqat from al-'Ayni, al-Fath, and Mulla Miskin on tadbir) 'And if he made tadbir of his mukatab etc.': That is, if the master makes tadbir of his mukatab, because he has the power to execute emancipation after kitabah, so he possesses the power to make a conditional emancipation, and this action is beneficial to him because it is possible that the master dies before the mukatab pays the kitabah substitute, so he becomes free without payment, or he becomes incapable of paying and remains mudabbar. [Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 104/8] 'If he becomes incapable etc.' either by ta'jiz (causing incapacity) meaning he declares himself incapable, or by 'ajz (incapacity) meaning he becomes unable to fulfill the kitabah. Conclusion: The mukatab whom the master has made tadbir remains mudabbar if he becomes incapable of kitabah due to the existence of the cause. (Mahshi)
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This lesson covers two interrelated topics: the validity of kitabah for umm walad and mudabbar, and the intra-Hanafi dispute on the sa'y obligation upon the master's death. First, it is established that a master can validly contract kitabah with his umm walad or mudabbar because he owns them, despite the special status of umm walad (non-commodity). The covenant is beneficial as it provides an early path to freedom. If the master dies, the umm walad becomes free automatically (istilad) and the kitabah debt is cancelled; if she paid before death, she is free by kitabah. For the mudabbar (a slave whose freedom is tied to the master's death), if the master dies poor with only the mudabbar and the mukatab, the mudabbar must perform sa'y (work to pay) either two-thirds of his value or the entire kitabah substitute, but there is a disagreement among the three Hanafi imams. Abu Hanifa gives him the choice between two-thirds of his value (paid immediately) or the entire substitute (deferred). Abu Yusuf obliges the lesser of two-thirds the value or the whole substitute, with no choice. Muhammad obliges the lesser of two-thirds the value or two-thirds of the substitute, also no choice. The root of the dispute is whether emancipation is divisible: Abu Hanifa holds that only one-third is freed by tadbir, leaving two-thirds as a slave with kitabah; thus the slave faces two obligations and can choose. The Sahibayn hold that the entire slave is freed by the one-third emancipation, dissolving kitabah, so only one amount is due. On the quantum, Muhammad argues that the kitabah was for the entire slave, but one-third is freed by tadbir, so that portion of the substitute is void; the Sahibayn counter that the substitute was only for the remaining two-thirds. The lesson also discusses tadbir of a mukatab: a master can make tadbir for his mukatab, which is beneficial in case of death or incapacity. If the mukatab becomes incapable of paying, he becomes a mudabbar (waiting for the master's death).

Key Terms
المدبر (al-mudabbar): A slave whose freedom is conditioned upon the master's death, like a will.
السعاية (al-sa‘āyah): The obligation of the mudabbar to work and pay a sum to cover the shortfall in the estate.
التخيير (al-takhyīr): The choice given to the mudabbar in Abu Hanifa's view between two amounts.
التجزئ (al-tajazzu’): Divisibility; here, the doctrine that emancipation can be partial, so tadbir only frees one-third.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what choice does a mudabbar mukatab have when the master dies poor?
A) He must pay two-thirds of his value immediately.
B) He can choose between two-thirds of his value (immediate) or the entire kitabah substitute (deferred).
C) He must pay the lesser of two-thirds of his value or the entire substitute.
D) He must pay the lesser of two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the substitute.

Key Takeaway
The sa'y dispute among the Hanafi imams hinges on whether emancipation is divisible, with Abu Hanifa giving the slave a beneficial choice.

10 min
Kitabah of Mudabbir Upon Master's Death: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Choice and Amount
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mudabbir's sa'y after master's death poor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi positions on the mudabbir's obligation when the master dies poor and identify the usul principle (tajazzu' al-i'taq) that underlies the dispute.

Core Idea
The mudabbir's obligation hinges on whether emancipation is divisible; this determines choice and quantum.

This passage tackles a nuanced scenario: a slave who is both mudabbir (freed upon master's death) and mukatab (freed upon paying a debt). When the master dies poor, how much must the slave work (sa'y) to secure freedom? The matn gives the basic ruling, but the commentary unpacks a rich intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The root of the difference lies in the usul principle of tajazzu' al-i'taq (divisibility of emancipation). Understanding this ikhtilaf deepens your grasp of how Hanafi usul generates concrete fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The case: a slave is both mudabbir (declared free upon master's death) and mukatab (under kitabah contract). The master dies poor, leaving no wealth beyond the slave's value. Determine the legal status of the slave and the obligations.
The slave is not yet free at death; freedom is conditional on payment or working.
2
State the Three Hanafi Positions
List the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding choice and amount. Abu Hanifa gives a choice between two alternatives; the Sahibayn negate choice and specify a single amount.
Refer to the commentary for exact formulations.
3
Trace the Ikhtilaf to the Usul Principle
Identify tajazzu' al-i'taq as the underlying principle. Abu Hanifa holds emancipation is divisible, so the slave remains partially slave after tadbir frees one-third. The Sahibayn hold it is indivisible, so the entire slave becomes free upon tadbir of one-third, voiding the kitabah.
This principle directly determines the existence of choice and the quantum of debt.
4
Analyze the Practical Consequence (Thamarah)
For each imam, calculate what the slave pays: two-thirds of value, entire debt, or a portion. Note the timing (immediate vs deferred).
Abu Hanifa's choice includes a deferred option; Sahibayn's amount is immediate.
5
Consider the Restriction 'Poor'
Why does the author specify 'poor'? If the master had left wealth, the mudabbir would be freed from the one-third by tadbir and the kitabah debt drops entirely.
The restriction isolates the dispute to the case where the slave must work.

كتاب المكاتب
۱۹۹
كتابة أم ولد والمدبر
صح، وعتقت مجانا بموته، وسعى المدبر في ثلثي قيمته أو كل البدل بموته فقيرا، أم الولد المكاتبة أي موت المولى
صح: عقد الكتابة حتى لو أديا بدل الكتابة قبل موت المولى عتقا بالكتابة. (مسكين) وعتقت مجانا إلخ: أي عتقت أم الولد بموت المولى بغير شيء يلزمها وسقط عنها بدل الكتابة؛ لأنها عتقت بالاستيلاد، وتسلم لها الأكساب والأولاد؛ لأنها عتقت وهي مكاتبة وملكها يمنع من ثبوت ملك الغير فيه، فصار كما إذا أعتقها المولى في حال حياته، ولئن انفسخت الكتابة في حقها بقيت الحرية في حق الأولاد والأكساب؛ لأن الفسخ للنظر، والنظر فيما ذكرنا، ولو أدت البدل قبل موت المولى عتقت بالكتابة كبقائها إلى وقت الأداء، وبالأداء تقرر، ولا يبطل. تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٠٣/٨] (عيني) وسعى المدبر إلخ: أي إن مات المولى فقيرا لا مال له سوى عبده المدبر ثم المكاتب، فهو مخير بين أن أن ثلثي قيمته، وبين في كل البدل عند أبي حنيفة لله، وعند أبي يوسف يسعى في الأقل من ثلثي القيمة يسعى وكل البدل، وعند محمد الله: يسعى في الأقل من ثلثي القيمة وثلثي البدل فالخلاف في موضعين في التخيير وفي المقدار، فأبو يوسف محليه محمد في عدم التخيير ومع أبي حنيفة حاله في المقدار، والكلام في الخيار ونفيه مبني على تجزئ الإعتاق، وعدمه، فعنده لما كان متجزئا بقي ما وراء الثلث عبدا وبقيت الكتابة فيه كما كانت قبل عتق الثلث، فتوجه لعتقه: جهتان كتابة مؤجلة وسعاية معجلة فيخير وعندهما لما عتق كله بعتق ثلثه بطلت الكتابة وبطل الأجل، ووجب عليه أحد المالين فيختار الأقل، فلا معنى للتخيير.
مع
وأما في المقدار فلمحمد أنه قابل البدل بالكل، وقد سلم الثلث بالتدبير، فمن المحال أن يجب البدل؛ لأن الكتابة صادفت كله، وقد عتق الثلث بالتدبير، فيبطل ما بإزائه من البدل ولهما أن جميع بدل الكتابة مقابل بثلثي رقبته، فلا يسقط منه شيء، ثم في التخيير عند أبي حنيفة محله فائدة؛ الجواز أن أكثر المالين أيسر باعتبار الأجل، وأقلهما أعسر أداء؛ لكونه حالا، فكان في التخيير فائدة وإن كان جنس المال متحدا، كذا في "الفتح" عن "الزيلعي"، واستفيد منه أنه يسعى في ثلثي قيمته حال أداء كل البدل موجلا، فافهم، وإنما قيد بقوله: "فقيرا"؛ لأنه لو مات وترك

الثلث، عتق
مالا يخرج المدبر من وسقط بدل الكتابة. ملتقط من العيني والفتح وملا مسكين بالتدبير
The Book of Mukatab. Section: Kitabah of Umm Walad and Mudabbir. It is valid. And she (umm walad) becomes free for free upon his death. And the mudabbir works for two-thirds of his value or the entire debt upon his death if he is poor. The umm walad who is a mukatabah upon the master's death: [commentary] The contract of kitabah is valid; even if they paid the kitabah debt before the master's death they become free by kitabah. (Miskin) 'And she becomes free for free' etc.: i.e., the umm walad becomes free upon the master's death without anything incumbent on her, and the kitabah debt is dropped from her because she becomes free by istilad. Her earnings and children are given to her because she became free while being a mukatabah, and her ownership prevents the establishment of another's ownership over her. So it is as if the master freed her during his life. Even if the kitabah is rescinded with respect to her, freedom remains with respect to the children and earnings because the rescission is for her benefit. If she paid the debt before the master's death, she becomes free by kitabah as if she remained until the time of payment, and with payment it is confirmed and does not become void. (completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:103) (Ayni) 'And the mudabbir works' etc.: i.e., if the master died poor, having no wealth except his mudabbir slave and then the mukatab, then he (the slave) is given a choice between working for two-thirds of his value and the entire debt according to Abu Hanifa. According to Abu Yusuf, he works for the lesser of two-thirds of the value and the entire debt. According to Muhammad, he works for the lesser of two-thirds of the value and two-thirds of the debt. Thus there is disagreement in two matters: the choice (takhyir) and the amount. Abu Yusuf agrees with Muhammad in negating the choice and with Abu Hanifa in the amount. The discussion of choice and its negation is based on whether emancipation is divisible (tajazzu') or not. According to Abu Hanifa, since it is divisible, what remains beyond the one-third remains a slave and the kitabah remains in that portion as before the emancipation of the one-third, so two considerations face his emancipation: deferred kitabah and immediate working. So he is given a choice. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), since all of him becomes free by the emancipation of one-third, the kitabah is invalidated and the deferment is invalidated, so one of the two amounts becomes incumbent upon him and he chooses the lesser; thus there is no meaning to choice. As for the amount, according to Muhammad, the debt is matched to the entire slave; one-third has been freed by tadbir, so it is impossible that the full debt be due because the kitabah applied to all of him, and one-third has become free by tadbir, so what corresponds to that is void. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), all of the kitabah debt is matched to two-thirds of his value, so nothing is dropped. Then in the choice according to Abu Hanifa there is a benefit; it is possible that the greater of the two amounts is easier due to the deferment, and the lesser is more difficult to pay because it is immediate, so there is benefit in the choice even if the type of wealth is the same. This is from al-Fath from al-Zayla'i. And from it it is understood that he works for two-thirds of his value while paying all of the debt deferred. So understand. And he (the author) only restricted by saying 'poor' because if he died and left wealth that covers the mudabbir from the one-third, he becomes free and the kitabah debt drops. (Collected from al-Ayni and al-Fath and Mulla Miskin on tadbir)
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the kitabah of umm walad and mudabbir when the master dies poor. The matn states the basic ruling: the umm walad becomes free for free (i.e., no need to pay the kitabah debt) because her freedom comes through istilad (bearing a child to the master), which overrides the kitabah contract. For the mudabbir who is also a mukatab, the master's death triggers either working for two-thirds of his value or the entire kitabah debt. The commentary then explains the ikhtilaf among the three Hanafi imams. Abu Hanifa gives the slave a choice between two alternatives, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say he must pay the lesser of the two amounts. The difference is rooted in whether emancipation is considered divisible (tajazzu' al-i'taq): Abu Hanifa holds it is divisible, so only one-third of the slave is freed by tadbir, and the kitabah remains on the remaining two-thirds. Thus there are two concurrent obligations (deferred kitabah and immediate working), and the slave may choose. The Sahibayn hold emancipation is indivisible, so the entire slave becomes free when one-third is freed, voiding the kitabah and leaving only one obligation (the lesser amount). On the amount due, Muhammad argues that since the kitabah debt corresponds to the entire slave and one-third is freed by tadbir, one-third of the debt should drop. Abu Yusuf and the text (representing the position of the two) say the entire debt is matched to the two-thirds that remain slave, so nothing drops. The passage also notes a practical benefit of the choice: the larger amount may be easier due to deferral. The restriction to 'poor' ensures that if the master leaves enough wealth to cover the mudabbir from the one-third (i.e., the tadbir is effective), the slave becomes free without any working.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered a kitabah contract with his master to pay a sum for freedom.
مدبر (mudabbir): A slave whose master has declared him free upon the master's death (tadbir).
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master.
تجزئ الإعتاق (tajazzu' al-i'taq): The principle that emancipation can be partial and divisible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what options does a mudabbir/mukatab have when the master dies poor?
A) He must pay two-thirds of the kitabah debt immediately.
B) He may choose between working for two-thirds of his value or the entire kitabah debt.
C) He must pay the lesser of two-thirds of his value or the entire debt.
D) He becomes free without any payment.

Key Takeaway
The dispute over the mudabbir's sa'y illustrates how a fundamental usul principle (tajazzu' al-i'taq) directly shapes the fiqh ruling, and knowing the positions of the three imams is essential for proper istifta'.

The Mukatab-Mudabbir Dispute: Choice or Fixed Amount?
Ruling on mukatab made mudabbir with master's insolvent death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the slave's obligation when a mukatab is made a mudabbir and the master dies insolvent, and apply the agreed calculation of two-thirds.

Core Idea
When a mukatab is made mudabbir and master dies insolvent, Abu Hanifa grants choice; Sahibayn fix the lesser amount.

This lesson examines a specific scenario where a master has both a kitabah (contract of manumission) and a tadbir (declaration of freedom upon death) over the same slave. When the master dies insolvent, the slave must work to earn full freedom, but how much? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, on whether the slave has a choice or must pay the lesser of two amounts. The passage also explains the agreed-upon calculation of two-thirds and the condition of the master's insolvency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Establish that the master first made a mukatab contract, then later made that same slave a mudabbir. The master dies insolvent (leaving no other estate). The slave has not failed to pay the kitabah installments.
If the slave fails (ta'jiz), he becomes a mudabbir only, no dispute.
2
State the dispute
Abu Hanifa holds that the slave has a choice: he may work for two-thirds of his market value or two-thirds of the remaining kitabah debt. The Sahibayn hold that he must work for the lesser of these two amounts.
The amount is agreed; the dispute is only about the choice (takhyir).
3
Explain the common calculation
Both sides agree that when kitabah preceded tadbir, the entire kitabah debt is matched to the whole slave. When tadbir frees one-third of the slave, exactly one-third of the debt drops. The remaining debt equals two-thirds of the original, and the remaining value is two-thirds of the slave's value. Thus the alternatives are two-thirds of value or two-thirds of debt.
This differs from the reverse order (tadbir first, then kitabah).
4
Trace the usul basis
The dispute is rooted in the divisibility (tajazzu') of emancipation. Abu Hanifa considers emancipation divisible, so the slave can choose which portion of the debt to offset. The Sahibayn consider emancipation indivisible, so no choice exists and the lesser is automatically due.
This principle was explained in a previous passage on a related issue.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the slave may choose the easier option (e.g., if value is low, he works for value; if debt is low, he works for debt). Under the Sahibayn, only the lesser is required, which might be beneficial if the lesser is indeed low, but the slave cannot choose a higher option if that somehow benefits him (e.g., if he prefers to work more to clear a larger debt faster).
No tarjih is given in this text; later fatwa may adopt the Sahibayn's view as more protective of the slave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن دبر مکاتبه إلخ: أي أن يدبر المولى مكاتبه؛ لأنه يملك تنجيز العتق بعد الكتابة، فيملك التعليق يصح بشرط، وهذا التصرف نافع له؛ لاحتمال أن يموت المولى قبل أداء بدل الكتابة، فيعتق مجانا أو يعجز عن أداء بدل الكتابة، فيبقى مدبرا تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٠٤/٨] فإن عجز إلخ إما من التعجيز أي عجز نفسه بمعنى اعترف بعجزه، أو من العجز أي عجز عن الكتابة، والحاصل: المكاتب الذي دبره المولى إن عجز عن الكتابة بقي مدبرا؛ لوجود السبب الموجب له. (محشي)
وإلا سعى في ثلثي قيمته أو ثلثي البدل بموته معسرا وإلا سعى إلخ يعني إن لم يعجز ومات المولى معسرا، فهو بالخيار بين أن يسعى في ثلثي قيمته أو ثلثي بدل الكتابة وهذا عند الإمام وقالا : يسعى في الأقل منهما، فالخلاف هنا في الخيار فقط، فعنده يخير بينهما، وعندهما: لا يتخير بل يتعين الأقل، وهو مبني على تجزي الإعتاق وعدمه، وقد . بيانه في المسألة المتقدمة. وأما المقدار هنا فمتفق عليه لا خلاف فيه؛ لأن بدل الكتابة مقابل بكل الرقبة؛ إذ لم يستحق المكاتب شيئا من الحرية قبل ذلك، فإذا عتق بعض الرقبة مجانا بعد ذلك سقط حصته من بدل الكتابة بخلاف ما إذا تقدم التدبير، ثم لحقه الكتابة؛ لأن بالتدبير سلم الثلث فيكون بدل الكتابة مقابلا بما لم يسلم وهو الثلثان على ما بينا فتذكر. تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٠٤/٨] وإنما قيد بقوله: "معسرا" ، لأنه لو كان موسرا ويخرج المدبر من ثلث المال يعتق ولا يلزمه السعاية. (فتح، ملا مسكين)
'And if he makes his mukatab a mudabbir' etc.: i.e., that the master makes his mukatab a mudabbir because he owns the power to execute immediate emancipation after kitabah, so he owns the power to suspend it, and it is valid with a condition. This act is beneficial for him because it is possible that the master dies before paying the kitabah debt, so he becomes free for free, or he becomes unable to pay the kitabah debt, so he remains as mudabbir. (completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:104) 'Then if he fails' etc.: either from ta'jiz meaning he declares himself unable, i.e., admits his inability, or from 'ajz meaning he is unable to perform the kitabah. The conclusion: the mukatab whom the master made mudabbir, if he becomes unable to perform the kitabah, he remains as mudabbir due to the existence of the cause obligating that. (Hashiya) 'And otherwise he works for two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the debt upon his death insolently': i.e., if he does not become unable and the master dies insolvent, then he has a choice between working for two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the kitabah debt. This is according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa). And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he works for the lesser of the two. So the disagreement here is only in the choice. According to him (Abu Hanifa), he chooses between them; according to them, he does not choose but must pay the lesser. This is based on the divisibility of emancipation, as explained in the previous issue. As for the amount here, it is agreed upon without dispute because the kitabah debt is matched to the entire slave; since the mukatab had not earned any freedom before that, if some of the slave becomes free for free afterwards, its portion of the kitabah debt drops, unlike the case where tadbir precedes and kitabah follows; because by tadbir one-third is secured, so the kitabah debt is matched to the remaining two-thirds as we explained. So remember. (completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:104) And he restricted by saying 'insolvent' because if he were wealthy and the mudabbir is taken from one-third of the estate, he becomes free and no working is incumbent upon him. (Fath, Mulla Miskin)
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where a master who has already contracted kitabah with his slave then also makes that slave a mudabbir (declares him free upon his own death). The commentator explains that this is valid because the master retains power over emancipation. The legal effect is that the mukatab continues in his kitabah; if he later fails to pay the installments, he becomes a pure mudabbir (i.e., his status changes from mukatab to mudabbir). If he does not fail and the master dies insolvent, the slave's position is similar to the earlier discussion: Abu Hanifa gives him a choice between working for two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the kitabah debt, while the Sahibayn oblige him to pay the lesser of the two. The key difference from the previous case is that here the amount is agreed upon (two-thirds of value or two-thirds of debt) because the entire kitabah debt corresponds to the whole slave at the outset; when one-third becomes free by tadbir, exactly one-third of the debt drops. The restriction 'insolvent' ensures that if the master leaves enough estate, the mudabbir is freed from the one-third portion without any working.

Key Terms
تعجيز (ta'jiz): The act of the slave declaring himself unable to pay the kitabah installments, which rescinds the kitabah.
معسر (mu'sir): Insolvent; a master who dies leaving no estate beyond the mudabbir and mukatab.
تخيير (takhyir): Choice; the slave's right to opt between two alternatives.
تجزي العتق (tajazzu' al-i'taq): The concept that emancipation can be partial and divisible, allowing proportional calculations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He remains a mukatab but must pay immediately.
B) He becomes a mudabbir only, and the kitabah is void.
C) He becomes free immediately.
D) He is sold to pay the debt.

Key Takeaway
In the case of a mukatab made mudabbir with master's insolvent death, Abu Hanifa grants choice between two-thirds of value or two-thirds of debt; Sahibayn fix the lesser amount, both based on the divisibility of emancipation.

Compromise on Deferred Kitabah Debt: Istihsan Overriding Qiyas
Ruling on compounding deferred kitabah debt for immediate payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits a compromise (sulh) on a deferred kitabah debt for a smaller immediate sum, applying the principle of istihsan to override the qiyas that would otherwise deem it riba.

Core Idea
Istihsan permits reducing a deferred kitabah debt for immediate payment because deferment is considered property for a mukatab.

This passage addresses a unique Hanafi concession: the validity of a sulh where a master accepts a smaller immediate payment instead of a larger deferred kitabah debt. Although qiyas would classify this as riba, istihsan overrides due to the special nature of kitabah. Understanding the reasoning deepens insight into how Hanafi jurists balance competing analogies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and the precise ruling
The act is a compromise (sulh) on a deferred kitabah debt. The Hanafi ruling is that it is valid (sahih) and not prohibited.
This is a concession specific to the master-mukatab relationship.
2
Recognize the qiyas objection
By strict qiyas, exchanging a larger deferred sum for a smaller immediate sum is riba, because deferment is not considered property and extra is taken for time.
This is the standard analogy used between free persons.
3
Apply the Hanafi istihsan rationale
Istihsan overrides qiyas because deferment for a mukatab is treated as property in one sense—the mukatab cannot pay without it. Also, the kitabah debt is not full property (e.g., no kafalah on it). Thus the exchange is balanced, no riba.
This is a khafiyyah (hidden) 'illa and a preferred view.
4
Consider the alternative explanation
Some jurists treat the sulh as a rescission of the original kitabah and a new contract for the immediate amount, which is clearly valid.
Both explanations avoid riba.
5
Note the limitation of the ruling
This concession does not apply to free persons or to a mukatab of another person; in those cases, qiyas stands.
The specificity is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كاتبه على ألف مؤجل، فصالحه على نصف حال صح. وإن كاتبه إلخ: أي . صح الصلح على خمسمائة حالة بعد أن كاتبه على ألف مؤجل في الاستحسان، والقياس أن لأنه اعتياض عن الأجل، وهو ليس بمال والدين، مال، فكان ربا؛ ولهذا لا يجوز بين الحرين بأن كان على الحر ألف مؤجل، فصالحه على خمسمائة حالة، ولا في مكاتب الغير بأن كان لرجل على مكاتب الغير ألف مؤجل، فصالحه على خمسمائة معجلة. يصح؛ من وجه الاستحسان: أن الأجل في حق المكاتب مال من وجه؛ لأنه لا يقدر على الأداء به، فأعطى له حكم المال، وبدل الكتابة من وجه غير مال حتى لا تصح الكفالة به، فاعتدلا، فلا، ربا، بخلاف العقد بين الحرين؛ لأنه عقد وجه، فكان ربا، أو أن هذا الصلح يجعل فسخا للكتابة السابقة وتجديدا للعقد منهما على خمسمائة حالة. (ملتقط من الشروح والحواشي)
And if he wrote a kitabah with him for a deferred thousand, then he compromised with him for half immediately, it is valid. 'And if he wrote a kitabah with him' etc.: i.e., the compromise for five hundred immediately after he wrote a kitabah with him for a deferred thousand is valid by istihsan. By qiyas it is not valid because it is an exchange for deferment, which is not property, and the debt is property, so it would be riba. For this reason it is not valid between free persons if one has a deferred thousand on a free man and he compromises for five hundred immediately, nor in the case of someone else's mukatab, if a man has a deferred thousand on another's mukatab and he compromises for five hundred immediate. It is valid by istihsan: because deferment with respect to the mukatab is property in one sense, since he is unable to pay with it, so it is given the ruling of property; and the kitabah debt is in one sense not property such that kafalah is not valid with it. So they are balanced, thus no riba. Unlike the contract between free persons because it is a usurious contract. Or: this compromise is considered a rescission of the previous kitabah and a renewal of the contract between them for five hundred immediate. (Collected from the commentaries and glosses)
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage allows a master to reduce the deferred kitabah debt in exchange for immediate payment. The qiyas (analogy) would prohibit it as riba (usury) because exchanging a larger deferred sum for a smaller immediate one involves an 'illa of deferment for extra. However, istihsan (equity) permits it due to the unique nature of kitabah. Deferment for a mukatab is considered a form of property because without it he cannot pay, and the kitabah debt itself is not fully property (e.g., kafalah is not valid on it). Thus the two values are balanced, avoiding riba. An alternative explanation is that the sulh is treated as a rescission of the old contract and a new kitabah for a smaller amount, which is valid. The commentary notes that this concession is specific to the mukatab and does not apply to free persons or the mukatab of another.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A compromise agreement to settle the kitabah debt by reducing it for immediate payment.
الأجل في حق المكاتب مال من وجه (al-ajal fi haqq al-mukatab mal min wajh): Deferment is considered property in one sense because the mukatab cannot pay without it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because deferment is considered property for the mukatab, balancing the exchange.
C) Because the master and mukatab are like two free persons.
D) Because it is a penalty for the mukatab's delay.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses istihsan to permit a master to accept a smaller immediate payment from a mukatab in lieu of a larger deferred debt, recognizing deferment as property for the mukatab and thereby avoiding riba.

Kitabah by a Terminally Ill Master: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Payment
Ruling on kitabah contracted by a terminally ill master and its effect on heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the immediate payment owed by a mukatab when the master dies ill, and calculate the amounts under each position.

Core Idea
When a terminally ill master writes kitabah above value, the bequest limit triggers a dispute on what the slave must pay immediately.

This passage examines a specific scenario: a master in terminal illness writes a kitabah contract with his slave for an amount greater than the slave's market value. The master dies, and the heirs do not approve the implied bequest (muhabah). The key question: how much must the mukatab pay immediately to secure his freedom? The Hanafi imams differ based on how they conceptualize the kitabah debt in relation to the slave's value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario and trigger
The master is terminally ill, writes kitabah for 2000, slave worth 1000, heirs disapprove. The bequest (waiver of excess) is limited to one-third of the estate.
The master has no other property; the kitabah debt is the entire estate.
2
State the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn)
They treat the entire kitabah debt as standing in place of the slave's value (badal al-kitabah qa'im maqam al-raqaba). Thus, the bequest is one-third of 2000 = 666.67, and two-thirds (1333.33) must be paid immediately.
The slave keeps the remaining 666.67 as waived bequest.
3
State the position of Imam Muhammad (the other Muhammad al-Shaybani, as a separate view)
Muhammad considers only the slave's actual value (1000) subject to the bequest. The excess (1000) is a deferred debt owned by the master. So the bequest is one-third of 1000 = 333.33, and two-thirds of 1000 (666.67) must be paid immediately. The remaining 1333.33 is either paid at term or the slave is returned.
The slave has the option to complete payment or revert to slavery for the unpaid portion.
4
Trace the underlying principle (qiyas khafi)
The dispute hinges on whether the kitabah debt is equivalent to the slave's value for inheritance purposes. The Sahibayn analogize it to a sale where the entire price is the slave's value; Muhammad treats the excess as a separate loan-like obligation.
This is a hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) about the nature of kitabah debt.
5
Apply the calculations to a hypothetical
Given the numbers: kitabah = 2000, value = 1000. Under the Sahibayn: immediate payment = 2/3 × 2000 = 1333.33. Under Muhammad: immediate payment = 2/3 × 1000 = 666.67. Practical difference of 666.66.
The difference affects the slave's immediate financial burden and potential freedom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مات مريض بدل الكتابة عن المكاتب كاتب المولى عبده ألف كاتب عبده على ألفين إلى سنة، وقيمته ألف، ولم تجز الورثة، أدى ثلثي البدل حالا، من المرض مؤجلا ولا مال له غيره التأجيل العبد وإلا سعى إلخ: يعني إن لم يعجز ومات المولى معسرا، فهو بالخيار بين أن يسعى في ثلثي قيمته أو ثلثي بدل الكتابة وهذا عند الإمام وقالا : يسعى في الأقل منهما، فالخلاف هنا في الخيار فقط، فعنده يخير بينهما، وعندهما: لا يتخير بل يتعين الأقل، وهو مبني على تجزي الإعتاق وعدمه، وقد . بيانه في المسألة المتقدمة. وأما المقدار هنا فمتفق عليه لا خلاف فيه؛ لأن بدل الكتابة مقابل بكل الرقبة؛ إذ لم يستحق المكاتب شيئا من الحرية قبل ذلك، فإذا عتق بعض الرقبة مجانا بعد ذلك سقط حصته من بدل الكتابة بخلاف ما إذا تقدم التدبير، ثم لحقه الكتابة؛ لأن بالتدبير سلم الثلث فيكون بدل الكتابة مقابلا بما لم يسلم وهو الثلثان على ما بينا فتذكر. تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٠٤/٨] وإنما قيد بقوله: "معسرا" ، لأنه لو كان موسرا ويخرج المدبر من ثلث المال يعتق ولا يلزمه السعاية. (فتح، ملا مسكين) مات مريض إلخ: أي مات مريض كاتبه في المرض؛ إذ لو كانت الكتابة في الصحة لنفذت المحاباة مطلقا وإن لم تجز الورثة، ولو قال كما في "التنوير": مريض كاتب عبده على ألفين إلى سنة فمات إلخ لكان أولى. (فتح) وقيمته ألف إلخ والحال أن قيمة العبد] فلو كان مال الكتابة والقيمة على السواء بأن كان ألفا، فإنه يجب تعجيل ثلثي الألف اتفاقا كما في "المفتاح". (فتح) أدى إلخ: أي بدل الكتابة وهو ألفان عندهما، وعند محمد: يؤدي ثلثي الألف وهو القيمة حالا، والباقي إلى أجله، أو يرد رقيقا ؛ لأن ما زاد على قيمته ملك المولى مؤجلا، وقيمته ملكه حالا، فنفذ في ثلث هذا، وتعجل في ثلثيه، ولهما أن بدل الكتابة قائم مقام الرقبة، فينفذ في ثلثه. رمز الحقائق ٢٩٧/٢]
A sick master died [while having] the kitabah debt from the mukatab, the master wrote a kitabah with his slave for two thousand deferred, and his value is one thousand, and the heirs did not approve; he pays two-thirds of the debt immediately. 'A sick master died' etc.: i.e., a sick master who wrote a kitabah while ill; if the kitabah were during health, the favor (muhabah) would take effect absolutely even if the heirs do not approve. And if he had said as in al-Tanwir: 'A sick man wrote a kitabah with his slave for two thousand to a year and died' it would be more appropriate. (Fath) 'And his value is one thousand' etc. and the condition is that the value of the slave is as stated; if the kitabah money and the value were equal, for example one thousand, then it is agreed that two-thirds of the thousand must be paid immediately, as in al-Miftah. (Fath) 'He pays' etc.: i.e., the kitabah debt is two thousand according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to Muhammad: he pays two-thirds of one thousand (the value) immediately, and the rest at its term, or he is returned as a slave; because what exceeds his value is owned by the master as deferred, and his value is owned immediately, so the (bequest) takes effect on one-third of this and expedites two-thirds of it. According to the two, the kitabah debt stands in place of the slave, so it takes effect on one-third of it. (Ramz al-Haqaiq 2:297)
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage deals with a terminally ill master who contracts kitabah with his slave for a sum greater than the slave's value. Since it is a bequest in effect (by waiving the excess), it is subject to the one-third rule of inheritance. The heirs may disapprove if it exceeds one-third of the estate. The commentary explains the disagreement: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the entire kitabah debt (2000) is treated as the price of the slave; only one-third of that debt can be waived (since it is a bequest), so the slave must pay two-thirds of the debt immediately (i.e., 1333.33) to the heirs, with the rest canceled? Actually, the text says 'he pays two-thirds of the debt immediately' which is 1333.33. According to Muhammad, only the portion equal to the slave's value (1000) is subject to bequest; the excess (1000) is owned by the master deferred, so the slave pays two-thirds of the value (666.67) immediately and the rest (333.33) at term or is returned as a slave? The commentary is dense and somewhat garbled. The key point: the slave must pay the operative amount immediately, with a dispute on the calculation.

Key Terms
محاباة (muhabah): Favour; here the master's waiver of the excess value in kitabah, considered a bequest.
بدل الكتابة قائم مقام الرقبة (badal al-kitabah qa'im maqam al-raqaba): The kitabah debt stands in place of the slave's value for inheritance purposes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, if a master dies ill after writing kitabah for 2000 on a slave worth 1000, and heirs do not approve, what must the slave pay immediately?
A) 2000
B) 1000
C) 1333.33 (two-thirds of 2000)
D) 666.67 (two-thirds of 1000)

Key Takeaway
The amount a mukatab must pay immediately after the master dies ill depends on whether the kitabah debt stands in place of the slave's value (Sahibayn) or only the value is subject to bequest (Muhammad).
