Mukatab's Option When Master Dies Insolvent: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute on mukatab's option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on the mukatab's option at the master's insolvent death and explain its basis in the divisibility of emancipation.

Core Idea
Emancipation's divisibility decides whether the mukatab chooses his payment or must pay the lesser.

This passage from the Kitab al-Mukatab addresses a specific scenario: the kitabah contract is active, the master dies insolvent, and the slave is not incapacitated (i.e., has not failed to pay). The matn states an obligation to pay two-thirds of something; the commentary reveals an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the slave has a choice between two different amounts. This lesson unpacks that dispute and its theoretical foundation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Determine the legal situation: master dies insolvent after kitabah contract, mukatab not incapacitated.
Insolvent means the estate cannot cover debts.
2
State the Obligation from the Matn
The matn says the mukatab must seek (sa'a) two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the kitabah price.
The phrase 'or' indicates a possible choice.
3
Recognize the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa holds the mukatab has a choice (takhyir) between the two amounts; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold he must pay the lesser of the two.
This is a purely Hanafi internal dispute.
4
Understand the Basis: Tajzi' al-I'taq
The dispute rests on whether emancipation can be partial: Imam says yes, the Sahibayn say no.
If divisible, the slave can choose which part drops; if indivisible, only the lesser is due.
5
Determine the Practical Effect (Thamarah)
Apply to a numerical example: value 1000, price 2000. Imam: choose 666.7 or 1333.3; Sahibayn: must pay 666.7.
The amount of two-thirds is agreed; only the option differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المكاتب كتابة أم ولد والمدبر وإلا سعى في ثلثي قيمته أو ثلثي البدل بموته معسرا وإن أعتق مكاتبه عتق، وسقط أي وإن لم يعجز شاء سعى في المولى القيام الملك فيه البدل، ووإلا سعى إلخ يعني إن لم يعجز ومات المولى معسرا، فهو بالخيار بين أن يسعى في ثلثي قيمته أو ثلثي بدل الكتابة وهذا عند الإمام وقالا : يسعى في الأقل منهما، فالخلاف هنا في الخيار فقط، فعنده يخير بينهما، وعندهما: لا يتخير بل يتعين الأقل، وهو مبني على تجزي الإعتاق وعدمه، وقد . بيانه في المسألة المتقدمة. وأما المقدار هنا فمتفق عليه لا خلاف فيه؛ لأن بدل الكتابة مقابل بكل الرقبة؛ إذ لم يستحق المكاتب شيئا من الحرية قبل ذلك، فإذا عتق بعض الرقبة مجانا بعد ذلك سقط حصته من بدل الكتابة بخلاف ما إذا تقدم التدبير، ثم لحقه الكتابة؛ لأن بالتدبير سلم الثلث فيكون بدل الكتابة مقابلا بما لم يسلم وهو الثلثان على ما بينا فتذكر. تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٠٤/٨] وإنما قيد بقوله: "معسرا" ، لأنه لو كان موسرا ويخرج المدبر من ثلث المال يعتق ولا يلزمه السعاية. (فتح، ملا مسكين)
Book of the Mukatab. Writing of Umm Walad and Mudabbar. And otherwise he seeks in two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the substitute upon his death insolvent. And if he emancipates his mukatab, he becomes free and it drops. Meaning: And if he is not incapable, he may seek in the master's... the ownership in it the substitute. And 'otherwise he seeks' etc. means if he is not incapable and the master dies insolvent, then he has the choice between seeking in two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the kitabah price. This is according to Imam. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he seeks in the lesser of the two. So the dispute here is about the choice only. According to him (Imam), he is given a choice between them; according to them, he does not have a choice but the lesser is determined. This is based on the divisibility of emancipation and its non-divisibility, and its explanation has been given in the previous issue. As for the amount here, it is agreed upon, no dispute; because the kitabah price is in exchange for the entire slave's person; since the mukatab had not deserved any freedom before that, so if part of the person becomes free gratis after that, his share of the kitabah price drops. Unlike if tadbir preceded and then kitabah followed; because by tadbir one-third is secured, so the kitabah price is in exchange for what was not secured, which is two-thirds, as we have explained, so remember. Completion of al-Bahr al-Raiq: 8/104. And he only restricted it by saying 'insolvent' because if he were wealthy and the mudabbar is taken out from one-third of the wealth, he becomes free and no seeking is required. (Fath, Mulla Miskin)
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the chapter on kitabah regarding the situation where a master, after entering into a kitabah contract with his slave, dies insolvent and the slave is not incapacitated (i.e., he has not failed to pay). The matn states that the mukatab must seek (sa'a) to earn and pay two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the kitabah price. The commentary clarifies that there is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) on the nature of this obligation. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the mukatab has a choice (takhyir) between paying two-thirds of his market value or two-thirds of the kitabah price. According to the Sahibayn, he does not have a choice; instead, he must pay the lesser of the two amounts. The dispute is based on the principle of tajzi' al-i'taq (divisibility of emancipation): Imam holds that emancipation can be partial, so the mukatab can choose which portion of the price to pay; the Sahibayn hold that emancipation is indivisible, so the lesser amount suffices. The passage also clarifies that the amount itself (two-thirds) is agreed upon because the kitabah price is in exchange for the entire slave, and when a portion becomes free gratis (due to the master's death), the corresponding portion of the price drops. The restriction to insolvency is explained: if the master is wealthy, the mudabbar (if he is a mudabbar) is freed from one-third of the estate, and no sa'y is required. This lesson highlights the subtle intra-madhhab differences and their theoretical foundations.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukātab): A slave who has entered into a kitabah contract with his master, agreeing to pay a sum in return for eventual emancipation.
سعى (saʿā): The act of the mukatab in earning money and paying the kitabah price; here, it refers to the obligation to earn and pay the required amount.
بدل الكتابة (badal al-kitābah): The price agreed upon in the kitabah contract that the slave must pay to gain freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn in this passage, how much must the mukatab pay when the master dies insolvent?
A) He may choose between two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the kitabah price.
B) He must pay two-thirds of his value.
C) He must pay two-thirds of the kitabah price.
D) He must pay the lesser of two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the kitabah price.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when a kitabah contract ends with the master's insolvent death, the mukatab must pay two-thirds of either his value or the kitabah price, but whether he has a choice depends on the divisibility of emancipation – a key intra-Hanafi dispute.

Sulh on Deferred Kitabah: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
Ruling with proof explaining why sulh on deferred kitabah is valid by istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sulh for deferred kitabah and explain the istihsan reasoning that overrides qiyas.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, istihsan permits a sulh on deferred kitabah because deferment has a monetary value for the mukatab, balancing the exchange.

This lesson examines a ruling from Kanz al-Daqaiq and its sharh, where a master accepts an immediate lesser payment from his mukatab in place of a larger deferred kitabah debt. While strict analogy (qiyas) would consider this riba, the Hanafi school uses istihsan (juristic preference) to validate it. You will explore the reasoning behind this ruling and its limits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the matn: 'If he contracts kitabah with him for a deferred thousand, then he makes sulh with him for half in cash, it is valid.' Note that the ruling is explicit: the sulh is valid (sahih).
The ruling is stated unconditionally for the mukatab case.
2
State the qiyas objection
The commentary explains that by qiyas, the sulh would be invalid because exchanging a deferred debt for a lesser immediate amount is compensation for deferment, which is not property; thus it constitutes riba.
This qiyas is based on the prohibition of riba al-nasi'ah.
3
Understand the istihsan justification
Two justifications are given: (1) For the mukatab, deferment is considered property in one aspect because he cannot pay immediately, so it balances with the kitabah price (which is not fully property), avoiding riba. (2) Alternatively, the sulh can be viewed as a rescission of the old contract and a new contract for the lesser immediate amount.
The first justification is the primary Hanafi reasoning.
4
Note the contrast with other cases
The text explicitly states that this istihsan does not apply between free men or with another's mukatab; in those cases, the sulh remains invalid by both qiyas and istihsan.
This restriction highlights the unique status of the mukatab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كاتبه على ألف مؤجل، فصالحه على نصف حال صح. أي صح الصلح على خمسمائة حالة بعد أن كاتبه على ألف مؤجل في الاستحسان، والقياس أن لأنه اعتياض عن الأجل، وهو ليس بمال والدين ،مال، فكان ربا؛ ولهذا لا يجوز بين الحرين بأن كان على الحر ألف مؤجل، فصالحه على خمسمائة حالة، ولا في مكاتب الغير بأن كان لرجل على مكاتب الغير ألف مؤجل، فصالحه على خمسمائة معجلة. يصح؛ من وجه الاستحسان: أن الأجل في حق المكاتب مال من وجه؛ لأنه لا يقدر على الأداء به، فأعطى له حكم المال، وبدل الكتابة من وجه غير مال حتى لا تصح الكفالة به، فاعتدلا، فلا ،ربا، بخلاف العقد بين الحرين؛ لأنه عقد وجه، فكان ربا، أو أن هذا الصلح يجعل فسخا للكتابة السابقة وتجديدا للعقد منهما على خمسمائة حالة. (ملتقط من الشروح والحواشي)
And if he contracts kitabah with him for a deferred thousand, then he makes a sulh with him for half in cash, it is valid. That is, the sulh for five hundred in cash after contracting kitabah for a deferred thousand is valid by istihsan. And by qiyas, it is not valid because it is a compensation for deferment, which is not property, and debt is property, so it would be riba. Therefore it is not permissible between free men, as if a free man owes a deferred thousand, then he makes sulh for five hundred in cash; nor in the mukatab of another, as if a man has a claim of a deferred thousand on the mukatab of another, then he makes sulh for five hundred prompt. It is valid from the face of istihsan: because deferment in the case of a mukatab is property in one aspect, because he cannot perform payment with it, so it is given the ruling of property, and the kitabah price is not property in one aspect such that suretyship is not valid for it. So they balance each other, thus no riba. Unlike the contract between free men, because it is a contract of exchange, so it would be riba. Or that this sulh is considered a rescission of the previous kitabah and a renewal of the contract between them for five hundred in cash. (Compiled from commentaries and glosses)
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of a sulh (compromise) on a deferred kitabah price. The matn rules that if a master contracts kitabah with his slave for a deferred sum (e.g., 1000), and subsequently makes a sulh with the slave for an immediate payment of half (500), this is valid. The commentary explains that this ruling is based on istihsan, while qiyas would render it invalid. By qiyas, such a transaction is considered a exchange of deferred debt for prompt payment with a discount, which resembles riba (interest) because the deferment is not considered property. However, by istihsan, the Hanafi school approves it for two reasons: (1) For the mukatab, deferment has a monetary value because he lacks the ability to pay immediately; thus it is treated as property on his side, while the kitabah price is not fully property (as suretyship is not valid for it), so they balance out and no riba occurs. (2) Alternatively, the sulh can be seen as a rescission of the old contract and a new contract for the lesser immediate amount, which is permissible. The text contrasts this with cases between free men or with another's mukatab, where such sulh is invalid. This lesson illustrates the Hanafi use of istihsan to achieve equitable outcomes despite strict analogy.

Key Terms
صلح (ṣulḥ): A compromise or settlement where the creditor accepts a lesser immediate payment in lieu of a larger deferred debt.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas to achieve a more equitable result; here, it validates the sulh despite qiyas suggesting riba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does istihsan permit the sulh between a master and his mukatab on a deferred kitabah price?
A) Because the deferment is considered property for the mukatab, balancing the exchange.
B) Because the master can forgive the debt unconditionally.
C) Because the mukatab is not legally capable of owning property.
D) Because qiyas is always rejected in financial transactions.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, istihsan overrides qiyas to permit sulh on deferred kitabah because deferment is considered property for the mukatab, balancing the exchange.

Kitabah in Death Illness: The Immediate Payment Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on calculation of immediate payment in death illness kitabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding immediate payment when a sick master contracts kitabah with deferment, and calculate the amounts according to both the Sahibayn and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
In death illness, the favor of deferment in kitabah is limited to one-third, but the basis for calculation—value or total price—is disputed.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and Muhammad al-Shaybani (in a separate transmission) regarding the immediate payment owed by a mukatab when the master dies after contracting kitabah in death illness. The master grants a favor (muhabah) by deferring payment beyond the slave's value, and the heirs do not consent. The dispute centers on whether the one-third limit applies to the slave's value or the total kitabah price.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The master, in death illness, contracts kitabah with his slave for 2000 dirhams deferred for one year. The slave's market value is 1000. The master has no other wealth. He dies, and the heirs do not consent to the deferment.
The act of deferment is considered a favor (muhabah) like a will, limited to one-third of the estate.
2
State the Two Positions
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani): the slave pays two-thirds of the total kitabah price (2000) immediately, i.e., 1333.3 dirhams. Muhammad al-Shaybani (in a separate transmission): the slave pays two-thirds of the value (1000) immediately, i.e., 666.6 dirhams, and the remainder at term.
Both agree that the slave must pay some amount immediately; the disagreement is on the base amount.
3
Analyze the Reasoning
Sahibayn: the entire kitabah price stands in place of the slave's person, so the one-third limit applies to the price. Muhammad: since the master could have contracted only for the value and forgo the excess, deferring the excess is a fortiori valid.
Muhammad's reasoning uses the concept of 'primary and secondary'—if the principal is waived, the attribute (deferment) is even more easily waived.
4
Examine the Analogies
Sahibayn analogize to a sale of a house for more than its value; the substitute replaces the property. Muhammad analogizes to khul' in death illness where deferment of the entire sum is upheld because the husband could have divorced without any compensation.
The rebuttal from Sahibayn distinguishes khul' because the vulva is not considered property, unlike the slave's person.
5
Determine the Practical Difference and the Matn's Position
The difference in immediate payment is 666.7 dirhams. The matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq adopts the Sahibayn's view, making it the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in this text.
The commentator presents both views but indicates the matn follows the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مات مريض بدل الكتابة عن المكاتب كاتب المولى عبده ألف كاتب عبده على ألفين إلى سنة، وقيمته ألف، ولم تجز الورثة، أدى ثلثي البدل حالا، من المرض مؤجلا ولا مال له غيره التأجيل العبد. أي مات مريض كاتبه في المرض؛ إذ لو كانت الكتابة في الصحة لنفذت المحاباة مطلقا وإن لم تجز الورثة، ولو قال كما في "التنوير": مريض كاتب عبده على ألفين إلى سنة فمات إلخ لكان أولى. (فتح) وقيمته ألف إلخ والحال أن قيمة العبد فلو كان مال الكتابة والقيمة على السواء بأن كان ألفا، فإنه يجب تعجيل ثلثي الألف اتفاقا كما في "المفتاح". (فتح) أدى إلخ: أي بدل الكتابة وهو ألفان عندهما، وعند محمد: يؤدي ثلثي الألف وهو القيمة حالا، والباقي إلى أجله، أو يرد رقيقا؛ لأن ما زاد على قيمته ملك المولى مؤجلا، وقيمته ملكه حالا، فنفذ في ثلث هذا، وتعجل في ثلثيه، ولهما أن بدل الكتابة قائم مقام الرقبة، فينفذ في ثلثه. رمز الحقائق ٢٩٧/٢] أدى أي عند انتهاء أجله المولى عبده في مرضه موجلاً والحال أن قيمته والباقي إلخ أي الباقي من البدل عند انتهاء أجله أقول : قد مر تحت قوله أدى ثلثي البدل أن المسألة خلافية، والمذكور في المتن هو قول الشيخين، وعند محمد يؤدي ثلثي الألف حالا، والباقي إلى أجله، وقد مر هناك دلائل الجانبين، لكنه كلام محمل. وتفصيل المقام وتوضيحه أن تصرفات الرجل في مرض موته لها حكم الوصية، فتنفذ ثلث تركته، والمسألة مفروضة فيما إذا لم يكن للمولى مال سوى هذا العبد فإذا كاتب المولى عبده في مرضه بألفين، وقيمته ألف، ثم مات يكون محاباة أي تبرعا من المولى بالأجل، فإنه كان حق الورثة متعلقا بالعبد حين موت المولى، فلما كاتبه إلى أجل صير حقهم متعلقا بالبدل بعد انقضاء الأجل، فتنفذ هذه المحاباة في الثلث إلا أنها عند محمد حله تنفذ في ثلث القيمة، وهو ثلاثمائة وثلاث وثلاثون درهما وثلث درهم، والألف الزائد على القيمة، فيؤدى ثلثي الألف أي ستمائة وستة وستين درهما وثلثي درهم حال موت المولى والباقي أي ألفا وثلاثمائة وثلاثة وثلاثين درهما وثلث درهم بعد انقضاء الأجل، وهو السنة. وعندهما: تنفذ في ثلث البدل ألفان، وهو فيؤدي ثلثي الألفين، وهو ألف وثلاثمائة وثلاثة وثلاثون درهما وثلث درهم في الحال، والباقي وهو ستمائة وستة وستون درهما وثلثا درهم عند انقضاء الأجل، لمحمد له: أنه لما كان للمولى أن يكاتبه على قيمته، وهي الألف، ويترك الزيادة، فله أن يؤخر الزيادة، وهي الألف الثاني بالطريق الأولى؛ لأنه لما جاز له ترك أصله جاز له ترك وصفه، وهو التأجيل في ثلث القيمة والزيادة، وصار كما إذا خالع امرأته في مرض موته على ألف إلى سنة ولا مال له غير هذا الألف ولم يجز الورثة التأجيل، فإنه يبقى التأجيل في كل المال؛ لأنه لو ترك بأن يطلقها بلا بدل صح، فيصح تأجيله. ولهما: أن جميع المسمى بدل الرقبة حتى جرى عليه أحكام الإبدال من حق الأخذ بالشفعة وغيره فيما إذا باع دارا تساوي ألفا بألفين وحق الورثة كان متعلقا بالمبدل فكذا يتعلق بالبدل فينفذ تصرفه أي المحاباة في ثلث البدل. وهذا بخلاف الخلع؛ لأن البدل فيه لا يقابل المال، فإن البضع في حالة الخروج لا يعتبر مالا، فلم يتعلق حق الورثة بالمبدل، فلا يتعلق بالبدل. ونظير هذه المسألة ما إذا باع المريض داره بثلاثة آلاف إلى سنة وقيمتها ألف ثم مات ولم يجز الورثة، فعندهما: يقال للمشتري أدّ ثلثي جميع الثمن حالا والثلث إلى أجله وإلا فانقض البيع، وعنده: يعتبر الثلث في قدر القيمة لا فيما زاد عليه؛ لما بينا، فاحفظه. وإنما قيد بقوله: "وقيمته ألف"؛ ليخرج ما إذا كان مال الكتابة والقيمة على السواء فإنه يجب حينئذ تعجيل ثلثي المال اتفاقا ويخرج ما إذا كانت القيمة زائدة على مال الكتابة فإنه أيضا متفق والله تعالى أعلم. أو رد رقيقا إلخ [إلى حالته الأولى رقيقا] يعني إن لم يؤد ثلثي البدل سيجيء عندهما، وثلثي القيمة عنده رده الورثة إلى الرقة. عليه كما
A sick person died; the kitabah price from the mukatab; the master contracted kitabah with his slave for a thousand; he contracted kitabah with his slave for two thousand to a year, and his value is one thousand, and the heirs did not consent; he pays two-thirds of the substitute immediately, deferred from the illness, and he has no other wealth; the slave's deferment. That is: a sick person died; he contracted kitabah with him during his illness; for if the kitabah were in health, the favor would have been executed absolutely even if the heirs did not consent. And it would have been better if he said as in al-Tanwir: a sick person contracted kitabah with his slave for two thousand to a year, then died etc. (Fath) And his value is one thousand etc. and the state is that the value of the slave; so if the kitabah money and the value are equal, as if it were one thousand, then immediate payment of two-thirds of the thousand is obligatory by agreement as in al-Miftah. (Fath) He pays etc.: i.e., the kitabah price, which is two thousand according to them (Sahibayn), and according to Muhammad: he pays two-thirds of the thousand, which is the value, immediately, and the remainder at its term, or he is returned as a slave; because what exceeds his value is owned by the master as deferred, and his value is owned by him immediately, so it is executed in one-third of this, and he expedites in two-thirds of it. According to them, the kitabah price stands in place of the slave's person, so it is executed in one-third of it. Hashiyat al-Haqa'iq 2/297. He pays i.e., at the termination of its term. The master's slave in his illness deferred, while his value is... And the remainder etc., i.e., the remainder of the substitute at the termination of its term. I say: it has passed under his statement 'he pays two-thirds of the substitute' that the issue is disputed, and what is mentioned in the matn is the statement of the two shaykhs (Sahibayn), and according to Muhammad he pays two-thirds of the thousand immediately, and the remainder at its term. And the proofs of both sides have passed there, but it is statement that is allegorical. And the detail of the subject and its clarification: that the actions of a man in his death illness have the ruling of a will, so one-third of his estate is executed. The issue is assumed when the master has no wealth other than this slave. So if the master contracts kitabah with his slave in his illness for two thousand, and his value is one thousand, then he dies, it is a favor (muhabah), i.e., a donation from the master of the deferment. For the right of the heirs was attached to the slave at the death of the master; when he contracted kitabah with him to a term, he made their right attached to the substitute after the expiration of the term. So this favor is executed in one-third; except that according to Muhammad, it is executed in one-third of the value, which is three hundred and thirty-three and one-third dirhams, and the one thousand excess over the value; so he pays two-thirds of the thousand, i.e., six hundred and sixty-six and two-thirds dirhams at the death of the master, and the remainder, i.e., one thousand three hundred and thirty-three and one-third dirhams after the expiration of the term, which is one year. And according to them (Sahibayn): it is executed in one-third of the substitute, which is two thousand; so he pays two-thirds of the two thousand, i.e., one thousand three hundred and thirty-three and one-third dirhams immediately, and the remainder, i.e., six hundred and sixty-six and two-thirds dirhams at the expiration of the term. In support of Muhammad: because since the master could contract kitabah with him for his value, which is one thousand, and forgo the excess, so he can defer the excess, which is the second thousand, by a stronger reason; because when it is permissible for him to forgo the principal, it is permissible for him to forgo its attribute, which is the deferment in one-third of the value and the excess. And it becomes like when a man divorces his wife in his death illness for a deferred thousand and he has no wealth other than this thousand, and the heirs do not consent to the deferment, then the deferment remains in all the wealth; because if he were to divorce her without any compensation, it would be valid, so his deferment is valid. And in support of them (Sahibayn): that all the named price is in exchange for the slave's person, such that it is subject to the rulings of exchange, like the right of pre-emption and others, as when he sells a house worth one thousand for two thousand, and the heirs' right was attached to the exchanged object, so likewise it attaches to the substitute. So his action, i.e., the favor, is executed in one-third of the substitute. And this is unlike khul'; because the substitute in it does not correspond to property, for the vulva at the time of exit is not considered property, so the heirs' right was not attached to the exchanged object, and thus does not attach to the substitute. And an analogy to this issue is: if a sick person sells his house for three thousand on term, its value one thousand, then dies, and the heirs do not consent; according to them (Sahibayn), the buyer is told: pay two-thirds of the entire price immediately and one-third at its term, otherwise the sale is rescinded; and according to him (Muhammad), one-third is considered in the amount of the value, not on what exceeds it, as we have explained, so remember. And he only restricted it by his statement 'and his value is one thousand' to exclude the case where the kitabah money and the value are equal, for then immediate payment of two-thirds of the money is obligatory by agreement, and to exclude the case where the value exceeds the kitabah money, for that is also agreed upon. And God Almighty knows best. Or he is returned as a slave etc. [to his original state as a slave] meaning if he does not pay two-thirds of the substitute according to them, and two-thirds of the value according to him, the heirs return him to slavery. Upon him as...
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage deals with a complex intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a kitabah contract entered into by a master during his death illness. The scenario: a master contracts kitabah with his slave for 2000 deferred, while the slave's market value is 1000, and the master has no other wealth. He dies, and the heirs do not consent to the deferment. The matn (following the Sahibayn) states that the slave must pay two-thirds of the entire 2000 immediately. However, Muhammad al-Shaybani differs: he holds that the slave must pay two-thirds of the value (i.e., two-thirds of 1000 = 666.6) immediately, and the remainder of the 2000 after the term. If he cannot pay the immediate portion, the heirs may return him to slavery. The commentary elaborates on the reasoning: the master's actions in death illness are treated like a will, effective only up to one-third of the estate. The favor (muhabah) here is the deferment of payment. The dispute centers on what the one-third is calculated on: the value of the slave or the total kitabah price. Muhammad argues that since the master could have contracted for the value only and waived the extra, he can also defer the extra; his analogy is to khul' in death illness where deferment of the entire sum is upheld because the husband could have divorced without any compensation. The Sahibayn argue that the entire kitabah price is the substitute for the slave's person, so the one-third applies to the entire price; they analogize to a sale of a house for more than its value, where the substitute replaces the property. A parallel case is given of a sick man selling a house for 3000 when its value is 1000. The lesson showcases the ijtihad of the early Hanafi imams in applying the principle of one-third to contractual obligations in death illness.

Key Terms
محاباة (muḥābāh): A favor or donation; here, the deferment of payment granted by the master to the slave, which is treated as a gratuitous act subject to the one-third limit in death illness.
بدل الكتابة (badal al-kitābah): The price agreed in the kitabah contract; here disputed whether it entirely substitutes for the slave's person or is partly a gift.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn in this passage, how much must the slave pay immediately if the kitabah price is 2000 and the slave's value is 1000?
A) 666.6 dirhams
B) 1333.3 dirhams
C) 1000 dirhams
D) 2000 dirhams

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi position is that the one-third limit applies to the entire kitabah price, so the slave immediately pays two-thirds of the total price, not just of the value.

Kitaba During Death Illness: Dispute on Immediate Payment
Intra-Hanafi dispute on kitaba during terminal illness with value differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on immediate payment in death illness kitaba and apply the relied-upon position of the Shaykhayn.

Core Idea
In death illness kitaba, the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad differ on whether the charitable waiver applies to the kitaba amount or the slave's value.

This passage presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding kitaba entered into during death illness. At stake is how the one-third rule for bequests applies to deferred payments in such contracts. You will examine the reasoning of the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) versus Imam Muhammad and understand why the Shaykhayn's view is the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal context
Recognize that kitaba during death illness is treated like a will; it is valid only up to one-third of the estate. The heirs' right attaches to the slave at death, and the kitaba substitutes the deferred payment as the object of that right.
This context is crucial for understanding why the dispute arises.
2
State the specific issue
The issue is: When the kitaba amount differs from the slave's value, what portion of the payment must be made immediately to protect the heirs' one-third limit?
The dispute centers on the object of the charitable waiver (muhabah).
3
Analyze the Shaykhayn's position and proof
The Shaykhayn hold that the muhabah applies to the entire kitaba amount, so two-thirds of that amount must be paid immediately. Their proof: the kitaba amount is the price of the slave, and the heirs' right attaches to it analogously to a sale of property.
The analogy used: selling a house worth 1000 for 2000 deferred.
4
Analyze Imam Muhammad's position and proof
Imam Muhammad holds that the muhabah applies only to the slave's value, so two-thirds of the value must be paid immediately. His proof: the charity is in the deferment itself, which is a waiver of a right tied to the slave's value; the excess over value is not subject to the one-third rule. He analogizes to khul'.
The khul' analogy is a key point of contention.
5
Determine the thamarah and tarjih
The practical difference: under the Shaykhayn, the immediate payment is larger (two-thirds of total kitaba); under Muhammad, it is smaller (two-thirds of value). The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of the Shaykhayn, as per the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq.
The tarjih is based on the strength of the analogy and the methodology of the Sahibayn.

والباقي إلخ أي الباقي من البدل عند انتهاء أجله أقول : قد مر تحت قوله أدى ثلثي البدل" أن المسألة خلافية، والمذكور في المتن هو قول الشيخين، وعند محمد يؤدي ثلثي الألف حالا، والباقي إلى أجله، وقد مر هناك دلائل الجانبين، لكنه كلام محمل.
وتفصيل المقام وتوضيحه أن تصرفات الرجل في مرض موته لها حكم الوصية، فتنفذ ثلث تركته، والمسألة مفروضة فيما إذا لم يكن للمولى مال سوى هذا العبد فإذا كاتب المولى عبده في مرضه بألفين، وقيمته ألف، ثم مات يكون محاباة أي تبرعا من المولى بالأجل، فإنه كان حق الورثة متعلقا بالعبد حين موت المولى، فلما كاتبه إلى أجل صير حقهم متعلقا بالبدل بعد انقضاء الأجل، فتنفذ هذه المحاباة في الثلث إلا أنها عند محمد حله تنفذ في ثلث القيمة، وهو ثلاثمائة وثلاث وثلاثون درهما وثلث درهم، والألف الزائد على القيمة، فيؤدى ثلثي الألف أي ستمائة وستة وستين درهما وثلثي درهم حال موت المولى والباقي أي ألفا وثلاثمائة وثلاثة وثلاثين درهما وثلث درهم بعد انقضاء الأجل، وهو السنة.
وعندهما: تنفذ في ثلث البدل ألفان، وهو فيؤدي ثلثي الألفين، وهو ألف وثلاثمائة وثلاثة وثلاثون درهما وثلث درهم في الحال، والباقي وهو ستمائة وستة وستون درهما وثلثا درهم عند انقضاء الأجل، لمحمد له: أنه لما كان للمولى أن يكاتبه على قيمته، وهي الألف، ويترك الزيادة، فله أن يؤخر الزيادة، وهي الألف الثاني بالطريق الأولى؛ لأنه لما جاز له ترك أصله جاز له ترك وصفه، وهو التأجيل في ثلث القيمة والزيادة، وصار كما إذا خالع امرأته في مرض موته على ألف إلى سنة ولا مال له غير هذا الألف ولم يجز الورثة التأجيل، فإنه يبقى التأجيل في كل المال؛ لأنه لو ترك بأن يطلقها بلا بدل صح، فيصح تأجيله. ولهما: أن جميع المسمى بدل الرقبة حتى جرى عليه أحكام الإبدال من حق الأخذ بالشفعة وغيره فيما إذا باع دارا تساوي ألفا بألفين وحق الورثة كان متعلقا بالمبدل فكذا يتعلق بالبدل فينفذ تصرفه أي المحاباة في ثلث البدل. وهذا بخلاف الخلع؛ لأن البدل فيه لا يقابل المال، فإن البضع في حالة الخروج لا يعتبر مالا، فلم يتعلق حق الورثة بالمبدل، فلا يتعلق بالبدل.

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses the ruling on kitaba (contract of manumission) entered into by a master during his death illness. The central issue is that such transactions are treated like wills, limited to one-third of the estate. The text presents two scenarios: (1) kitaba amount exceeds value, and (2) value exceeds kitaba amount. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the charitable element (muhabah) is evaluated in the entire kitaba amount, so two-thirds of the total kitaba must be paid immediately and one-third deferred. Imam Muhammad holds that the charity is evaluated in the slave's value only, so only two-thirds of the value (not the total kitaba) must be paid immediately; the remainder is deferred. The passage provides arguments for each view, including analogies to a sale of a house and to khul'. The relied-upon position (as per the matn) is that of the Shaykhayn.

Key Terms
محاباة (muhabah): Charitable waiver or kindness; here, the act of deferring payment or reducing the price in a kitaba during death illness, treated as a bequest.
بدل (badal): Consideration or price; in kitaba, the payment that frees the slave.

Kitaba by Proxy and Joint Kitaba: Istihsan Over Qiyas
Ruling on kitaba by proxy and joint kitaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kitaba by a third party and on joint kitaba of a present and absent slave, and explain how istihsan overrides qiyas in these cases.

Core Idea
A third party's payment can free a slave without his consent; joint kitaba with an absent slave is valid on both by istihsan.

This lesson explores two special cases of kitaba (contract of manumission by payment). The first involves a free man acting as proxy, paying the slave's ransom without the slave's prior acceptance. The second involves a master writing kitaba on two slaves, one present and one absent. In both cases, the Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) to validate the arrangements, departing from strict analogy (qiyas) to achieve benefit for the slave and follow custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage discusses two distinct rulings: (1) kitaba by a free man on behalf of a slave, (2) joint kitaba on a present and absent slave. Note the conditions and outcomes for each.
The first scenario includes a condition that the third party pays; the second involves the present slave paying the full amount.
2
Analyze the qiyas (analogy) position
For each scenario, state what the strict analogy would require. For the first, qiyas says the slave is not freed because the contract is suspended and no conditional statement was made. For the second, qiyas says only the present slave becomes a mukatab because the absent one cannot consent.
Understanding the default ruling helps appreciate why istihsan intervenes.
3
Identify the istihsan (juristic preference) argument
For the first, istihsan frees the slave because there is no harm (la darar) and the arrangement benefits him. For the second, istihsan includes the absent slave as a dependent (tabi'), like a child included in the mother's kitaba.
Note the key phrases: 'la darar' (no harm) and 'tabi'' (dependent).
4
Extract the ruling and its conditions
From the istihsan position, derive the final ruling: In the first case, the slave is freed upon payment by the third party even without his acceptance. In the second, the kitaba is valid on both slaves, and the present one must pay the entire amount.
If the slave rejects before payment, he does not become free even if paid later.
5
Connect to Hanafi usul: istihsan as a source
Reflect that these rulings illustrate the Hanafi principle that istihsan can override qiyas when there is a stronger evidence (here: benefit and custom). This is a characteristic of the Hanafi school.
This is not a universal principle; other schools may limit istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتابة أم ولد والمدبر
(فتح) كاتب إلخ: لما فرغ المصنف عن بيان أحكام تتعلق بالأصل في الكتابة شرع في أحكام تتعلق بالنيابة فيها، فقال: "حر كاتب عن عبد إلخ، وصورة المسألة: أن يقول أجنبي لمولى عبد: كاتب عبدك فلانا على على أني إن أديت إليك ألفا فهو حر فكاتبه المولى على هذا الشرط، وأدى الرجل الألف، يعتق العبد بحكم الشرط من غير قبول العبد ،وإجازته، وإن قبل العبد الكتابة حين سمع كلامه قبل أدائه صار مكاتبا، فإن هذا العقد له جهتان نافذ في حق ما ينتفع العبد، أن وهو يعتق عند أداء الشرط وموقوف على إجازة من له الإجازة، فإذا قبله صار مكاتبا؛ لأن الإجازة في الانتهاء كالإذن في الابتداء.
ألف
درهم
وإن قال: لا أقبله، ثم أدّى القائل الألف لم يعتق؛ لأنه ارتد برده، ولو لم يقل الحر في هذه المسألة: على أني إن أديت إليك ألفا فهو حر وأدى لا يعتق في القياس؛ لأن العقد موقوف والموقوف لا حكم له، ولم يوجد التعليق، وفي الاستحسان يعتق؛ لأنه لا ضرر على العبد في عتقه بأداء الأجنبي، قال بعضهم: وهذه الصورة الأخيرة هي صورة المسألة المذكورة في المتن . (ملتقط من الحواشي والشروح) وإن كاتب إلخ: يعني إذا كاتب عبدين أحدهما حاضر والآخر غائب، سواء كان البداية من العبد بأن قال: كاتبني بألف عن نفسي وعن فلان الغائب، فكاتبهما المولى، فقبل الحاضر، أو من السيد بأن قال لعبده: كاتبتك وفلانا بألف، فقبل الحاضر، صح العقد عليهما استحسانا والقياس أن يصير الحاضر مكاتبا وحده؛ لأنه عقد الكتابة على نفسه وعلى الغائب، فينفذ عليه، ويتوقف في حق الغائب على إجازته كما إذا باع ماله ومال غيره، أو كاتب عبده وعبد غيره. وجه الاستحسان: أن المولى خاطب الحاضر قصدا وجعل الغائب تبعا له والكتابة على هذا الوجه مشروعة كالأمة إذا كوتبت دخل في كتابتها ولدها المولود في الكتابة، أو المشترى فيها، أو المضموم إليها في العقد تبعا لها حتى يعتقوا بأدائها، وليس عليهم شيء من البدل، فإذا كان كذلك ينفرد به الحاضر، ويستغني عن شرط رضا الغائب،=
Writing of umm walad and mudabbar. (Fath) He says: The author wrote about kitaba by proxy. A free man writes on behalf of a slave. The scenario: A stranger says to the master: 'Write a kitaba for your slave so-and-so on condition that if I pay you 1000, he is free.' The master does so, the man pays, the slave becomes free by the condition without acceptance. If the slave accepts before payment, he becomes a mukatab. The contract has two aspects: effective for benefit, and suspended on acceptance. If he refuses, then the man pays, he is not freed because he rejected. According to qiyas, if the man says 'if I pay...' and pays without condition? Actually it says: if the man does not say the condition, in qiyas he does not become free because the contract is suspended. In istihsan, he becomes free because no harm. Some say this is the scenario in the matn. If the master writes a kitaba on two slaves, one present and one absent, and the present accepts, the contract is valid on both by istihsan. By qiyas, only the present becomes a mukatab. Reason for istihsan: The master addresses the present and makes the absent a dependent, like a female slave's children included in her kitaba.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage discusses two issues related to kitaba by proxy. First, if a free man (ajnabi) says to the master: 'Make a kitaba with your slave on the condition that if I pay you 1000 dirhams, he is free,' and the master agrees, then if the man pays, the slave is freed by virtue of the condition, even without the slave's consent. If the slave accepts the kitaba before payment, he becomes a mukatab. This ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) because it benefits the slave. Second, if a master makes a kitaba on two slaves—one present and one absent—and the present one accepts, the kitaba is valid on both according to istihsan, with the present one responsible for the entire payment. The analogy (qiyas) would be that only the present one becomes a mukatab, but istihsan prevails due to custom (the absent slave is a dependent, similar to a child included in the mother's kitaba).

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that allows a departure from strict analogy (qiyas) for a stronger reason, here the benefit to the slave or custom.
كتابة (kitaba): A contract between a master and slave whereby the slave is promised freedom upon payment of a specified sum.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning: applying a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the joint kitaba of a present and absent slave, what is the basis for the istihsan ruling that the contract is valid on both?
A) The absent slave is treated as a dependent (tabi') of the present one
B) The master's unilateral declaration is sufficient
C) The absent slave is considered to have given proxy by custom
D) The payment is split equally between the two

Key Takeaway
Hanafi school uses istihsan to permit kitaba by proxy and joint kitaba with an absent slave, prioritizing benefit and custom over strict qiyas.

Kitaba of a Female Slave with Her Young Sons
Ruling and commentary on kitaba by an umm walad for herself and her children

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a female slave's kitaba for herself and her young sons, explain the basis in istihsan, and apply the rulings on payment and manumission in this joint kitaba.

Core Idea
A female slave can validly include her children in her kitaba by istihsan, despite lacking guardianship.

The Hanafi school upholds the validity of a female slave's kitaba contract that includes her young sons, even though the mother lacks legal guardianship over her children as a slave herself. This ruling is established by istihsan (equitable preference), overriding a strict qiyas that would require guardianship. The inclusion of the children is treated as a condition (shart) rather than a matter of guardianship, drawing an analogy to the case of an absent person included in a kitaba without their permission. This lesson unpacks the principal ruling, the proof from istihsan, and the detailed subsidiary rulings on payment, manumission, and the distribution of freedom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principal ruling and its proof
Start by noting that the kitaba by a female slave for herself and her young sons is declared 'sahih' (valid) by istihsan. The proof is not from Quran or Sunnah but from a rational preference: the benefit of enabling freedom and the precedent of the absent party case.
The text says 'صح استحسانا' – valid by istihsan.
2
Understand the analogy to the absent party case
The inclusion of children is analogous to including an absent person in a kitaba. The absence of guardianship is overcome because the children enter the contract as a conditional appendage, similar to an absent party who is included without their agency.
Just as an absent party's permission is immaterial, so too the children's acceptance or rejection is not considered.
3
Analyze the subsidiary rulings on payment and freedom
If any one of the parties (mother or sons) pays the full kitaba amount, all become free, and the master must accept. The paying party cannot reclaim from the others. If the master manumits one party, the obligations adjust accordingly.
The present/absent framework governs these details: the present party is liable for the whole payment, the absent party is a follower.
4
Apply the ruling to scenarios
Consider scenarios: what if the master gifts the payment to the mother? All become free. Gifting to an absent son does not free the others. If the absent son is manumitted, the present's share is dropped. The earnings of the absent child cannot be taken by the master.
These rules mirror the case of a kitaba between a present and absent individual.

Source Text

وإن كاتبت الأمة عن نفسها وعن ابنين صغيرين لها، صح، وأي أدّى، لم يرجع. المؤدي للأمة على صاحبه - ويطالب الحاضر بكل البدل؛ لأن كله عليه دون الغائب، ولا يعتبر إجازة الغائب ولا ردّه، ولا يؤاخذ الغائب بالبدل، ولا بشيء منه، ولو اكتسب شيئا ليس للمولى أن يأخذه منه ولو أبرأ المولى الحاضر، أو وهب بدل الكتابة له عتقا جميعا، وإن وهبه للغائب لم يعتقا، ولو أعتق الغائب سقط عن الحاضر حصته من البدل، ولو أعتق الحاضر لم يعتق الغائب، وسقط حصة الحاضر من الكتابة، ويؤدي الغائب حصته حالا، وإلا رد إلى الرق كذا في "التكملة" و"العيني" وغيرهما. وأيهما أدى عتقا إلخ: أي وأي من الحاضر والغائب أدى بدل الكتابة عتقا جميعا؛ لوجود شرط عتقهما، ويجبر المولى على القبول، أما إذا دفع الحاضر؛ فلأن البدل عليه وأما إذا دفع الغائب؛ فلأنه ينال به شرف الحرية، فيجبر المولى على القبول، لكونه مضطرا كما إذا أدى ولد المكاتبة فإنه يجبر على القبول، وإن لم يكن البدل عليه. تكملة البحر الرائق: ١١٠/٨] دین ولا يرجع على صاحبه إلخ يعني لا يرجع واحد منهما بما أدى من البدل على الآخر، أما الحاضر؛ فلأنه قضى نفسه، وأما الغائب؛ فلكونه أدى بغير أمره، وليس مضطر فيه تكملة البحر الرائق: ١١٠/٨] (عيني) ولا يؤخذ إلخ يعني لا يطالب المولى العبد الغائب ببدل الكتابة؛ لأنه لا دين عليه؛ لأنه لم يلتزم له بشيء، وإنما دخل في الكتابة تبعا ، فصار نظير ولد المكاتبة. [ تكملة البحر الرائق: ١١٠/٨] (عيني) وقبوله لغو : يعني قبول الغائب ورده لغو ؛ لأن الكتابة قد نفذت وتمت من غير قبوله، فلا يعتبر بعد ذلك قبوله ولا رده كمن كفل دينا عن غيره بغير ،أمره فبلغه فإجازته ،باطلة ولا يتغير حكمه حتى لو أدى لا تكملة البحر الرائق: ۱۱۱/۸] صح: أي صـ هذا العقد استحسانا والقياس أن لا يجوز، وقد ذكرنا وجهه في صح مسألة الغائب؛ لأن هذه مثلها في جميع ما ذكرنا من الأحكام؛ لأن الأم والأب الرقيق لا ولاية لهما على ولدهما، فيكون دخول الولد في كتابتهما بالشرط لا بالولاية كدخول الغائب في كتابة الحاضر، وقبول الأولاد وردهم لا يعتبر. [ تكملة البحر الرائق: ١١١/٨] يرجع. وأي أدى إلخ [ أي أي واحد من الثلاثة وهم الأم والابنان. (عيني)] أي لا يرجع أحدهم على صاحبه لما ذكرنا في مسألة الغائب، ويجبر المولى على القبول، ولو أعتق الأم بقي عليهم من بدل الكتابة بحصتهم يؤدونها في الحال، بخلاف المولود في الكتابة والمشترى حيث يعتقان بعتقها ويطالب المولى الأم ،دونهم، ولو أعتقهم سقط عنها حصتهم، وعليها الباقي على نجومها، وليس له أن يبيعهم، ولو أبرأهم عن الدين أو وهبهم لا يصح، ولها يصح، ويعتقون معها، لما ذكرنا في كتابة الحاضر مع الغائب تكملة البحر الرائق: ١١١/٨] (عيني)
And if a female slave makes a kitaba contract for herself and for two young sons of hers, it is valid, and whichever of them pays, they do not reclaim [from the other]. The one who pays for the female slave [does not claim] from its companion. And the present one is demanded for the entire payment because it is all upon him, not the absent one. The permission of the absent one nor his rejection are considered. The absent one is not taken to account for the payment nor any part of it. And if he earns something, the master may not take it from him. And if the master discharges the present one, or gifts the kitaba payment to him, they both become free. But if he gifts it to the absent one, they do not become free. And if the absent one is manumitted, the present one's share of the payment is waived. And if the present one is manumitted, the absent one does not become free, and the present one's share of the kitaba is dropped, and the absent one pays his share immediately, otherwise he is returned to slavery. Thus in al-Takmila and al-Ayni and others. 'And whichever of them pays, they become free etc.': meaning whichever of the present and absent pays the kitaba payment, they both become free because the condition for their freedom exists, and the master is compelled to accept. If the present pays, because the payment is upon him; if the absent pays, because he attains the honor of freedom, so the master is compelled to accept because he is compelled, just as if the child of a female slave under kitaba pays, he is compelled to accept even though the payment is not upon him. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:110) 'And they do not reclaim from its companion etc.': means neither of them reclaims from the other what he paid. As for the present, because he paid his own debt; as for the absent, because he paid without his order, and he is not compelled. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:110) (Ayni) 'And the absent is not taken etc.': means the master does not demand from the absent slave the kitaba payment because he has no debt on him, since he did not undertake anything, but entered the kitaba as a follower, so he became like the child of the female slave under kitaba. [Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:110] (Ayni) 'And his acceptance is void': means the absent one's acceptance and rejection are void because the kitaba has been executed and completed without his acceptance, so afterwards his acceptance or rejection are not considered, like one who guarantees a debt for another without his order, then it reaches him, his permission is invalid and its ruling does not change, even if he pays. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:111) 'Valid': i.e., this contract is valid by istihsan, and by qiyas it would not be permitted, and we have mentioned its basis in the discussion of the absent one, because this is like that in all the rulings we mentioned, because the mother and father when they are slaves have no guardianship over their children, so the inclusion of the child in their kitaba is by condition, not by guardianship, like the inclusion of the absent one in the kitaba of the present one. And the acceptance or rejection of the children is not considered. [Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:111] 'They do not reclaim': 'And whichever pays etc.' [i.e., whichever of the three, the mother and the two sons (Ayni)] i.e., none of them reclaims from the other for the reason we mentioned in the case of the absent one. And the master is compelled to accept. And if the mother is manumitted, the remaining kitaba payment remains on them according to their share, which they pay immediately, unlike the child born during kitaba or purchased, for they become free by her manumission and the master demands from the mother, not them. And if they are manumitted, their share is waived from her, and the remainder is on her according to her installments. And he may not sell them. And if he discharges them from the debt or gifts it to them, it is not valid, but it is valid for her, and they become free with her, as we mentioned in the kitaba of the present with the absent. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:111) (Ayni)
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school on the validity of a female slave entering into a kitaba contract (a contract of manumission) for herself and her two young sons. The ruling is established by istihsan, and it contrasts with qiyas which would deem it invalid because the mother lacks legal guardianship over her children (she is herself a slave). The Hanafi position is that the inclusion of the children is by condition (shart) and not by guardianship, analogous to the case of an absent person included in a kitaba by a present person without their permission. The passage then discusses various scenarios: if any one of them (mother or sons) pays the kitaba payment, all become free and none can reclaim from the other. Detailed rules follow about the treatment of a present and absent party in a joint kitaba, which serve as an analogy for the mother-child case. The commentary emphasizes that the children's acceptance or rejection is not considered because the contract is executed without their agency. The passage also covers situations where the master manumits one party, the effect of gifts or discharge, and the immediate payment obligations. The ruling is derived from the principle that a slave's earnings belong to the master, but under kitaba, the slave's earnings apply to the debt. The commentary from al-Takmila and al-Ayni confirms the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
مكاتبة (mukatabah): A female slave who has entered into a kitaba contract (contract of manumission) with her master, agreeing to pay a certain sum in installments in exchange for freedom upon completion.
استحسان (istihsan): A method of legal reasoning that prefers a ruling based on equity, public benefit, or a stronger analogy, departing from the apparent qiyas. Here, it validates the kitaba despite the lack of guardianship.
تجزؤ الكتابة (tajazzu' al-kitaba): The divisibility of a kitaba contract, meaning that partial performance can result in partial freedom. In the context of joint kitaba, it determines how payment and freedom are allocated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the mother has inherent wilayah over her children even as a slave.
B) Because the children are included by condition (shart) as a subordinate part of the kitaba, analogous to the inclusion of an absent party.

D) Because the children are considered joint owners in the kitaba.

Key Takeaway
A female slave can validly include her young sons in her kitaba contract by istihsan, based on the analogy to the absent party case, with detailed rules on payment and manumission following from that analogy.

Kitaba of a Joint Slave: The Dispute on Divisibility (Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on kitaba divisibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the divisibility of kitaba for a jointly-owned slave and apply the ruling to determine ownership of payments and freedom.

Core Idea
Kitaba divisibility determines whether partial payment frees one share or the whole slave.

In this lesson, we examine a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: when one co-owner of a slave authorizes the other to make a kitaba on his share, does the kitaba affect only that share or the entire slave? The answer hinges on whether the kitaba contract is divisible (tatajazzau) or indivisible. This dispute has practical consequences for who owns the collected payments and the slave's status upon partial payment or incapacity. We will explore the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two great students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Two individuals jointly own a slave. One owner (the authorizer) grants permission to the other (the authorized) to make a kitaba contract for the authorized owner's share and to collect the kitaba payments. The slave pays part of the price and then becomes incapable (ajaza).
The authorization is specifically for the authorized owner's share, not the whole slave.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling
Abu Hanifa holds that the kitaba is divisible (tatajazzau). Therefore, the collected payments belong exclusively to the authorized owner who collected them. Only the authorized owner's share in the slave is freed proportionally to the payment. The slave remains partially slave in the other owner's share.
This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school (mufta bihi).
3
State the Sahibayn's ruling
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the kitaba is indivisible. The authorization to make kitaba for a share is effectively authorization for the whole slave. Thus, the contract covers both owners, payments are shared between them, and full payment frees the entire slave.
This view is considered strong but not the operative position for fatwa.
4
Trace the basis of the dispute
The dispute originates from whether the kitaba contract is analogous to emancipation (i'taq) in terms of divisibility. Abu Hanifa compares it to freeing a share, which is allowed. The Sahibayn emphasize the unity of the contract subject matter, arguing that a kitaba cannot be split.
Both sides use qiyas (analogical reasoning) but reach different conclusions.
5
Apply to practical consequences
Under Abu Hanifa, if the slave becomes unable to pay, the collector keeps what was collected, and the slave is partially free. The silent partner may rescind before payment if not authorized. Under the Sahibayn, payments are shared and the entire slave is freed upon full payment.
The condition of 'collection' in the authorization is crucial for Abu Hanifa's ruling.

Source Text

والتكملة وملا مسكين بتغيير] ويقبض إلخ: إنما قيد الإذن بالكتابة بالقبض؛ لينقطع حقه في المقبوض ويختص به القابض؛ لأن إذنه بالقبض إذن لعبده بالأداء إليه فيكون الآذن متبرعا بنصيبه على العبد المكاتب إلا إذا نهاه قبل الأداء، فيصح لهيه؛ لأنه تبرع لم يتم. فتح باختصار) بألف رجع
Chapter on the Kitaba of the Joint Slave: A slave owned by two men, one of them authorized his partner to make a kitaba for [the partner's] share of the joint slave for a thousand [dirhams] and to collect the kitaba payment... owned by two, i.e., the two owners, one of the owners, i.e., his partner in the slave, i.e., the share of the authorized one. 'Chapter on the Kitaba of the Joint Slave': This is a chapter explaining the rulings on the kitaba of a joint slave. When he finished the kitaba of a slave not jointly owned, he began with the kitaba of a joint slave because the default is non-partnership, as stated in Ghayat al-Bayan. Most commentators say: he mentioned the kitaba of two after one because two comes after one. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:111) 'His partner authorized him to make a kitaba etc.': i.e., if a slave is owned by two, and one authorized his partner to make a kitaba for his share of the joint slave for a thousand, and to collect the kitaba payment, so he made an agreement and collected part of the thousand, then the slave became incapable (ajaza), then what was collected of the thousand belongs to the collector, according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he is a mukatab for both of them, and what was collected is shared between them. The basis is that the kitaba is divisible (tatajazzau) according to Imam [Abu Hanifa], and according to them it is not divisible as mentioned in emancipation. So if that is the case, it confers freedom from one aspect, so it is confined to his share due to divisibility in his view. According to them, since the kitaba is not divisible, the authorization to make a kitaba for his share is an authorization to make a kitaba for the whole; so he is principal in half and agent in half, so it is between them, and what is collected is common between them, so it remains so after incapacity. According to Imam, the mukatab's half earnings belong to the authorizer. So if he authorized the mukatab to spend his half earnings which is his share, his authorization is valid, and that authorization is completed by the mukatab paying his debt with it, so what is collected goes to the collector. If the mukatab becomes incapable, the authorizer does not reclaim that, even if his objective (freedom) is not achieved, because the beneficiary of the gift is the slave. If the authorizer reclaims, he reclaims from the slave, and a master cannot claim a debt from his slave. He restricted it by saying 'one of them authorized' because if one did not authorize and the other made kitaba, he has the right of rescission before the payment of kitaba price according to all, because it harms the kitaba since it prevents the sale of his share immediately, and it becomes a case of istis'a (earning) in the second instance, and it is not valid except by a judge's decree or the slave's consent. And if he did not rescind the kitaba until the slave paid the kitaba price, then the share of the one who made kitaba is freed according to Abu Hanifa because kitaba is divisible in his view. The silent partner may take from the one who made kitaba half of what he took of the kitaba price. Then it is considered: if the one who made kitaba had contracted for the whole slave for a thousand, he does not reclaim anything from the mukatab slave of what his partner took from him; if he only contracted for his share, then [the silent partner reclaims] from the mukatab what his partner took. According to them (the two), by payment the whole is freed, and the silent partner reclaims from his partner if he is wealthy, otherwise from the slave as if he had manumitted him. And he may take half of the remaining earnings because it is the earnings of a joint slave. From al-Fath, al-Ayni, al-Takmila, and Mulla Miskin with modifications. 'And he collects etc.': He only restricted the authorization for kitaba with collection so that his right in what is collected is cut off and the collector is singled out. Because his authorization for collection is an authorization for his slave to pay to him, so the authorizer becomes a donor of his share to the mukatab slave, unless he forbids him before payment, then his prohibition is valid because the gift is not completed. (al-Fath concisely) 'With a thousand he reclaims.'
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage opens a new chapter on the kitaba of a jointly-owned slave ('abd mushtarak). The central issue is the legal effect when one of two co-owners authorizes the other to make a kitaba contract for the authorized person's share of the slave. The author presents the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn). Abu Hanifa holds that kitaba is divisible (tatajazzau), meaning that partial payment frees the paying party's share proportionally. Therefore, if the authorized person makes a kitaba for his own share and collects part of the payment, that part belongs to him alone, and only his share becomes free if full payment is made. The silent co-owner retains his share in the slave. In contrast, the Sahibayn hold that kitaba is indivisible; thus, the authorization to make kitaba for a share is effectively an authorization for the entire slave, making the contract valid for both owners. Consequently, the payments are shared between them, and full payment frees the whole slave. The passage details the consequences in various scenarios, such as when the slave becomes incapable of paying, and the rights of the co-owners to seek compensation. The commentary cites multiple sources (al-Fath, al-Ayni, al-Takmila) and explains that the condition of 'collection' in the authorization ensures that the collector becomes the exclusive owner of the collected amount, as the authorizer is deemed to have gifted his share to the slave. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is generally that of Abu Hanifa, especially in transactions, though the Sahibayn's view is also considered strong. The passage also discusses the silent partner's right to rescind the contract before payment if he did not authorize.

Key Terms
عبد مشترك (abd mushtarak): A slave owned jointly by two or more masters. The chapter deals with kitaba involving such a slave.
تجزؤ الكتابة (tajazzu' al-kitaba): The divisibility of a kitaba contract, meaning that the contract can be partially executed regarding ownership shares. Abu Hanifa holds it is divisible; Sahibayn hold it is not.
إذن (idhn): Permission or authorization given by one co-owner to the other to perform a legal act (like making a kitaba) on the joint property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if one co-owner of a joint slave is authorized by the other to make a kitaba for his share, and the slave pays part of the kitaba price and then becomes incapable, what happens to the amount already paid?
A) It is divided equally between both owners.
B) It belongs exclusively to the authorized owner who collected it.
C) It is returned to the slave.
D) It is given to the silent partner as compensation.

Key Takeaway
The divisibility of kitaba is a core principle in Hanafi fiqh that determines the effects of partial ownership and payment in joint slave contracts, and the relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa.

Ruling on Collection from Jointly Owned Mukatab in Case of Failure
Concise ruling on joint kitabah failure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the disposition of collected kitabah payments when a jointly owned mukatab fails to pay the remainder.

Core Idea
The collecting co-owner keeps what he took; the slave must still work for the silent partner's share.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a specific scenario in the law of kitabah (contract of manumission by payment). When two co-owners jointly manumit a slave on a kitabah, and one co-owner collects part of the payment, what happens if the slave fails to pay the rest? The concise ruling provides clarity: the collected amount belongs to the collector, and the slave remains obliged to the silent partner. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and implications.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the scenario
Identify the facts: jointly owned slave, kitabah contract, partial collection by one co-owner, then the slave's failure (ajz) to pay the remainder.
The slave's failure could be due to incapacity, death, or inability to earn.
2
State the ruling
Memorize the principle: 'fama qabada fa lilmā qābid' – what was collected belongs to the collector. The silent partner has no claim on that amount.
This is the core of the matn.
3
Understand the rationale
The silent partner consented to the kitabah, so he implicitly accepted that the other co-owner might collect and retain payments. Hence, no liability arises.
The text says 'li-annahu yardāhu' – because he is pleased with him.
4
Note the positive case
If the slave does not fail but completes payment, the co-owner who authorized the kitabah has his share of the slave freed.
This is the counter-example that highlights the condition.
5
Apply to similar cases
The slave must continue working to pay the silent partner's share; the collector is not obligated to share what he collected.
This maintains the slave's obligation toward the silent partner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المكاتب ٢٠٥ كتابة العبد المشترك فكاتب وقبض بعضه، فعجز، فالمقبوض للقابض. المكاتب أي بعض الألف من بدل الكتابة الشريكان أداء الباقي ولو لم يعجز وأدى جميع البدل، عتق حظه أي المأذون له في المكاتب، الاختلاف فعجز المكاتب بفتح التاء عن ولا يضمن لشريكه؛ لأنه يرضاه، ولكن يسعى العبد في نصيب الساكت.
Book of the Mukatab. Writing of the jointly owned slave. So he made a contract of kitabah and collected part of it, then he became unable, so what was collected belongs to the collector. The mukatab means some of the thousand from the kitabah price. The two partners pay the rest. And if he did not become unable and paid all the price, his share becomes free, i.e., the one authorized in the kitabah. The difference: if the mukatab (with fatha on the ta) fails, he does not guarantee for his partner because he is pleased with him, but the slave works for the share of the silent one.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq followed by a brief commentary. The ruling: If a jointly owned slave is made a mukatab, and one co-owner collects part of the kitabah payment, and then the slave fails to pay the rest (i.e., becomes unable), the amount already collected belongs to the collector. This is because the collection was valid and the slave's failure does not retroactively invalidate it. The commentary explains that 'al-mukatab' here refers to part of the payment (the thousand dirhams typically mentioned in kitabah). If the slave does not fail but completes payment, the co-owner who authorized the kitabah has his share freed. If the slave fails, the collecting co-owner does not owe anything to his partner for the collected amount because the partner implicitly consented when he allowed the kitabah. However, the slave must continue to work towards the silent partner's share until it is paid off.

Key Terms
المكاتب (al-mukatab): A slave who has made a contract of kitabah with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
القابض (al-qabid): The one who receives and takes possession of payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two co-owners make their jointly owned slave a mukatab, one co-owner collects 500 dirhams, and then the slave fails to pay the remaining 500, what happens to the collected amount?
A) It is divided equally between the co-owners.
B) It is returned to the slave or his heirs.
C) It belongs to the co-owner who collected it.
D) It is forfeited to the state.

Key Takeaway
When a jointly owned mukatab fails after partial payment, the collecting co-owner keeps his collection, and the slave continues to work for the silent partner's share.
