Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Divisibility of Istilad in Mukatabah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on divisibility of istilad in mukatabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the divisibility of istilad in a jointly owned mukatabah and apply the mufta bihi position to determine ownership and lineage.

Core Idea
In a mukatabah, istilad is divisible per Abu Hanifa but indivisible per the Sahibayn, affecting ownership and lineage.

This passage presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions regarding the legal effect of a co-owner having a child with a jointly owned mukatabah. The dispute hinges on whether kitabah is analogous to tadbir (binding contract) or can be rescinded to complete istilad. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly determining the status of the slave-girl and the children.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three slave statuses
The passage categorizes slaves into qinn (ordinary), mudabbara (with tadbir), and mukatabah (under kitabah). For qinn, istilad is indivisible; for mudabbara, it is divisible. The dispute centers on mukatabah.
Consensus exists on qinn and mudabbara; only mukatabah is contested.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa holds istilad in mukatabah is divisible (like mudabbara) because kitabah is a binding contract akin to tadbir, preventing transfer of ownership. Thus, only the co-owner's share becomes umm walad.
He argues that tadbir prevents transfer, similarly kitabah prevents completion of istilad across both shares.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
The Sahibayn hold istilad is indivisible (like qinn) because kitabah can be rescinded when the mukatab is not harmed, allowing the completion of istilad by obtaining full ownership.
They argue that istilad must be completed as much as possible; rescinding kitabah for this purpose is permissible.
4
Apply the dispute to the concrete scenario
Two co-owners have a mukatabah; one has a child (first), then the other (second); then she fails. Under Abu Hanifa, the first's share becomes umm walad, and after failure, the entire slave becomes his, compensating the partner. The second's child is free by value (like al-maghroor). Under the Sahibayn, the entire slave becomes umm walad for the first immediately, and the second's child has no lineage.
This shows the practical financial and lineage differences.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi school follows Abu Hanifa's view as recorded in the matn. Commentators like al-Marghinani prefer it. This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states Abu Hanifa's view, indicating its authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أمة بينهما كاتباها، فكاتب وقبض بعضه، فعجز، فالمقبوض للقابض. أمة بينهما كاتباها، فكاتب وقبض بعضه، فعجز، فالمقبوض للقابض. أمة بينهما إلخ: هذه المسألة خلافية أيضا بين الإمام وصاحبيه كالسابقة، والمذكور هو قول الإمام، ومبنى بين الإمام وصاحبيه على تجزي استيلاد المكاتبة ،وعدمه وبيانه: أن الاستيلاد إما أن يقع في القنة، فهو غير متجز بالإجماع، فإذا كانت أمة مشتركة بين اثنين واستولدها أحدهما تصير أم ولد له ويتملك نصيب صاحبه، ويضمن له قيمته؛ لأن القنة تقبل النقل، فيكمل الاستيلاد وإما أن يقع في المدبرة، فهو متجز بالإجماع، فإذا استولد مدبرة مشتركة لا يكمل الاستيلاد ولا يصير كلها أم ولد له بل يقتصر على نصيبه؛ لأن المدبرة لا يمكن تمليكها؛ إذ التدبير يمنع النقل من ملك إلى ملك، وإما أن يقع في المكاتبة، فهو متجز عنده، غير متجز عندهما، فإذا استولد مكاتبة مشتركة تصير أم ولد له ويتملك نصيب الآخر عندهما، ويقتصر الاستيلاد على نصيبه عنده. لهما: أن الاستيلاد يجب تكميله ما أمكن، وقد أمكن هنا كما في الأمة المشتركة؛ لأن الكتابة تحتمل الفسخ فيما لا يتضرر به المكاتب والاستيلاد لا يحتمل فرجحنا الاستيلاد وكملناه، وفسخنا الكتابة في حق التمليك؛ لأنها تنفسخ فيما لا يتضرر المكاتب، وتبقى فيما وراءه، وإنما قلنا: الفسخ في حق أداء البدل، فيكون عليها كل بدل لكتابة عند الجمهور؛ لأن الانفساخ لضرورة التملك تكميلا للاستيلاد، فلا يظهر فيما وراءه، ولهذا جاز عتقه في الكفارة، بخلاف المدبرة؛ إذ التدبير يمنع النقل، فلا يمكن التمليك. للإمام : أن الاستيلاد يقبل التجزي إذا وقع في محل لا يقبل النقل، كالمدبرة بين اثنين إذا استولدها أحدهما، الكتابة عقد لازم كالتدبير، فتمنع تكميل ،الاستيلاد وإذا تمهد هذا، فاعلم أن في الصورة المذكورة لما استولدها حدهما، وادعى الولد يصير نصيبه أم ولد له ويقتصر على نصيبه فيثبت نسب الولد منه؛ لأنه وطئ في ملكه، لم إذا وطئها الآخر، وادعى الولد صحت دعوته، وثبت نسبه؛ لقيام ملكه، ثم إذا عجزت جعلت الكتابة كأن لم تكن، وتبين أن الأمة أم ولد للأول؛ لأن المقتضي للتكميل قائم والمانع من التكميل – وهو الكتابة – قد زال، يعمل المقتضي عمله من وجوده، فيضمن الأول للآخر نصف قيمتها؛ لأنه يتملك نصيبه لتكميل الاستيلاد، نصف عقرها؛ لوطئه جارية مشتركة، وضمن الآخر للأول قيمة الولد والولد حر بالقيمة؛ لأنه بمنزلة ولد المغرور؛ لأنه حين وطئها كان ملكه قائما ظاهرا، وولد المغرور ثابت النسب منه حرّ بالقيمة، والعقر كامل وطئه أمة الغير، هذا كله عند أبي حنيفة له. عندهما: لما لم يتجزأ استيلاد المكاتبة يصير هي أم ولد للأول، وهي مكاتبته كلها، وعليه نصف قيمتها حال كونها مكاتبة لشريكه عند أبي يوسف؛ لأنه تملك نصيب شريكه حال كتابتها وقيمة المكاتب على النصف من يمة القن، وعند محمد: يجب عليه الأقل من نصف قيمته ومن نصف ما بقي من بدل الكتابة، ولا يثبت نسب ولد الأخير من الآخر، ولا يكون الولد حرا بالقيمة ويغرم العقر لها. فافهم واحفظ.
A slave-girl jointly owned by two, they made her a mukatabah. Then one made a kitabah and collected part, then she failed, so what was collected belongs to the collector. A slave-girl between them etc.: This issue is also disputed between the Imam and his two companions like the previous, and what is mentioned is the Imam's statement. The basis between the Imam and his two companions is the divisibility of istilad of the mukatabah and its non-divisibility. Its explanation: Istilad either occurs in a qinn (ordinary slave) – it is indivisible by consensus. So if a jointly owned slave-girl between two and one of them has a child with her, she becomes umm walad for him and he owns the share of his partner and guarantees its value to him, because the qinn accepts transfer, so istilad is completed. Or it occurs in a mudabbara – it is divisible by consensus. So if one has a child with a jointly owned mudabbara, istilad is not completed and she does not become all umm walad for him, rather it is confined to his share, because the mudabbara cannot be owned, because tadbir prevents transfer from one ownership to another. Or it occurs in a mukatabah – it is divisible according to him, not divisible according to them. So if one has a child with a jointly owned mukatabah, she becomes umm walad for him and he owns the other's share according to them, and istilad is confined to his share according to him. Their proof: Istilad must be completed as much as possible, and it was possible here as in the jointly owned qinn, because kitabah can be rescinded where the mukatab is not harmed, and istilad does not bear rescission. So we gave weight to istilad and completed it, and we rescinded the kitabah regarding ownership, because it is rescinded where the mukatab is not harmed, and it remains beyond that. We only say: rescission regarding payment of the price, so all the kitabah price becomes due upon her according to the majority, because the rescission is for the necessity of ownership to complete istilad, so it does not appear beyond that. Hence his manumission is valid in kaffarah, unlike the mudabbara, because tadbir prevents transfer, so ownership is not possible. Imam's proof: Istilad can be divisible when it occurs in a place that does not accept transfer, like a mudabbara between two when one has a child with her; kitabah is a binding contract like tadbir, so it prevents completion of istilad. When this is established, know that in the mentioned scenario, when he had a child with her and claimed the child, his share becomes umm walad for him and istilad is confined to his share, and the lineage of the child is established from him, because he had intercourse in his ownership. Then if the other had intercourse with her and claimed the child, his claim is valid and lineage is established due to his existing ownership. Then if she fails, the kitabah is treated as if it never was, and it becomes clear that the slave-girl is umm walad for the first, because the ground for completion exists and the preventer – kitabah – has been removed. So the ground operates and from its existence, the first guarantees to the other half her value, because he owns his share to complete istilad, and half her dower due to his intercourse with a jointly owned slave-girl. The other guarantees to the first the value of the child, and the child is free by its value, because it is like the child of a deceived person (al-maghroor), because when he had intercourse, his ownership was existing externally. The child of the deceived has lineage established from him and is free by its value. The full dower is due for his intercourse with another's slave-girl. All this according to Abu Hanifa. According to them: Since istilad of the mukatabah is indivisible, she becomes umm walad for the first, and she is entirely his mukatabah. He owes half her value as a mukatabah to his partner according to Abu Yusuf, because he owned his partner's share at the time of her kitabah, and the value of the mukatab is half the value of a qinn. According to Muhammad: He owes the lesser of half her value or half the remaining kitabah price. The lineage of the last child is not established from the second, nor is the child free by value, and he pays the dower for her. So understand and memorize.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) concerning the divisibility (tajazzi) of istilad (causing pregnancy) in a jointly owned mukatabah (female slave under kitabah). The passage first establishes the general categories: istilad in an ordinary slave (qinn) is indivisible by consensus, meaning if one co-owner has a child with the slave-girl, she becomes entirely his umm walad and he must pay the partner's share. Istilad in a mudabbara (slave with tadbir) is divisible, so the child-bearing only affects the co-owner's share. For a mukatabah, Abu Hanifa holds it is divisible (like mudabbara), while the Sahibayn hold it is indivisible (like qinn). Each side presents its reasoning. The Sahibayn argue that kitabah can be rescinded for the purpose of completing istilad, as is done in the case of a qinn, while Abu Hanifa argues that kitabah is a binding contract similar to tadbir, preventing transfer of ownership. After establishing the principle, the passage applies it to a specific scenario: two co-owners have a mukatabah; one has a child with her and claims it; then the other also has a child and claims it; then she fails to pay. According to Abu Hanifa, the first co-owner's share becomes umm walad, the second's claim is also valid, but upon failure, the first gets full ownership (since the preventer—kitabah—is removed), and he pays the second half her value and half her dower. The second pays the value of his child (which becomes free). According to the Sahibayn, istilad is indivisible, so she becomes entirely umm walad for the first, and he pays either half her value as a mukatabah (Abu Yusuf) or the lesser of half value or half remaining kitabah price (Muhammad). The second's child does not have lineage established and is not free. The passage concludes with 'fa-ifham wa-ihfadh' indicating this is a critical point to understand and memorize.

Key Terms
استيلاد (istilad): The act of a master having a child with his female slave, which gives her the status of umm walad.
تجزئ (tajazzi): Divisibility: whether the legal effect of istilad is confined to the share of the co-owner who caused it or extends to the entire slave.
المغرور (al-maghroor): A person who marries or has intercourse with a woman believing she is free or his property but she turns out to be a slave or another's property. The child is free and the 'deceived' father pays the value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if two co-owners jointly own a mukatabah and one co-owner has a child with her, what happens to the co-owner's share?
A) The entire slave-girl becomes his umm walad.
B) Only his share becomes umm walad, and he does not own the partner's share.
C) He must sell his share to his partner.
D) The slave-girl is freed immediately.

Key Takeaway
The divisibility of istilad in a jointly owned mukatabah is governed by the nature of kitabah: Abu Hanifa views it as binding (like tadbir), making istilad divisible; the Sahibayn view it as rescindable, making istilad indivisible. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.

Tadbir by a Co-Owner of a Mukatabah Who Then Fails
Ruling on tadbir by one co-owner of a jointly owned mukatabah who then fails

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on tadbir by a co-owner of a jointly owned mukatabah when she fails, and explain the consensus and underlying reasoning of the Hanafi imams.

Core Idea
Failure of a mukatabah voids a co-owner's tadbir retroactively, making her umm walad for the first istilad.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hanafi fiqh: the case of a jointly owned slave-girl who is a mukatabah. One co-owner has intercourse and claims a child; the second co-owner, instead of intercourse, performs tadbir (postponed manumission). When the slave fails (cajazat) to fulfill the kitabah, what is the legal outcome? The text presents a consensus ruling among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, while revealing differences in their legal reasoning. Understanding this ruling deepens appreciation for the conditions of tadbir and the effect of istilad on a mukatabah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the legal acts
List the sequence: two co-owners of a mukatabah, first has intercourse and claims child, second performs tadbir without intercourse, then the mukatabah fails. Recognize the key acts: istilad, tadbir, and cajaz.
The second co-owner did not have intercourse, only performed tadbir.
2
Determine the effect of failure on the kitabah
Upon failure, the kitabah is rescinded and the slave returns to slavery. The ownership of the slave, which was partially suspended, becomes fully vested in the master(s).
Failure retroactively reveals the true ownership status.
3
Apply the condition of ownership for tadbir
Tadbir requires complete ownership at the time of execution. Since the slave was a mukatabah, ownership was not complete for the second co-owner. Upon failure, it becomes clear that the first co-owner had prior istilad, which takes precedence.
The condition of ownership is key; tadbir by a non-owner is void.
4
Understand the consensus and differing rationales
The ruling is agreed: tadbir voids, she becomes umm walad for the first, financial obligations are imposed. But the reasoning differs: Sahibayn argue the first's istilad made him owner before failure, while Abu Hanifa argues failure retroactively reveals complete ownership for the first.
Despite different usul, the furu' (ruling) is unanimous.
5
Derive the financial consequences
The first must pay half the slave's value and half the dower (for his intercourse) to the second. The child belongs to the first. Payments made to the mukatabah before failure are valid and returned upon failure.
Financial obligations arise from istilad and joint ownership.

Then one of them had intercourse with her, and she gave birth, and he claimed the child. Then the other had intercourse, and she gave birth, and he claimed. Then she failed [to pay]. So she is umm walad for the first. He guarantees to his partner half her value and half her dower. His partner guarantees her dower for his intercourse with a jointly owned slave-girl, and the value of the child. And if either pays the dower to the mukatabah, it is valid. And if the second performed tadbir and did not have intercourse with her, then she failed, the tadbir is void, and she is umm walad for the first. He guarantees to his partner half her value and half her dower, and the child belongs to the first. 'And if pays' etc. means that if either of them pays the dower to the mukatabah before failure, it is permissible, because it is her right while the kitabah is valid, since she is entitled to her own benefits and earnings. So when she fails, she returns it to the master. This is the statement of the Imam. According to them, she became umm walad for the first, and he owes all the dower, because intercourse in the abode of Islam does not avoid either valid guarantee or preventive hadd penalty. The hadd is dismissed due to ambiguity, so the dower is obligatory. If she fails and is returned to slavery, she is returned to the master due to the appearance of his exclusive right. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:116). 'And if the second performed tadbir' etc. means in the mentioned scenario, that a slave-girl jointly owned with a kitabah, one had intercourse with her and claimed the child. If the second partner performed tadbir on the slave-girl without intercourse, then she fails in the kitabah, the tadbir is void, and she becomes umm walad for the first. He guarantees to his partner half her value and half her dower. This is by consensus among them. According to them, because the one who caused istilad owned her before failure, due to the indivisibility of istilad of the mukatabah as passed. According to him (Abu Hanifa), because upon failure it appears that all of her is umm walad for the first, and that the second never had ownership in her, as explained. Ownership is a condition for the validity of tadbir, unlike establishing lineage, because apparent ownership is sufficient for establishing lineage and entitlement to the child by deception. Hence, if someone bought a slave-girl and performed tadbir on her, then she proved to be owned by another, the tadbir is void. If he had a child with her and she proved to be owned by another, it is not void, and the child is free by its value. Likewise here: She is umm walad for the first, because he owns his partner's share and completes istilad due to possibility. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:116) (Ayni) 'And he guarantees to his partner' because istilad owned his share from the beginning according to them, and after failure it appears that the first owned it at the time of istilad, and the second's ownership is removed according to him, so he guarantees half her value. (Takmilat with clarification from the commentator) 'Half her value' because he owns half of her by istilad as we explained (Ayni). 'Half her dower' because he had intercourse with a jointly owned slave-girl, so he owes the dower accordingly. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:116) (Ayni) 'And the child is for the first' because his claim is established as passed. This ruling that the child is for the first, although derived from his statement 'she is umm walad for the first', is not repetition, because that is regarding the slave-girl herself, while this is regarding the child itself. If he had replaced it with 'and istilad is completed for the first', it would be better; because his saying 'the child is for the first' suggests that the second had intercourse and claimed the child, contrary to the assumed scenario. (Fath).
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on a special case: a jointly owned mukatabah, where the first co-owner has intercourse and claims a child, and then the second co-owner, instead of having intercourse, performs tadbir (postponed manumission) without intercourse, and then the slave-girl fails to complete the kitabah. The ruling, agreed upon by consensus among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, is that the tadbir becomes void, the slave-girl becomes umm walad entirely for the first co-owner, and he must pay half her value and half her dower to his partner. The child belongs exclusively to the first co-owner. The reasoning is explained: According to the Sahibayn, the first co-owner already owned the entire slave-girl before failure due to indivisible istilad, so the second had no right to perform tadbir. According to Abu Hanifa, although istilad was originally confined to his share, upon failure the preventer (kitabah) is removed, and it becomes apparent that the first owns the entire slave, retroactively voiding the tadbir. The condition of ownership for tadbir is not met. However, lineage is different: apparent ownership suffices for establishing lineage, so the second partner's potential child (if he had one) would still be his, but in this case he did not have intercourse. The passage also addresses the payment of dower: if either partner pays the dower to the mukatabah before failure, it is valid; after failure, it goes to the master. This underscores that the mukatabah has right to her earnings until failure. The final part from 'Fath' clarifies that the phrase 'the child is for the first' is not redundant: it refers to the child itself, while 'she is umm walad for the first' refers to the mother's status.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): A contract by which a master promises freedom to his slave upon his (the master's) death.
عقر (aqr): Dower or compensation paid to the owner of a slave-girl for having intercourse with her without right.
مكاتبة (mukatabah): A slave-girl who has a contract of kitabah, i.e., an agreement to purchase her freedom by paying installments.
استيلاد (istilad): The act of having a child with a slave-girl, which grants her the status of umm walad and freedom upon the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where the second co-owner performs tadbir without intercourse, and the mukatabah fails, what happens to the tadbir?
A) It remains valid because it was made in apparent ownership.
B) It becomes void, and the slave-girl becomes umm walad for the first co-owner.
C) It is upheld only for the share of the second co-owner.
D) It requires payment of half the value to the first co-owner to be valid.

Key Takeaway
Upon failure of a jointly owned mukatabah, a co-owner's tadbir is void due to lack of complete ownership, and she becomes umm walad for the co-owner who had istilad.

Kitaba of a Jointly Owned Slave: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn on Divisibility of Manumission
Explaining ruling when one partner frees a kitaba slave who becomes insolvent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the divisibility of manumission and explain the practical difference between Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's rulings in the case of a jointly owned mukatabah who becomes insolvent.

Core Idea
Manumission is divisible per Abu Hanifa, indivisible per Sahibayn — this changes recourse.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a nuanced scenario: two partners write a kitaba for their jointly owned female slave, then one partner frees her while wealthy. She later becomes unable to pay. Who bears the loss? The answer depends on a foundational principle: is manumission divisible or indivisible? We will trace the differing views of Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, and see how this principle affects the options available to the silent partner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Clearly state the facts: two partners co-own a slave, write a kitaba, one partner frees her while wealthy, then she becomes insolvent (unable to pay the kitaba installments).
This is the case in the passage.
2
Identify the core principle in dispute
The dispute hinges on whether manumission is divisible (tajazzu') or indivisible. This principle determines the legal effects of partial freeing.
Abu Hanifa: divisible; Sahibayn: indivisible.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's view and its consequences
Since manumission is divisible, only the freeing partner's share becomes free upon liberation. The other partner's share remains a mukatab until the slave's inability triggers the silent partner's options. The freeing partner guarantees half the value only after inability, then recovers from the slave.
The guarantee is postponed until inability.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's view and its consequences
Manumission is indivisible, so the entire slave is freed immediately upon the one partner's act. The kitaba is dissolved. The freeing partner must compensate the silent partner (if wealthy) but cannot recover from the slave; the silent partner may make the slave work (isti'sa') if the freeing partner is insolvent.
No recourse against the slave for the freeing partner.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its practical impact
The matn follows Abu Hanifa's view; later fatwa works generally uphold his position. Understand how the choice of principle changes the financial burden between the partners.
The mufta bihi gives the freeing partner recourse against the slave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كاتباها، فحررها أحدهما، موسرا، فعجزت ضمن لشريكه نصف قيمتها، ورجع به عليها. أي الشريكان الأمة أعتقها حال كون المعتق عن الكتابة المعتق ورجع به عليها. وإن كاتباها إلخ: صورة المسألة ظاهرة، وهذا المذكور من ضمان المعتق لشريكه نصف قيمتها، ورجوع الضامن بما أدى على الأمة مذهب أبي حنيفة وعندهما لا يرجع المعتق عليها، ويستسعيها الساكت إن كان المعتق معسرا. والأصل في هذا أن الإعتاق لا يتجزأ عندهما، والكتابة السابقة لا تمنع العتق فلما حررها أحدهما عتقت كلها للحال وانفسخت الكتابة، فيضمن المعتق لشريكه إن كان موسرا ولا يرجع عليها ويستسعيها إن كان معسرا، ومن أصل الإمام أن العتق يتجزأ عنده فجاز إعتاق النصف، فلا يؤثر الفساد في نصيب شريكه بل يبقى على حاله مكاتبا، فلا يضمن المعتق قبل العجز ؛ لعدم ظهور أثر الإعتاق فيها، فإذا عجزت ظهر أثر العتق، وكان للساكت الخيارات المذكورة في العتق وهي إن كان موسرا فله أن يعتق أو يستسعي أو الضمان، فإذا ضمن كان للمعتق أن على العبد، وإن كان المعتق معسرا كان له خيار العتق أو الاستسعاء على ما بينا في العتق تكملة البحر الرائق: ١١٦/٨] (عيني) فعجزت: إنما قيد الضمان بعجزها عن الكتابة؛ لأن الشريك ليس له أن يضمن المعتق قبل عجزها عند الإمام؛ لأن الإعتاق لما كان يتجزأ عنده كان أثره أن يجعل نصيب غير المعتق كالمكاتب فلا يتغير نصيب صاحبه بالعتق؛ لأنها مكاتبة قبل ذلك، وعندهما لما كان لا يتجزأ يعتق الكل فله أن يضمنه قيمة نصيبه مكاتبا إن كان موسرا، العبد إن كان معسرا. فتح بتغيير رجع به عليها أي رجع المعتق الذي يضمن لشريكه عليها عند الإمام؛ لأن المعتق قام مقام الساكت، وعندهما لا يرجع؛ لأنه ضمن حصته لشريكه بإعتاقه، وهو فعله، فلا يلزمها ضمان ما لزمه بفعله؛ لأن الإعتاق لا يتجزأ عندهما. (فتح)
And if they both wrote a kitaba, then one freed her while being wealthy, and she became unable to pay, he guarantees to his partner half her value, and he recovers it from her. Meaning the two partners (of the female slave) freed her while the freeing one was acting on behalf of the kitaba, and he recovers it from her. The phrase 'and if they both wrote a kitaba etc.' : the scenario is clear. This mentioned ruling—that the freeing one guarantees to his partner half her value and the guarantor recovers what he paid from the female slave—is the madhhab of Abu Hanifa. According to the two companions, the freeing one does not recover from her, and the silent partner makes the slave work for the value if the freeing one is insolvent. The principle is that manumission is indivisible according to them, and the previous kitaba does not prevent manumission; so when one freed her, she becomes fully free immediately and the kitaba is dissolved. Thus the freeing one guarantees to his partner if wealthy and does not recover from her, and he makes her work for the value if insolvent. According to the Imam's principle, manumission is divisible for him, so freeing half is valid; thus the corruption does not affect the partner's share but it remains as a mukatabah. So the freeing one does not guarantee before inability because the effect of manumission is not manifest. When she becomes unable, the effect of manumission appears, and the silent partner has the options mentioned in manumission: if wealthy, he may free, make the slave work, or demand guarantee. If he demands guarantee, the freeing one has [recourse] against the slave. If the freeing one is insolvent, the silent partner has the option of freeing or making the slave work, as we explained in manumission. (Completion from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:116) (Ayni). The phrase 'fa'ajazat' (so she became unable): The guarantee is conditioned upon her inability in the kitaba because the partner cannot demand guarantee from the freeing one before her inability according to the Imam, since manumission is divisible for him so its effect makes the non-freeing partner's share like a mukatab, so his share does not change by the freeing because she was a mukatabah before. According to them, since manumission is indivisible, the whole becomes free, so he can demand the value of his share as a mukatab if the freeing one is wealthy, and [make him pay] the slave if insolvent. (Fath). 'Returning upon her' means that the freeing one who guarantees to his partner recovers from her according to the Imam because the freeing one stands in place of the silent partner. According to them, he does not recover because he guaranteed his share to his partner by his own act of freeing, so she is not liable for what he incurred by his act, since manumission is indivisible according to them. (Fath).
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage belongs to the chapter on kitaba (contract of manumission) of a jointly owned slave. It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a scenario where two partners co-own a female slave (ama) and write a kitaba for her. Later, one partner frees her while wealthy, but she becomes unable to pay the kitaba. The ruling according to Abu Hanifa (Imam) is that the freeing partner must guarantee half her value to his partner (the silent partner), and then he can recover that amount from the slave. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the freeing partner cannot recover from the slave; instead, the silent partner has the option to make the slave work for the value (isti'sa') if the freeing partner is insolvent. The root of the ikhtilaf is the divisibility of manumission (i'taq). In the Hanafi school, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that manumission is divisible; thus, when one partner frees his share, only his portion becomes free, while the other partner's share remains under kitaba. Therefore, the freeing partner does not immediately owe anything until the slave's inability to pay becomes apparent, at which point the silent partner can choose among three options: (1) demand the freeing partner pay half the slave's value, (2) free his own share, or (3) make the slave work for the value. If the silent partner chooses to demand payment (daman), the freeing partner then has the right to recover that amount from the slave. The two companions, on the other hand, consider manumission indivisible. Hence, when one partner frees, the entire slave is freed immediately, dissolving the kitaba. The freeing partner must compensate his partner for his share regardless of the slave's ability, but he cannot recover that from the slave because it is his own act. The silent partner, if the freeing partner is insolvent, can make the slave work for the value of his share but cannot force the freeing partner to pay. The passage then explains the conditioning of the guarantee upon the slave's inability in Abu Hanifa's view. This is because before inability, the effect of the freeing is not manifest in the partner's share (it remains a mukatab). After inability, the freeing takes effect and the silent partner's options arise. The commentary also clarifies that when the freeing partner recovers from the slave, he stands in place of the silent partner. According to the two companions, no recovery is possible because the freeing partner's payment to his partner is a result of his own act of freeing, so the slave is not liable for it.

Key Terms
كتابة (kitaba): A contract between a master and a slave where the slave agrees to pay a certain sum in installments in exchange for eventual manumission.
عتق يتجزأ (i'taq yatajazza'): The principle of divisibility of manumission, meaning when a jointly owned slave is freed by one owner, only that owner's share becomes free.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a kitaba contract and is working toward freedom.
استسعاء (isti'sa'): Making a slave work to earn the value of his freedom, often used when a partial owner frees a slave and the other owner demands compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two companions (Sahibayn), if one partner frees a jointly owned mukatabah and she becomes insolvent, what happens?
A) The freeing partner compensates the silent partner and recovers from the slave.
B) The freeing partner compensates the silent partner and has no recourse against the slave.
C) The silent partner can demand the freeing partner pay half the value, but the freeing partner cannot recover from the slave.
D) The slave is freed immediately and the silent partner must work for the value.

Key Takeaway
The divisibility of manumission is a foundational principle that determines whether a freeing partner can recover from a jointly owned slave after compensating the co-owner.

Tadbir and Manumission in Joint Ownership: Options and Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on divisible vs indivisible tadbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the mudabbir's options under Abu Hanifa and the two companions when tadbir and freeing occur in different orders, and identify the practical consequences of the divisibility dispute.

Core Idea
The sequence of tadbir and manumission determines the mudabbir's remedies due to differing views on divisibility.

When a jointly owned slave receives tadbir from one partner and is later freed by the other, or when the order is reversed, the mudabbir's options depend on whether tadbir is considered divisible. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the views of Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn), highlighting a classic intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to predict outcomes in joint ownership scenarios involving contingent manumission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage covers two cases: (1) tadbir then freeing, (2) freeing then tadbir. Note the order and the parties involved (mudabbir and the other partner).
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and principle
Abu Hanifa holds that tadbir is divisible. Analyze how this affects each share: tadbir is confined to the mudabbir's share but 'corrupts' the other share, giving the mudabbir initial options.
The mudabbir's options are: demand guarantee (daman), free his own share, or make the slave work (isti'sa').
3
State the two companions' position and principle
The Sahibayn hold that tadbir is indivisible. Therefore, the mudabbir's tadbir encompasses the entire slave, making any later freeing void and automatically transferring the partner's share to the mudabbir.
Under Sahibayn, the freeing partner must pay half the value as daman tamalluk, regardless of wealth.
4
Apply the dispute to each scenario
For each order, trace how the mudabbir's options change. In the first scenario (tadbir then freeing), Abu Hanifa says initial options are truncated by the freeing; in the second, the mudabbir loses the guarantee option. Under Sahibayn, the second tadbir is void in the reverse order.
Pay attention to the valuation: mudabbar is worth two-thirds of a qinn because sale benefits are lost.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference is whether the mudabbir can choose among remedies or automatically becomes sole owner. Under Abu Hanifa, the mudabbir has flexibility; under Sahibayn, he must accept ownership and the partner pays a fixed amount.
The mufta bihi in this text is Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عبد لهما دبره أحدهما ثم حرره الآخر وهو موسر فللمدبر إن شاء أن يضمن المعتق نصف قيمته وإن شاء أعتق وإن شاء استسعى، وهذا عند الإمام ووجهه أن التدبير يتجزأ عنده، فيقتصر التدبير على نصيب المدبر لكن يفسد به نصيب الآخر، فيثبت له خيار التضمين أو الإعتاق أو الاستسعاء على ما عرف من مذهبه فإذا أعتقه الآخر لم يبق له خيار التضمين والاستسعاء، فيقتصر الإعتاق على نصيبه؛ لأنه يتجزأ عنده، لكن يفسد نصيب الآخر، أي المدبر فله أن يضمنه نصيبه وله خيار العتق والاستسعاء، فإذا ضمنه يضمنه قيمته مدبرا. تكملة البحر الرائق: ۱۱۷/۸] وعندهما: إذا دبره أحدهما، فإعتاق الآخر باطل؛ لأنه لا يتجزأ عندهما، فيملك المدبر نصيب صاحبه بالتدبير، ويضمن نصف قيمته موسرا كان أو معسرا؛ لأنه ضمان تملك فلا يختلف بهما، ويضمن نصيب قيمته قنا؛ لأنه صادفه التدبير، وهو قن رمز الحقائق: ۳۰۱/۲] للمدبر أن يضمّن المعتق نصف قيمته، وإن حرّره أحدهما، ثم دبره الآخر لا يضمن أي أعتق العبد أحد الشريكين أي الشريك الآخر المعتق. بيع وشبهه، للمدير: بكسر الباء أي الذي دبر العبد نصف قيمته أي يضمن المعتق للمدبر نصف قيمة العبد، لكن يلزم عليه نصف قيمته حال كونه مدبرا؛ لأن الإعتاق صادفه مدبرا وهو ثلثا قيمته قنا؛ لأن المنافع ثلاثة: واستخدام وشبهه وإعتاق وتوابعه وفات البيع فيسقط الثلث ولا يتملكه بالضمان؛ إذ لا يقبل النقل كما لو غصب مديرا وأبق وضمن قيمته. (فتح) وإن حرره أحدهما إلخ: هذه الصورة عكس الصورة السابقة ففي السابقة دبره أحدهما أولا ثم حرره الآخر، وفي هذه الصورة حرره أولا ثم دبره الآخر، والفرق بين حكمهما أن في الأولى للمدبر أن يضمن المعتق أو يعتق أو يستسعى، وهنا ليس للمدبر أن يضمن المعتق وإنما خياره في الاستسعاء والإعتاق؛ لأن المدبر كان له الخيارات السابقة من التضمين والإعتاق والاستسعاء، فإذا دبره لم يبق له خيار التضمين وبقي خيار العتق والاستسعاء وهذا عند الإمام، وعندهما: تدبير الثاني باطل؛ لأن الإعتاق لا يتجزأ عندهما، فيعتق كله فلم يصادف التدبير الملك، ويضمن المعتق قيمته إن كان موسرا؛ لأن هذا ضمان إعتاق، فيختلف بين اليسار والإعسار . (تكملة بزيادة من المحشي)
A slave jointly owned by two, one of whom gives tadbir (posthumous manumission), then the other frees him while wealthy: the mudabbir may, if he wishes, demand that the freeing one pay half his value, or he may free [his share], or he may make the slave work for it. This is according to the Imam. The rationale is that tadbir is divisible for him, so the tadbir is confined to the share of the mudabbir, but it corrupts the share of the other. Thus, the mudabbir has the option of demanding guarantee, freeing, or istis'a' as known from his madhhab. When the other frees him, the options of guarantee and istis'a' no longer remain; the freeing is confined to his own share because it is divisible for him, but it corrupts the share of the other, i.e., the mudabbir. So the mudabbir may demand his share [from the freeing one] and has the option of freeing and istis'a'. If he demands guarantee, he is guaranteed its value as a mudabbar. (Completion from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:117). According to the two companions: if one gives tadbir, the other's freeing is void because [manumission] is indivisible for them; the mudabbir owns the partner's share through tadbir, and he guarantees half his value whether the freeing one is wealthy or insolvent because it is a guarantee of ownership (daman tamalluk) and thus does not differ based on wealth, and he guarantees the value of his share as a slave (qinn) because tadbir encountered him as a slave. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:301). The mudabbir may demand that the freeing one pay half his value. If one freed him, then the other gave tadbir, the mudabbir does not demand guarantee — meaning the slave was freed by one of the two partners, i.e., the other partner freed him. (Explanation of 'sale and the like'). The mudabbir (with kasr of the ba – the one who gave tadbir) demands half his value, i.e., the freeing one guarantees to the mudabbir half the slave's value. But it is required of him half his value while being a mudabbar, because the freeing encountered him as a mudabbar, and he is two-thirds the value of a qinn, because the benefits are three: use and the like, freeing and its consequences, and the possibility of sale is lost, so one-third falls away, and he does not own it by the guarantee because it does not accept transfer, like if someone usurped a mudabbar and it ran away and he guaranteed its value. (Fath). The phrase 'if one freed him, then the other gave tadbir' etc.: This scenario is the reverse of the previous scenario. In the previous, one gave tadbir first, then the other freed. In this scenario, he freed first, then the other gave tadbir. The difference between their rulings is that in the first, the mudabbir may demand guarantee, free, or istis'a'. Here, the mudabbir does not have the option of demanding guarantee; rather, his option is istis'a' and freeing. Because the mudabbir had the earlier options of guarantee, freeing, and istis'a'; when he gave tadbir, the option of guarantee no longer remains, and the option of freeing and istis'a' remain. This is according to the Imam. According to the two companions, the second tadbir is void because manumission is indivisible for them, so the whole slave becomes free, and the tadbir does not encounter ownership, and the freeing one guarantees his value if wealthy, because this is a guarantee of manumission (daman i'taq), so it differs based on wealth and insolvency. (Completion with addition from the commentator).
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on kitaba discusses the interaction between tadbir (posthumous manumission) and manumission (i'taq) in a jointly owned slave. It covers two scenarios and, as in the previous lesson, the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn) based on the principle of divisibility of manumission. In the first scenario, one partner gives tadbir (becoming the mudabbir) and then the other partner frees the slave while wealthy. According to Abu Hanifa, tadbir is divisible, so the tadbir is limited to the mudabbir's share but corrupts the other share. The mudabbir initially has three options: (1) demand the freeing partner pay half the slave's value, (2) free his own share, or (3) make the slave work (isti'sa'). However, once the other partner actually frees the slave, the mudabbir loses the options of demanding guarantee and istis'a' (since the freeing act has already occurred) and retains only the option to free his own share or make the slave work. If the mudabbir chooses to demand guarantee, he will be paid the value as a mudabbar (not as a regular slave). Under the two companions, the freeing by the second partner is void because manumission is indivisible; the mudabbir automatically owns the partner's share through the tadbir, and the freeing partner must pay half the slave's value as a guarantee of ownership (daman tamalluk), which does not differ based on wealth. In the second scenario (reverse order), one partner frees the slave first, then the other gives tadbir. According to Abu Hanifa, the mudabbir (the one who gave tadbir second) no longer has the option to demand guarantee from the freeing partner; he can only free his own share or make the slave work. This is because at the time of giving tadbir, the mudabbir had already lost the right to demand guarantee (since the freeing had already occurred). According to the two companions, this second tadbir is void, and the freeing partner must pay the full value if wealthy (as it is a guarantee of manumission, which varies with wealth). The passage also explains the calculation of the value: when a slave is a mudabbar, his value is reduced (e.g., to two-thirds of a regular slave) because the benefits of sale are lost. This affects the amount the mudabbir can claim.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): A declaration by a master that a slave will be free upon the master's death; it is a form of contingent manumission.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been given tadbir; he becomes free upon the master's death.
ضمان تملك (daman tamalluk): A guarantee of ownership, where the guarantor pays the value and acquires ownership of the slave.
ضمان إعتاق (daman i'taq): A guarantee related to manumission, where the payment is required from the freeing party and depends on his financial status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two companions (Sahibayn), in the scenario where one partner gives tadbir and the other subsequently frees the slave, what happens to the freeing?
A) The freeing is valid but only for the freeing partner's share.
B) The freeing is void, and the mudabbir owns the entire slave automatically.
C) The freeing triggers the mudabbir's option to demand guarantee.
D) The freeing is valid, and the mudabbir must accept it.

Key Takeaway
The sequence of tadbir and manumission determines the mudabbir's remedies, and the key ikhtilaf is whether tadbir is divisible, affecting the entire outcome.

Order of Tadbir and Itq: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on a Jointly Owned Slave
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sequence of tadbir and itq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a jointly owned slave is freed before being made mudabbar, and explain how Imam Abu Hanifa's view differs from that of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The order of tadbir and itq changes the mudabbar-owner's remedies; when freedom precedes, the option to claim value is lost.

This lesson examines a specific case from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: a jointly owned slave who is first freed by one partner and then later made mudabbar by the other. The ruling hinges on the sequence of events, and there is a disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). Understanding this distinction clarifies the Hanafi position on the indivisibility of emancipation and the rights of a mudabbar-owner.

Guided Path
1
State the two scenarios
The passage presents two opposite sequences: (1) tadbir then itq, (2) itq then tadbir. Identify each.
2
Identify the Hanafi position for each scenario
For scenario 1, the mudabbar-owner has three options (claim value, free, seek earnings). For scenario 2, according to Abu Hanifa, the mudabbar-owner loses the option to claim value but retains the other two.
3
Explain the Sahibayn's objection
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the second tadbir is invalid because emancipation is indivisible; the slave is fully freed, and the manumitter must guarantee the value if wealthy.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in scenario 2, Abu Hanifa allows the mudabbar-owner to still free or seek earnings, while the Sahibayn hold that the slave is fully free and the manumitter pays compensation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq follows Abu Hanifa's view, which is the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتابة العبد المشترك
للمدبر أن يضمّن المعتق نصف قيمته، وإن حرّره أحدهما، ثم دبره الآخر لا يضمن أي ، أعتق العبد أحد الشريكين أي الشريك الآخر المعتق. بيع وشبهه، للمدير: بكسر الباء أي الذي دبر العبد نصف قيمته أي يضمن المعتق للمدبر نصف قيمة العبد، لكن يلزم عليه نصف قيمته حال كونه مدبرا؛ لأن الإعتاق صادفه مدبرا وهو ثلثا قيمته قنا؛ لأن المنافع ثلاثة: واستخدام وشبهه وإعتاق وتوابعه وفات البيع فيسقط الثلث ولا يتملكه بالضمان؛ إذ لا يقبل النقل كما لو غصب مديرا وأبق وضمن قيمته. (فتح) وإن حرره أحدهما إلخ: هذه الصورة عكس الصورة السابقة ففي السابقة دبره أحدهما أولا ثم حرره الآخر، وفي هذه الصورة حرره أولا ثم دبره الآخر، والفرق بين حكمهما أن في الأولى للمدبر أن يضمن المعتق أو يعتق أو يستسعى، وهنا ليس للمدبر أن يضمن المعتق وإنما خياره في الاستسعاء والإعتاق؛ لأن المدبر كان له الخيارات السابقة من التضمين والإعتاق والاستسعاء، فإذا دبره لم يبق له خيار التضمين وبقي خيار العتق والاستسعاء وهذا عند الإمام، وعندهما: تدبير الثاني باطل؛ لأن الإعتاق لا يتجزأ عندهما، فيعتق كله فلم يصادف التدبير الملك، ويضمن المعتق قيمته إن كان موسرا؛ لأن هذا ضمان إعتاق، فيختلف بين اليسار والإعسار . (تكملة بزيادة من المحشي)
Writing of the jointly owned slave. The mudabbar-owner can guarantee the half value from the manumitter. If one of them freed him, then the other made him mudabbar, he does not guarantee. That is, one of the two partners freed the slave, meaning the other partner manumitted. [Commentary] For the mudabbar: with kasra of the ba, i.e. the one who declared tadbir for the slave, half its value, i.e. the manumitter guarantees to the mudabbar half the value of the slave. But that which is due from him is half its value at the time it was mudabbar, because the emancipation encountered it as mudabbar, and it is two-thirds of its value as a slave, because benefits are three: use and similar, and emancipation and its consequences, and the sale is lost, so the third falls and he does not own it by guarantee, since it does not accept transfer, just as if he usurped a mudabbar and he [the slave] fled and he guaranteed its value. (Fath) 'And if one of them freed him, etc.': This case is the opposite of the previous case. In the previous case, one of them first made him mudabbar, then the other freed him. In this case, he freed him first, then the other made him mudabbar. The difference between their rulings is that in the first, the mudabbar-owner may demand the value from the manumitter, or he may free him, or he may seek earning. Here, the mudabbar-owner may not demand the value from the manumitter; rather his choice is between seeking earning and freeing, because the mudabbar-owner previously had the choices of demanding value, freeing, and seeking earning. When he made him mudabbar later, his option to demand value ceases, and the options of freeing and seeking earning remain. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the second tadbir is invalid, because emancipation is indivisible according to them, so he is completely freed, and thus the tadbir did not meet ownership, and the manumitter guarantees its value if he is wealthy, because this is the guarantee of emancipation, so it differs between wealth and poverty. (Takmila with addition from the margin)
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states a ruling on a jointly owned slave. When one partner makes the slave mudabbar (declared to be freed upon the owner's death), and the other partner then sets him free immediately, the mudabbar-owner has the right to claim half the slave's value from the manumitter. This is because the emancipation occurred while the slave was mudabbar, so the mudabbar-owner is entitled to compensation equivalent to his share. The commentary from Fath al-Qadir explains that the slave's value at that point is two-thirds of his free-market value, as a mudabbar's benefits are distributed over use, emancipation, and other aspects. The main point is the reversal of events: when tadbir precedes itq, the mudabbar-owner can claim value, free the slave, or seek earnings (istis'a). However, when itq precedes tadbir, the mudabbar-owner cannot claim value; he can only free or seek earnings. This distinction is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. His two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, hold that the second tadbir is entirely invalid because emancipation is indivisible; thus the slave is fully freed, and the manumitter must pay the slave's full value if he is wealthy, since it is a guarantee of emancipation.

Key Terms
التدبير (al-tadbir): Declaring that a slave will be freed upon the owner's death, making the slave a mudabbar.
الضمان (al-daman): Guarantee or financial liability for the value of a slave in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where one partner frees a slave first, and the other later makes him mudabbar, what option does the mudabbar-owner have according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) He can demand half the slave's value from the manumitter.
B) He can free the slave or seek earnings, but not demand value.
C) He can demand the full value from the manumitter if wealthy.
D) He has no options; the tadbir is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The sequence of tadbir and itq determines the mudabbar-owner's remedies; when itq precedes tadbir, Abu Hanifa holds the option to claim value is lost, but the Sahibayn deem the second tadbir invalid.

The Mukatab's Incapacity: Three-Day Grace Period and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on a mukatab's incapacity with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the declaration of a mukatab's incapacity after a missed installment, explain the three-day grace period, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute between the Sahibayn (three-day wait) and Abu Yusuf (two stars).

Core Idea
A mukatab who misses a payment is given three days to receive expected wealth before his contract is rescinded.

When a mukatab (a slave who has contracted to earn his freedom) fails to pay an installment (najm), the law balances his interest and the master's. The primary rule from the matn requires the qadi to wait three days if the mukatab has wealth expected to arrive; otherwise, the kitaba is rescinded. However, there is a known disagreement within the Hanafi school: Abu Yusuf held that two consecutive missed stars are required, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf in his majority view with Muhammad) maintain the three-day rule. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proofs, and the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling from the matn
Read the matn carefully: it speaks of a mukatab who is 'ajiz (incapable) of paying a star, but who has wealth that will reach him. The qadi does not declare him incapable for three days; otherwise he declares him incapable and rescinds the kitaba.
Note that 'wealth that will reach him' means money owed by others or assets expected within three days.
2
Analyze the condition: expected wealth vs. no wealth
If the mukatab has expected wealth, the qadi must wait three days. If he has no such wealth, the qadi declares him incapable immediately at the master's request (or the master may rescind with consent).
The three-day period is a fixed legal standard for granting excuses, like the period given to a debtor to settle.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
The matn's ruling is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn). However, a separate narration from Abu Yusuf holds that the qadi should not declare incapacity until two consecutive stars are missed.
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf (dispute within the school), not a conflict with an outside madhhab.
4
Examine the proofs for each position
The Sahibayn cite the practice of Umar (RA) who rescinded a kitaba for a single missed star. Abu Yusuf cites the hadith of Ali (RA): 'When two consecutive stars follow for the mukatab, he returns to slavery.'
The Hanafi response is that Ali's hadith does not negate rescission for one star; it is silent. Umar's explicit action is stronger evidence.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the three-day wait as stated in the matn. This is the view of the Sahibayn and is the established ruling in the school.
The dispute shows that even within the school, imams can differ, but the later practice settled on the three-day rule.

بل هو خاص بما إذا كاتبه وحده قال في "المحيط" : ولو كاتب عبدين كتابة واحدة، فعجز أحدهما، فرده القاضي إلى الرق، والقاضي لا يعلم بمكاتبة الآخر، معه ثم أدى الآخر بدل الكتابة، عتقا جميعا؛ لأنه لم يصح ردّ الأول في الرق ما دام الآخر قادرا على أداء بدل الكتابة، ولهذا لو علم القاضي بكتابة الآخر لا يرد حتى يجتمعا تكملة البحر الرائق: ۱۱۸/۸] أو سيده إلخ: أي يفسخ الكتابة مولى العبد برضاه وهذا يفيد أن الكتابة لازمة من جانب المولى، غير لازمة من جانب العبد، فلو أراد العبد أن يعجز نفسه ويفسخ الكتابة وأبى المولى ذلك، فللعبد ذلك في الرواية الصحيحة، والرواية الثانية: أنها لازمة من جانب العبد أيضا تكملة البحر الرائق: ۱۱۹/۸] وعاد إلخ: يعني إذا عجز عاد إلى أحكام الرق؛ لأن الكتابة قد انفسخت، وفك الحجر كان لأجل عقد الكتابة، فلا يبقى بدون العقد، ولا يخفى أن المؤلف قال: "عاد أحكام الرق" ولم يقل عاد إلى الرق؛ لأنه كان باقيا فيه. [ تكملة البحر الرائق: ١١٩/٨]
Chapter on the death of the mukatab, his incapacity, and the death of the master regarding payment of the kitaba. A mukatab who is incapable of paying a star, and he has wealth that will reach him, the qadi does not declare him incapable for three days; otherwise he declares him incapable. That is, a monthly installment, for example, for the mukatab will reach him. And he rescinds it (the kitaba) or his master by his consent, and the rulings of slavery return. That is, the kitaba is rescinded by the qadi or the master. The slave is [declared incapable] immediately but he gives him time. The chapter on death of the mukatab etc. is in explanation of the rulings of death of the mukatab etc. Delaying the chapter on rulings of these matters is clearly appropriate, because these matters come after the contract of kitaba. So likewise their explanation. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/118) 'The qadi does not declare him incapable etc.': That is, if the mukatab is incapable of paying an installment from installments, and he has wealth that will reach him, such as having some remaining transactions with people, the qadi does not declare him incapable for three days, considering both sides. The three days are the period set for granting excuses, like giving the opponent time to pay and the debtor time to settle. So no increase is made. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2/118) 'Otherwise he declares him incapable etc.': That is, if he has no wealth that will reach him within three days, the qadi rescinds the kitaba if the master requests its rescission, or the master rescinds with the mukatab's consent. This is according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: He does not declare him incapable until two stars follow consecutively, because of the saying of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): 'When two stars follow consecutively for the mukatab, he returns to slavery.' And matters that are not grasped by analogy are based on reports. Also because it is a contract of kindness, so even the deferment in it is a year. Their proof is what was reported from Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that he rescinded it due to the mukatab's incapacity to pay a star and returned him to slavery, and this report is like a marfu' hadith. What was reported from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) does not negate rescission if he is incapable of one star; rather it is silent about it. The meaning of 'he rescinds it' is that the qadi judges his incapacity, because it is obligatory when the master requests and he has authority for that even if the slave does not consent. So judgment is necessary, like the return due to a defect. The apparent meaning of 'a mukatab incapable of a star' includes whether he made a kitaba alone or with others, but it is not so; rather it is specific to when he made a kitaba alone. In al-Muhit: If he made a kitaba with two slaves jointly, and one became incapable, and the qadi returned him to slavery, and the qadi does not know about the kitaba of the other with him, then the other pays the kitaba, both become free, because the return of the first to slavery was not valid as long as the other is capable of paying the kitaba. Thus if the qadi knew about the kitaba of the other, he would not return him until they both are [incapable]. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/118) 'Or his master etc.': That is, the master of the slave rescinds the kitaba by his consent. This indicates that the kitaba is binding on the master's side, not binding on the slave's side. So if the slave wants to declare himself incapable and rescind the kitaba, and the master refuses that, the slave may do so according to the correct narration. The second narration: it is binding on the slave's side as well. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/119) 'And the rulings of slavery return': That is, when he becomes incapable, he returns to the rulings of slavery, because the kitaba has been rescinded. The removal of restrictions was for the sake of the kitaba contract, so it does not remain without the contract. It is not hidden that the author said 'returned to the rulings of slavery' and did not say 'returned to slavery' because he remained in it. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/119)
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on the mukatab's death, incapacity, and the master's death. It first presents the ruling from the matn: if a mukatab fails to pay an installment but has wealth expected to arrive, the qadi should give him a three-day grace period before declaring him incapable. If no wealth is expected, the qadi rescinds the kitaba contract at the master's request, or the master may rescind with the mukatab's consent. The commentary from Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the rationale: three days is the standard period for granting excuses in legal matters. It then notes that this ruling is according to the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). However, Abu Yusuf is reported to have a separate view: he would not declare the mukatab incapable until two consecutive stars (installments) are missed, citing a hadith from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him). The text then discusses the proofs: the Sahibayn rely on a report from Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that he rescinded the kitaba upon failure of one star. It also clarifies that the ruling applies when the mukatab is alone in the contract; if he is jointly contracted with another slave, the qadi cannot rescind partially until both are incapable. The passage further explains that the kitaba contract is binding on the master but not on the slave—the slave has the right to declare himself incapable even against the master's will, according to the correct narration. Finally, the phrase 'return to the rulings of slavery' is precise: the slave was always a slave, but his restrictions were lifted; upon incapacity, those restrictions return.

Key Terms
المكاتب (al-mukatab): A slave who has entered into a kitaba contract to earn his freedom by paying installments to the master.
النجم (al-najm): An installment or a portion of the kitaba payment due at a specified time.
العجز (al-`ajz): Incapacity; in this context, the inability to pay a star when due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A mukatab fails to pay an installment. The qadi determines he has wealth expected to arrive in two days. According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what should the qadi do?
A) Immediately declare the mukatab incapable because one missed star is sufficient.
B) Wait three days; if the wealth does not arrive, then declare incapacity.
C) Wait until two stars are missed, as per Abu Yusuf's individual narration.
D) Rescind the kitaba only if the master consents to the delay.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi ruling is that a mukatab who misses a single star is given a three-day grace period if he has expected wealth; otherwise the kitaba is rescinded immediately upon the master's request, and this is the operative position despite Abu Yusuf's individual view requiring two stars.

Rulings on the Mukatab's Inability and Death
Explains rulings when mukatab fails to pay or dies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the mukatab's inability to pay and his death, and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, and between the Hanafi and Shafi'i views.

Core Idea
The kitaba contract is a mu'awada (exchange) that survives death and only dissolves upon verified inability.

The kitaba contract creates a unique legal status: the mukatab is part-free, part-slave. When he fails to pay or dies, complex questions arise: does the contract dissolve? Who gets his property? What about his children? This lesson examines the Hanafi answers, grounded in the analogy to sale and reports from Umar and Ali.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage covers two main scenarios: the mukatab's inability to pay an installment, and the mukatab's death. Identify which part of the text deals with each.
Inability is discussed first, death second.
2
State the majority Hanafi ruling for inability
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if the mukatab misses one installment and has no funds expected within three days, the judge cancels the kitaba at the master's request. The three-day grace period is for cases where funds are due.
3
Note Abu Yusuf's dissent
Abu Yusuf requires two consecutive missed installments before cancellation, citing a report from Ali. The Hanafi majority responds that the report from Umar supports immediate cancellation, and Ali's report does not negate it.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.
4
State the Hanafi ruling for death
If the mukatab dies leaving enough assets to pay the kitaba, the contract is not dissolved. The kitaba is paid from the estate, and the mukatab is deemed free at the last moment of life, freeing his children born during the kitaba.
This is based on Ibn Mas'ud's view, analogizing kitaba to a sale.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i view
Imam al-Shafi'i, following Zayd ibn Thabit, holds that the kitaba dissolves upon death because the purpose (freedom through payment) becomes impossible. The Hanafi response emphasizes the contract's nature as mu'awada and the benefit to children.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is the status of the children.

Source Text

باب موت المكاتب وعجزه وموت المولى
مكاتب عجز عن نجم، وله مال سيصل لم يعجزه الحاكم إلى ثلاثة أيام، وإلا عجزه، أي قسط شهر مثلا للمكاتب إليه وفسخها، أو سيده برضاه، وعاد أحكام الرق، أي الكتابة الحاكم عليه العبد في الحال بل يمهله كان باب موت المكاتب إلخ في بيان أحكام موت المكاتب ألخ تأخير باب أحكام هذه الأشياء ظاهر التناسب؛ لأن هذه الأشياء متأخرة عن عقد الكتابة، فكذا بيان أحكامها تكملة البحر الرائق: ١١٨/٨] لم يعجزه الحاكم إلخ: أي إذا عجز المكاتب أداء قسط عن أقساط وله مال سيصل إليه بأن يكون له عند من الناس شيء من بقية المعاملات لم يعجزه الحاكم ثلاثة أيام نظرا للجانبين، والثلاثة هي المدة التي ضربت لإمهال الأعذار كإمهال الخصم للدفع والمديون للقضاء، فلا يزاد عليه تكملة البحر الرائق: ١١٨/٢] وإلا عجزه إلخ : يعني إذا لم يكن له مال سيصل إليه في ثلاثة أيام فسخ الحاكم الكتابة إذا طلب المولى فسخها، أو فسخها المولى برضاء المكاتب، وهذا عندهما، وقال أبو يوسف لا يعجزه حتى يتوالى عليه نجمان؛ لقول علي ه: "إذا توالى على المكاتب نجمان يرد في الرق، والأمر فيما لا يدرك بالقياس كالخبر، ولأنه عقد إرفاق حتى التأجيل فيه سنة ولهما ما روي عن عمر الله أنه فسخها بعجز المكاتب عن نجم ورده إلى الرق، والأثر فيه كالمرفوع، وما رواه عن علي الله لا ينفي الفسخ إذا عجز عن نجم، بل هو مسكوت عنه. والمراد بقوله: "فسخها" يعني يحكم الحاكم بعجزه؛ لأنه واجب عند طلب المولى وله ولاية ذلك وإن لم يرض العبد، فلابد من القضاء كالرد بالعيب وظاهر قوله مكاتب" عجز عن نجم" صادق بما إذا كاتبه وحده أو مع غيره، وليس كذلك بل هو خاص بما إذا كاتبه وحده قال في "المحيط" : ولو كاتب عبدين كتابة واحدة، فعجز أحدهما، فرده القاضي إلى الرق، والقاضي لا يعلم بمكاتبة الآخر ،معه ثم أدى الآخر بدل الكتابة، عتقا جميعا؛ لأنه لم يصح ردّ الأول في الرق ما دام الآخر قادرا على أداء بدل الكتابة، ولهذا لو علم القاضي بكتابة الآخر لا يرد حتى يجتمعا تكملة البحر الرائق: ١١٨/٨] أو سيده إلخ: أي يفسخ الكتابة مولى العبد برضاه وهذا يفيد أن الكتابة لازمة من جانب المولى، غير لازمة من جانب العبد، فلو أراد العبد أن يعجز نفسه ويفسخ الكتابة وأبى المولى ذلك، فللعبد ذلك في الرواية الصحيحة، والرواية الثانية: أنها لازمة من جانب العبد أيضا تكملة البحر الرائق: ١١٩/٨]
وعاد إلخ: يعني إذا عجز عاد إلى أحكام الرق؛ لأن الكتابة قد انفسخت، وفك الحجر كان لأجل عقد الكتابة، فلا يبقى بدون العقد، ولا يخفى أن المؤلف قال: "عاد أحكام الرق" ولم يقل عاد إلى الرق؛ لأنه كان باقيا فيه. [ تكملة البحر الرائق: ١١٩/٨]

وما في يده لسيده وإن مات وله مال لم تفسخ، وتؤدّى كتابته لأن كسب عبده العبد والحال أنه الكتابة بعتقه في آخر حياته، وإن ترك ولدا ولد في كتابته .
أي بعتق المكاتب جزء من أجزاء حياته المكاتب موصوف صفته أي بدل الكتابة من ماله، وحكم أي مال المكاتب
وما في يده أي المكاتب الذي عجز لسيده إلخ لأنه ظهر أنه كسب عبده إذا كان المال بين أن يكون للعبد إذا أدى الكتابة وبين أن يكون للمولى إذا عجز وقد تحقق العجز ، فكان لمولاه تكملة البحر الرائق: ١١٩/٨] وإن مات إلخ يعني لا تفسخ الكتابة بموت العبد إذا كان له مال يؤدى بدل الكتابة منه، وهذا قول ابن مسعود لله، وبه أخذ علماؤنا، وقال زيد بن ثابت ه: تنفسخ بموته، وبه أخذ الإمام الشافعي، له: أن العقد لو بقي لبقي لتحصيل العتق بالأداء، وقد تعذر إثباته فبطل، بخلاف موت المولى؛ لأنه ليس بمعقود عليه بل عاقد، والعقد يبطل بموت المعقود عليه لا يموت العاقد ؛ ولأن المولى يصلح أن يكون معتقا بعد الموت، بخلاف العبد فإنه لا يثبت له العتق بعد الموت لنا: أن الكتابة عقد معاوضة لا تنفسخ بموت أحد المتعاقدين، وهو المولى، فلا تنفسخ بموت الآخر، وهو العبد كالبيع؛ لأن قضية المعاوضة المساواة، فإذا بقي العقد بعد موت المولى لحاجته إلى الولاء وغيره، جاز أن يبقى بعد موت العبد لحاجته إلى الحرية ليتوصل إلى حرية أولاده، ولو مات عاجزا تفسخ الكتابة تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٢٠/٨] وتؤدى كتابته إلخ أي يؤدى بدل الكتابة من مال المكاتب الذي مات وترك مالا، ويكون أداء الخليفة كأدائه بنفسه، وفي "الأصل": إذا مات المكاتب عن وفاء، وعليه ديون لأجنبي سوى بدل الكتابة وله مال يوفى، وله وصايا، من تركته بدين الأجنبي، ثم بدل الكتابة، وتبطل وصاياه، وما بقي يقسم بين ورثته، وإن لم يبق بعد قضاء الدين شيء، يبدأ ببدل الكتابة ولا يبدأ بالدين، وإن لم يترك مالا إلا دينا على الناس، فاستسعى المولود في الكتابة فعجز يرد في الرق، فإذا خرج الدين بعد ذلك، فذلك للمولى تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٢٠/٨] وحكم بعتقه إلخ : أي حكم بعتق المكاتب في آخر جزء من أجزاء حياته بأن يقام الترك الموجود منه في آخر حياته مقام التخلية بين المال والمولى، وهو الأداء المستحق عليه، وما بقي فهو لورثته تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٢٠/٨] قول الجمهور، وذهب بعضهم إلى أنه يعتق بعد الموت بأن يقدر حيا قابلا للعتق كما قدر المولى حيا مالكا معتقا كذا في "الكافي". واعلم أن سياق قول المصنف : وإن مات وله مال إلخ" يقتضي أنه لا يحكم له بالعتق قبل الأداء، وكذا في "الحموي" من "البناية" و"الاختيار"، وقال في "الينابيع": إنه يعتق قبل موته، ولا يتوقف على الأداء. (فتح الله المعين) وإن ترك ولدا إلخ يعني إذا مات المكاتب وترك ولدا ولد في الكتابة لا قبلها، ولم يترك مالا يفي ببدل الكتابة، سعى الولد في كتابته على نجومه كسعي أبيه لو كان حيا؛ لأن المولود في الكتابة يتكاتب تبعا لأبيه، وكان التأجيل ثابتا لأبيه، فلا يسقط التأجيل بموته، بخلاف الحر إذا مات وعليه دين مؤجل، يحل؛ لأن حق التأجيل لم يثبت للوارث.
يبدأ
قوله: "حكم" "بعتقه" يعني إذا أدى الولد بدل الكتابة حكم بعتقه؛ لأنه داخل في كتابته، وكسبه ككسبه، فيخلفه
Chapter of the mukatab's death and his inability and the death of the master. A mukatab who fails to pay an installment, and he has wealth that will come to him, the judge does not declare his inability for up to three days; otherwise, he declares his inability and cancels [the kitaba], or his master [cancels] with his consent, and the rulings of slavery return... And what is in his hand belongs to his master. And if he dies and has wealth, it is not cancelled, and his kitaba is paid from it, and it is ruled that he is freed in the last part of his life. And if he leaves a child born during his kitaba...
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, with commentary from Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, covers rulings on the mukatab's inability to pay and his death. It begins with the scenario of inability: if a mukatab misses an installment but has funds due to arrive, the judge gives him a three-day grace period. If no funds are expected, the judge cancels the kitaba at the master's request, or the master cancels with the mukatab's consent. This is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two). Abu Yusuf holds that cancellation requires two consecutive missed installments, citing a report from Ali. The Hanafi response is that the report from Umar supports immediate cancellation, and the report from Ali does not negate it. The passage also discusses that the kitaba is binding on the master but not on the servant, so the servant can cancel at will. Regarding death: if the mukatab dies with sufficient assets to pay the kitaba, the contract is not dissolved; rather, the kitaba is paid from his estate, and he is deemed free in the last moment of life, allowing his children to be free. This is based on the view of Ibn Mas'ud, contrary to Zayd ibn Thabit and al-Shafi'i who hold that death dissolves the contract. The Hanafi argument analogizes the kitaba to a contract of exchange (like sale) which does not dissolve by the death of either party. If the deceased mukatab leaves a child born during the kitaba and insufficient assets, that child must continue working to pay the installments, as the child is included in the father's kitaba. The child's earnings become like the father's earnings, and upon full payment, the child is also freed.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a kitaba contract with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
كتابة (kitaba): A contract whereby a master agrees to free his slave upon payment of a specified sum in installments.
نجم (najm): An installment payment due under the kitaba contract.
عجز ('ajz): Inability of the mukatab to pay an installment when due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position, when can a judge cancel a mukatab's kitaba due to inability to pay an installment?
A) Only after two consecutive missed installments.
B) Immediately upon missing one installment, if no funds are expected within three days.
C) Only if the mukatab admits inability.
D) Never; cancellation is only by mutual consent.

Key Takeaway
The kitaba contract is resilient: it is not dissolved by death if assets exist, and cancellation requires verified inability with a three-day grace for expected funds.

Children of the Mukatab: Born vs. Purchased
Rulings on the mukatab's child born during kitaba and the purchased child.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the child born during a mukatab's kitaba and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on the purchased child, applying qiyas reasoning.

Core Idea
The born child continues the kitaba; the purchased child does not—Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn on deferment.

When a mukatab dies leaving a child, the child's status depends on whether he was born during the kitaba or purchased during it. The Hanafi school has clear rules for the born child, but a dispute arises regarding the purchased child. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Note the two types of children: born during kitaba (mawlud fi al-kitaba) and purchased during kitaba (walad mushtara). Recognize that the ruling differs.
The born child is a dependent mukatab; the purchased child was not part of the original contract.
2
Analyze the ruling for the born child
The born child continues the father's kitaba on the same installments. Understand why the deferment survives the father's death: it was established for the father and passes to the dependent child.
Contrast with a free person's deferred debt which becomes due upon death.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the purchased child
Abu Hanifa holds that the purchased child must pay the entire kitaba immediately or be enslaved. The Sahibayn hold that he can pay in installments like the born child. Identify the basis of each view.
Abu Hanifa: deferment is specific to the contract; Sahibayn: purchase makes him a mukatab.
4
Trace the qiyas argument
Use the qiyas panel: the born child is the asl (with deferment), the purchased child is the far. The illa is whether the child entered the original contract. Abu Hanifa says no; Sahibayn say yes via purchase.
The commentary defends Abu Hanifa by distinguishing between entering for connection vs. extension.
5
Apply the inheritance rules
The child inherits if both become free simultaneously (e.g., born child or both in one kitaba). A child with a separate kitaba does not inherit because his freedom is later.
Slavery prevents inheritance at the moment of the father's death.
