وإن ترك ولدا ولد في كتابته ولم يترك مالا يفي ببدل الكتابة، سعى الولد في كتابته على نجومه كسعي أبيه لو كان حيا؛ لأن المولود في الكتابة يتكاتب تبعا لأبيه، وكان التأجيل ثابتا لأبيه، فلا يسقط التأجيل بموته، بخلاف الحر إذا مات وعليه دين مؤجل، يحل؛ لأن حق التأجيل لم يثبت للوارث. فإذا أدى الولد بدل الكتابة حكم بعتقه؛ لأنه داخل في كتابته، وكسبه ككسبه، فيخلفه. وحكم بعتق أبيه في آخر جزء من أجزاء حياته. ولو ترك ولدا مشترى عجل البدل حالا أو ردّ رقيقا. وهذا عند الإمام وعندهما يسعى على نجومه كالمولود في الكتابة؛ لأنه صار بمنزلة المكاتب حتى جاز للمولى إعتاقه كما يجوز إعتاق المكاتب بنفسه، بخلاف سائر أكساب المكاتب، فإنه لا يملك إعتاقه. وللإمام أن الأجل يثبت بالشرط في العقد، فيثبت في حق من دخل تحت الكتابة والمشترى لم يدخل تحت العقد؛ لأنه لم يضف إليه العقد، ولم يسر حكمه إليه؛ لكونه منفصلا وقت الكتابة. وأورد عليه أنه قد المكاتب إذا اشترى أباه أو ابنه دخل في كتابته، وأيضا لو لم يسر حكمه إليه لما عتق عند الإمام بأداء بدل الكتابة حالا، وأجيب أن المراد بدخول الولد المشترى في كتابة أبيه ليس لسراية حكم العقد الذي جرى بين المكاتب ومولاه إليهم، بل يجعل المكاتب مكاتبا لولده باشترائه تحقيقا للصلة وبأن عتق الولد المشترى عنده بأداء بدل الكتابة حالا ليس لأجل السراية أيضا، بل لضرورة المكاتب إذ ذاك بمنزلة من مات عن وفاء، بخلاف المولود في الكتابة؛ لأنه . مائه في الكتابة. ورثه ابنه أي يرث الابن من المكاتب في صورة اشترى المكاتب ابنه وترك وفاء أي مالا ومات؛ لأنه لما أدى بدل الكتابة حكم بعتقه في آخر جزء من أجزاء حياته فيتبعه ولده في ذلك، فيكونان حرين، فظهر أنه مات حرا عن ولد حر. وكذا لو كان هو وابنه مكاتبين كتابة واحدة؛ لأن الولد إن كان صغيرا فهو تبع لأبيه، وإن كان كبيرا جعلا كشخص واحد، فإذا حكم بعتق أحدهما في وقت، حكم بعتق الآخر في ذلك الوقت ضرورة اتحاد الوقت فيصير المكاتب حرا مات عن ابن حر. وأما إذا كان الابن مكاتبا بعقد على حدة، لم يرث الابن منه شيئا؛ لأنه لا يعتق بعتق أبيه، بل يعتق بأدائه فيتأخر عتقه عن أبيه، فلا يرث؛ لأن الرق مانع من فيء الإرث كالكفر، وإن أدى الابن قبل أداء أبيه، فلا مانع من إرثه منه حينئذ.
If he leaves a child born during his kitaba and does not leave property sufficient for the kitaba payment, the child strives/stives in his kitaba on his installments as his father would have strived if he were alive. Because the child born during the kitaba becomes a mukatab in subordination to his father, and the term was established for his father, so the term is not dropped by his death, unlike a free person who dies with a deferred debt which becomes due, because the right of deferment was not established for the heir. When the child pays the kitaba payment, he is judged to be free, because he is included in his kitaba, and his earning is like his earning, so he succeeds him. And the ruling of the father's emancipation in the last part of his life. If he leaves a purchased child, he must pay the payment immediately or be returned as a slave. This is according to the Imam, while according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he strives on his installments like the child born in the kitaba, because he has become like a mukatab such that it is permissible for the master to emancipate him just as it is permissible to emancipate a mukatab himself, unlike other earnings of the mukatab, for he does not own their emancipation. For the Imam (Abu Hanifa): the deferment is established by the condition in the contract, so it is established in favor of one who enters under the kitaba, and the purchased child did not enter under the contract because the contract was not attributed to him, nor did its ruling extend to him due to his being separate at the time of the kitaba. It was objected that if the mukatab buys his father or son, he enters into his kitaba, and also if its ruling did not extend to him, he would not be free according to the Imam by paying the kitaba payment immediately. It is answered that the meaning of the purchased child entering into the kitaba of his father is not by the extension of the contract between the mukatab and his master to them, rather the mukatab is made a mukatab for his child by purchasing him for the realization of connection, and that the emancipation of the purchased child according to him by paying the kitaba payment immediately is not for the sake of extension either, but for the necessity of the mukatab being like one who died with sufficient funds, unlike the child born in the kitaba because of his [..] in the kitaba. His son inherits from him, meaning the son inherits from the mukatab in the case where the mukatab bought his son and left sufficient funds (i.e., property) and died; because when he paid the kitaba payment, he was judged to be free in the last part of his life, so his son follows him in that, and both become free, so it becomes clear that he died free leaving a free son. Similarly, if he and his son were both mukatabs in one kitaba, because if the son is young he is subordinate to his father, and if he is adult they are considered as one person. So if the emancipation of one is ruled at a time, the emancipation of the other is ruled at that time necessarily due to the unity of time, so the mukatab becomes free dying leaving a free son. But if the son is a mukatab by a separate contract, he does not inherit anything from him because he is not freed by the emancipation of his father; rather, he is freed by his own payment, so his freedom is after his father's freedom, so he does not inherit because slavery prevents inheritance as does disbelief. If the son pays before his father's payment, then there is no obstacle to his inheritance from him at that time.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage provides detailed rulings on the children of a mukatab. The first scenario is when the mukatab dies leaving a child born during the kitaba (not before) and insufficient property. The child continues the kitaba on the same installments as his father, because he is a dependent mukatab and the deferred term remains. This is contrasted with a free person whose deferred debts become due upon death. When the child completes payment, both he and his father are deemed free (the father at the last moment of his life). The second scenario is when the mukatab leaves a purchased child (whom he bought during the kitaba). Here Abu Hanifa holds that the child must pay the entire kitaba immediately or be returned to slavery, because he did not enter the original kitaba contract. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he can pay in installments like the born child, because he becomes like a mukatab through purchase. The argument involves whether the contract's term extends to the purchased child. Abu Hanifa's view is that the term is specific to the contract, so the purchased child, being separate at the time of the contract, does not benefit from the deferment. An objection is raised about a purchased father or son entering the kitaba, and the response distinguishes between entering for connection and for extension. The passage then discusses inheritance: if the mukatab bought his son and dies with sufficient property, the son inherits from him because both are freed simultaneously (the father at death, the son by payment). Similarly, if both are mukatabs in one contract, they share the same time of freedom, so inheritance occurs. But if the son is a separate mukatab, he does not inherit because his freedom is later, and during the father's death he was still a slave, which prevents inheritance. However, if the son pays first, he becomes free earlier and can inherit from the father.

Key Terms
مولود في الكتابة (mawlud fi al-kitaba): A child born during the period of a mukatab's kitaba contract.
ولد مشترى (walad mushtara): A child purchased by the mukatab during his kitaba.
سعى (sa'a): To strive or work to earn and pay the kitaba installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He continues his father's kitaba on installments.
B) He must pay the entire kitaba immediately or be enslaved.
C) He is automatically free.
D) He is returned to slavery without any payment option.

Key Takeaway
The mukatab's born child continues his kitaba; the purchased child does not and must pay immediately per Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn differ.

Mukatab After Master's Death: Payment and Manumission by Heirs
Explains rulings on payment to heirs and manumission by heirs after master's death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three rulings for a mukatab after the master's death and explain the istihsan reasoning that allows manumission by all heirs in one sitting.

Core Idea
When all heirs free a mukatab in one sitting, he becomes free immediately—istihsan overrides qiyas.

This passage from Takmilah al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the rulings concerning a mukatab (a slave under a manumission contract) after the death of his master. It clarifies three key situations: continued payment to heirs, manumission by all heirs, and manumission by some heirs. The central legal issue is whether the heirs, who inherit only the right to receive payments, can free the slave. The Hanafi school employs istihsan (juristic preference) to allow manumission by all heirs, treating it as an implicit release of the debt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
List the three rulings given in the text: (1) mukatab continues paying installments to heirs; (2) if all heirs free him in one sitting, he becomes free without payment; (3) if only some heirs free him, the freeing is ineffective.
These are the legal consequences (ahkam) for each situation.
2
Understand the qiyas argument
By strict analogy (qiyas), the mukatab should not become free when heirs free him because the heirs do not own the mukatab—they only inherited the right to receive the kitaba payments. Ownership is the illa (effective cause) for valid manumission.
Qiyas would deny freedom in both scenario 2 and 3.
3
Understand the istihsan reasoning
Istihsan overrides qiyas in scenario 2: the freeing by all heirs is treated as an implicit release (ibra) of the debt, because the heirs collectively own the right to the payments. Their act of freeing is construed as forgiving the debt, thus discharging the mukatab's liability.
This is a Hanafi application of istihsan based on underlying rationale (ma'na).
4
Note the condition and the minority view
The freeing must occur in a single sitting. There is a reported opinion (qila) that if heirs free separately, the mukatab becomes free as long as the first has not revoked, but the main position requires a single sitting. Partial freeing by some heirs is entirely ineffective.
The condition of a single sitting prevents piecemeal release.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويؤدي المال إلى ورثته على نجومه، وإن حرّروه عتق مجانا، وإن حرر البعض لم ينفذ
المكاتب
عتقه.
أي ورثة سيده
أي الورثة المكاتب
أي بعض الورثة
ويؤدي المال إلخ : يعني يؤدي المكاتب المال بعد موت المولى إلى الورثة على نجومه المقررة، وليس للورثة إسقاط الأجل، والمطالبة في الحال؛ لأن النجوم حق المكاتب؛ لأنها أجل وهو حق المطلوب، فلا يبطل بموت الطالب، هذا إذا كاتبه وهو صحيح، ولو كاتبه وهو مريض لا يصح تأجيله إلا من الثلث فيؤدي ثلثي البدل حالا والباقي على نجومه وقد ذكرناه تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٢٦/٨]
وإن حرروه إلخ يعني إن حرر جميع الورثة المكاتب عتق مجانا بلا بدل والقياس أنه لا يعتق؛ لأنهم لم يملكوه، وجه الاستحسان : أنه يجعل إبراء عن بدل الكتابة فإنه حقهم، وقد جرى فيه الإرث، فيكون الإعتاق منهم إبراء اقتضاءا أو إقرارا بالاستيفاء منه فتبرأ ذمته كما إذا أبرأه المولى عن بدل الكتابة كله، ويشترط أن يعتقوه في مجلس واحد حتى لو أعتقوه متفرقا لم يعتق، وقيل: يعتق إذا أعتقه الباقون ما لم يرجع الأول. تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٢٦/٨]
لم ينفذ عتقه إلخ: يعني إن حرر المكاتب بعض الورثة لم ينفذ إعتاقه؛ لأنه لم يملكه، ولا عتق فيما لا يملك، ولا يمكن أن يجعل إبراء ولا إقرارا بالاستيفاء كما يجعل في الصورة الأولى؛ لأن إبراء البعض واستيفاؤه لا يوجب عتقه؛ لتعذر ثبوت العتق من جهته فيبطل المقتضي وهو الإعتاق ولا يبرأ من الدين أيضا؛ لأن البراءة لم تثبت إلا اقتضاءا، فإذا بطل المقتضي للإبراء بطل المقتضى أيضا بخلاف إعتاق الجميع.
And he (the mukatab) pays the money to his (the master's) heirs according to his (the mukatab's) installments. And if they (the heirs) free him, he becomes free gratuitously. And if some of them free him, his manumission does not take effect. (Explanation: He pays the money after the master's death to the heirs according to his fixed installments. The heirs may not drop the term and demand immediately because the installments are the right of the mukatab; they are a term and it is the right of the one obligated, so it is not voided by the death of the claimant. This is if he made the kitaba while healthy. If he made it while sick, the deferment is only valid from one-third, so he pays two-thirds of the price immediately and the rest on his installments. And if all the heirs free him, he becomes free gratuitously without payment. By analogy he would not become free because they (the heirs) do not own him. The basis of istihsan: that it is made an ibra (release) from the kitaba price because it is their right, and inheritance has occurred in it, so their freeing becomes an ibra by implication or an acknowledgment of receipt from him, so his liability becomes discharged, just as if the master had released him from the entire kitaba price. And it is required that they free him in one sitting; if they free him separately he does not become free. And it is said: he becomes free if the rest free him as long as the first has not revoked. And if some of the heirs free him, his manumission does not take effect because he does not own him, and there is no freeing in what one does not own. And it cannot be made an ibra or acknowledgment of receipt as in the first case because the ibra of some and his receipt does not necessitate his freedom, because establishing freedom from his side is impossible, so the effective cause (the freeing) is void, and he is not released from the debt either because the release was only established by implication; so when the effective cause for the release is void, the effect is also void, unlike the freeing by all.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with three scenarios concerning a mukatab (a slave who has contracted with his master to earn his freedom by paying installments) after the master's death. First, the mukatab continues to pay the remaining installments to the master's heirs according to the original schedule; the heirs cannot demand immediate payment because the installment schedule is a right of the mukatab. An exception is if the master was terminally ill when making the contract—then deferment is only valid up to one-third of his estate, so two-thirds must be paid immediately. Second, if all the heirs collectively free the mukatab, he becomes free without any further payment. This is based on istihsan (juristic preference): although by strict analogy the heirs do not own the mukatab (they inherited only the right to receive payments), their act of freeing is treated as an implicit release (ibra') of the debt, thus discharging the mukatab's liability. However, this requires that all heirs perform the freeing in one sitting; if they do so separately, it is ineffective. Third, if only some of the heirs free the mukatab, the freeing does not take effect at all because the partial heir does not own the mukatab, and the act cannot be construed as a release since a partial release does not achieve freedom. Thus the mukatab remains obligated.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract (kitaba) with his master to earn his freedom by paying a specified sum in installments.
إبراء (ibra'): A legal release from a debt or obligation.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that sets aside a strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable ruling based on custom, necessity, or underlying rationale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mukatab's master dies and all of his heirs free the mukatab in one sitting, what is the ruling?
A) The mukatab must continue paying the remaining installments to the heirs.
B) The mukatab becomes free without any further payment.
C) The mukatab becomes free only if the heirs give a written document.
D) The mukatab remains a slave because the heirs do not own him.

Key Takeaway
A mukatab may become free upon the master's death only if all heirs free him collectively in one sitting; partial freeing is void and strict analogy is overridden by istihsan.

Causes of Wala' and Invalidity of Sa'iba Condition
Ruling on four causes of wala' and voidness of sa'iba condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four causes of wala' and explain why the condition of sa'iba is void according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Wala' is established by four fixed causes; any condition to negate it is void.

In this passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, we encounter a concise statement of the four causes that establish wala' (the right of inheritance through clientage) and a ruling that any condition to negate wala' is void. This ruling is a foundational principle in Hanafi inheritance law. Understanding these causes helps you determine who inherits from a freed slave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four causes of wala'
From the text, list the four causes: tadbir, kitaba, istilad, and milk qarib. These are the only ways wala' is established.
The text also implies that any other form of emancipation also establishes wala'.
2
Understand each cause's operation
For each cause, identify how emancipation occurs: tadbir (freedom after master's death), kitaba (contract for payment), istilad (bearing master's child), milk qarib (owning a close relative).
Tadbir and istilad involve freedom after death; kitaba and milk qarib are immediate.
3
Analyze the sa'iba condition
The condition that a freed slave will not inherit (sa'iba) is void because it contradicts the Shari'a right of wala'.
The text emphasizes that conditions opposing legal rights are null.
4
Note the evidence and ikhtilaf
The hadith 'Women have no wala' except from those they freed' supports that wala' is automatic. Imam Ahmad differs, holding the condition valid.
This cross-madhhab difference is important for understanding the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حق الولاء بتدبير وكتابة واستيلاد وملك قريب، وشرط السائبة لغو. بتدبير : بأن دبر عبده فمات فعتق من ثلث ماله (عيني) وكتابة بأن كاتب عبده وأدى بدل الكتابة فعتق. (عيني) واستيلاد أي الولاء لمن أعتق وإن كان العتق باستيلاد بأن استولد المولى جارية ومات وعتقت من جميع ماله، لكن يرد عليه أن الولاء بالتدبير والاستيلاد كيف يكون للمولى مع أنهما يعتقان بعد موته؟ وأجيب بأنه فيما إذا ارتد المولى ولحق بدار الحرب، حتى حكم بعتق مدبره و أم ولده ثم جاء مسلما فمات مدبره وأم ولده فالولاء له، والأحسن أن يقال: المراد أن ثبوت الولاء لعصبة المولى إنما يكون بسبب ثبوته للمولى فإنه المستحق له، وسبب العتق منه ثم يسري منه إلى عصبته. (فتح بزيادة) وملك قريب بأن ملك ذا رحم محرم منه ] أي الولاء لمن أعتق وإن كان العتق حصل بملك المولى قريبه، بأن ملك أباه أو ابنه بشراء أو هبة أو وصية أو نحو ذلك، فعتق عليه، وذلك لإطلاق الحديث والحاصل أن كلا من التدبير والكتابة والاستيلاد وملك القريب إعتاق يثبت به الولاء والمرأة في جميع ذلك كالرجل؛ لقوله علية: "ليس للنساء . من الولاء إلا ما أعتقن" إلى آخر الحديث. فتح وعيني بزيادة وشرط السائبة إلخ: يعني لو أعتق المولى عبده، وشرط أن لا يرثه كان الشرط لغوا؛ لكونه مخالفا لحكم الشرع فيرثه كما في النسب إذا شرط أن لا يرثه. تكملة البحر الرائق: ۱۳۰/۸] وعند أحمد شرط السائبة صحيح، والسائبة مشتق من ساب أي جرى وذهب كل مذهب والمراد منه العتق بلا ولاء. (عيني تكملة وغيرهما)
Wala' is established by tadbir, kitaba, istilad, and possessing a relative, and the condition of sa'iba is void. Tadbir: that he made his slave a mudabbar and he died and was freed from one-third of his wealth. Kitaba: that he made his slave a mukatib and he paid the kitaba price and was freed. Istilad: meaning wala' is for the one who freed even if the freeing was by istilad, that the master made his slave-woman an umm walad and she died and is freed from his entire wealth. But it is objected: how can wala' be for the master by tadbir and istilad while they are freed after his death? The answer: this is when the master apostatized and joined the dar al-harb, so it was ruled that his mudabbar and umm walad are freed, then he came back Muslim and they died, so wala' is for him. And the best is to say: the meaning is that establishment of wala' for the 'asaba of the master is only due to its establishment for the master, for he is the one entitled to it, and the cause of freeing is from him, then it passes from him to his 'asaba. And possessing a relative: by possessing a mahram relative from him, meaning wala' is for the one who freed even if the freeing occurred by the master possessing his relative, by buying his father or son, or gift, bequest, etc., and he should be freed on him, due to the hadith. The conclusion is that each of tadbir, kitaba, istilad, and possessing a relative is emancipation by which wala' is established. And the woman in all of that is like the man, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Women have no wala' except from those they freed' to the end of the hadith. And the condition of sa'iba: meaning if the master freed his slave and stipulated that he will not inherit from him, the condition is void because it contradicts the ruling of the Shari'a, so he inherits from him as in lineage if he stipulates that he will not inherit. (Mukhtasar from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 130/8) And according to Ahmad, the condition of sa'iba is valid. Sa'iba is derived from 'saba' meaning he ran and went every direction; the intent is emancipation without wala'.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a matn ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq stating the four causes of wala' (the right of inheritance through clientage): tadbir (declaring a slave will be free after the master's death), kitaba (written contract of emancipation for a price), istilad (making a slave-woman an umm walad by bearing her master's child), and milk qarib (owning a close relative such as father or son). The text then rules that if a master frees a slave with a condition that he will not inherit from him (making him a sa'iba), the condition is void. This is because wala' is a legal right established by emancipation, and any condition that negates a legal right is invalid. The commentary explains that wala' in these cases actually accrues to the master's 'asaba after his death, as clarified by later scholars. It also notes that the ruling applies equally to women masters, citing the hadith 'Women have no wala' except from those they freed.' The commentary further mentions the Hanafi position that the condition of sa'iba is void, contrasting with Imam Ahmad's view that it is valid.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): The master declares that a slave will be free after the master's death.
كتابة (kitaba): A contract between master and slave for emancipation upon payment of a sum.
استيلاد (istilad): A slave-woman becomes umm walad by bearing her master's child.
ملك قريب (milk qarib): Owning a close relative (like father or son) who is a slave.
سائبة (sa'iba): A slave freed with the condition that he has no wala' and no inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a condition that the freed slave will not inherit from the master (sa'iba)?
A) Valid, the condition is upheld and the slave does not inherit.
B) Void, the condition is null and inheritance persists.
C) Recommended to avoid.
D) Obligatory to include.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that wala' is established by four causes, and any condition to negate it is void.

Wala' of Child of Freed Pregnant Slave Wife
Ruling on wala' of child when pregnant slave is freed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the wala' of a child born to a freed pregnant slave woman and apply the condition of birth timing to determine whether the wala' can transfer to the father's master.

Core Idea
The wala' transfers to the father's master only if the child is born six months or more after the mother's freeing and the father is freed before the child's death.

The question of who inherits the wala' (patronage) of a child born to a freed slave woman is intricate. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies the Hanafi position, relying on the hadith 'al-wala' liman a'taqa' and analogy to lineage. Understanding the timing of birth and the father's status is key to applying this ruling correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: the wala' of a child when a pregnant slave woman is freed. The ruling distinguishes two scenarios based on the timing of birth relative to the freeing.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith 'al-wala' liman a'taqa' (wala' is for the one who frees) is cited. This establishes that the master who frees the mother gets the child's wala' initially.
This is a zanni al-thubut hadith, but its meaning is considered definitive for this ruling.
3
Distinguish the two birth scenarios
If the child is born less than six months after the freeing, the wala' stays with the mother's master permanently. If born six months or more, the wala' can later transfer to the father's master if the father is freed.
The passage explains that the timing confirms the existence of the pregnancy at the time of freeing.
4
Apply the condition of the father's freedom
For transfer to occur, the father must be freed before the child's death. If freed after, no transfer. This is the 'jarr al-wala'' (drawing of wala').
The analogy with lineage (nasab) is used: wala' is like lineage, and lineage is to the father when possible.
5
Understand the objection and response
An objection that wala' cannot be rescinded is answered: the original wala' is not rescinded; a stronger wala' takes precedence, like a closer relative in inheritance.
This highlights the Hanafi principle of priority, not nullification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القن: المملوك لرجل آخر عتقت وعتق حملها. (عيني) لا ينتقل إلخ : يعني لو أعتق رجل أمة حاملا من زوجها القن المملوك لآخر حال قيام نكاحه وجاءت بالولد لأقل من ستة أشهر لا ينتقل ولاء الحمل عن موالي الأم إلى موالي الأب أبدا؛ لأن الجنين عتق بعتق أمه، وعتق أمه مقصود، فكذا هو يعتق مقصودا؛ لأنه هو جزء الأم، والمولى أوقع الإعتاق على جميع أجزائها مقصودا، والولاء لا ينتقل عن المعتق؛ لقوله عليه: "الولاء لمن أعتق"، وإنما يعرف كون الحمل موجودا عند العتق بأن تلده لأقل من ستة أشهر من وقت العتق ليتيقن وقت العلوق. رمز الحقائق: ٣٠٤/٢] وكذا لو ولدت ولدين أحدهما لأقل من ستة أشهر، والآخر لأكثر منه، وبينهما أقل من نصف، يثبت الولاء لموالي الأم، ولا ينتقل إلى موالي الأب؛ لأنهما توأمين. وإنما قلنا: "وجاءت بالولد لأقل من ستة أشهر"؛ لأنها لو جاءت لستة أشهر أو أكثر منها، فالحكم ليس كذلك كما سيأتي، وإنما قيدنا إعتاق الأمة حال قيام نكاح الزوج القن؛ لأن ما بعد النكاح لا يتأتى فيه هذا التفصيل، ووصف الزوج بالقن ليس للاحتراز، بل هو على سبيل التمثيل؛ لأن حكم الزوج المكاتب والمدبر كذلك. (ملتقط) ولاء الحمل عن موالي الأم أبدا، فإن ولدت بعد عتقها لأكثر من ستة أشهر، فولاؤه إلى موالي الأب أي الولد لمولى الأم، فإن عتق العبد جرّ ولاء ابنه إلى مواليه. أي موالي الأب أبدا حتى لو أعتق الأب لا يجر ولاؤه إلى موالي الأب. فإن ولدت إلخ يعني إذا أعتق رجل أمة حاملا من زوجها القن، وولدت لأكثر من ستة أشهر أو لستة أشهر فولاؤه لموالي الأم؛ لأن الولد جزؤها، فيتبعها في الصفات الشرعية، ألا تری أنه يتبعها في الحرية، فكذا الولاء عند تعذر جعله تبعا للأب لرقه تكملة البحر الرائق: ۱۳۰/۸] ولو لم يكتف المصنف على قوله: "الأكثر من ستة أشهر بل قال: لستة أشهر أو أكثر منها" لكان أولى. واعلم أن هذه الصورة هي الصورة الأولى بعينها إلا أنها في الأولى جاءت بالولد لأقل من ستة أشهر، وههنا جاءت لستة أشهر أو أكثر منها، والفرق بين حكمهما بعد أن تثبت الولاء فيهما لموالي الأم أن في الأولى لم يمكن . جر الولاء إلى موالي الأب، وفي هذه الصورة يمكن الجر كما بينه المصنف. التكملة والفتح مع زيادة من المحشي) جر ولاء إلخ يعني في الصورة المذكورة، وهي أن جاءت بالولد لستة أشهر أو أكثر منها إن عتق زوجها جر ولاء ابنه إلى مواليه؛ لأن الولاء كالنسب والأصل فيه: أن يكون للأب إلا أنه تعذر ،لرقه، فإذا أعتق الأب أمكن نسبته إليه، فجعل الولد تبعا له أولى من جعله تبعا للأم، قال علي: "الولاء لحمة كلحمة النسب"، والنسب إلى الآباء، فكذا الولاء ينتقل إلى موالي الأب إذا زال المانع كولد الملاعنة يثبت نسبه من قوم الأم، فإذا أكذب نفسه ينتقل إلى الأب؛ لزوال المانع. فإن قيل: الولاء كالنسب، وهو لا يحتمل الفسخ بعد ثبوته، قلنا: لم ينفسخ بل حدث ولاء أقوى منه فقدم عليه كما قيل: الأخ عصبة، فإذا حدث من هو أولى منه بالإرث لا يبطل تعصيبه ولكنه يقدم، وهذا إذا لم تكن الأمة معتدة، وإن كانت معتدة فجاءت بولد لأكثر من ستة أشهر من وقت العتق ولأقل من سنتين من وقت الفراق لا ينتقل ولاؤه إلى موالي الأب، وقد أشرنا إلى هذا في حاشية قول المصنف: ولا ينتقل ولاء الحمل فتذكره، والأصل في ثبوت جر الولاء من موالي الأم إلى موالي الأب أنه مروي عن علي وعمر وعبد وزيد بن ثابت له ولا يعرف لهم مخالف، واعلم أن جر الولاء في هذه الصورة مقيد بما إذا أعتق العبد قبل موت الابن، وأما بعد موته فلا جر. (ملخص الشروح والحواشي)
Al-qinn: the slave owned by another man; she was freed and her pregnancy was freed. (Ayni) 'It does not transfer' etc.: meaning if a man freed a pregnant slave woman whose husband is a qinn owned by another, while her marriage exists, and she gives birth to a child in less than six months, the wala' of the pregnancy does not transfer from the mother's mawali to the father's mawali ever; because the fetus is freed by the freeing of its mother, and freeing of the mother is intended, so it is freed intentionally as well, because it is a part of the mother, and the master performed the emancipation on all her parts intentionally, and wala' does not transfer from the emancipator, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Wala' is for the one who frees.' And the existence of the pregnancy at the time of freeing is known by her giving birth in less than six months from the time of freeing, to be certain of the time of conception. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 304/2) And likewise if she gives birth to two children, one at less than six months and the other at more, with less than six months interval, wala' is established for the mother's mawali and does not transfer to the father's mawali because they are twins. And we only said: 'she gave birth in less than six months' because if she gives birth at six months or more, the ruling is otherwise as will come. And we restricted the freeing of the slave-woman while the marriage of her qinn husband exists, because after marriage this detail does not apply, and describing the husband as qinn is not restrictive but by way of example, because the ruling of the mukatib and mudabbar husband is the same. A child born to a freed slave-woman after six months or more: his wala' goes to the mother's master. Then if the slave-husband is freed, he draws the wala' of his son to his (the father's) mawali. Meaning the father's mawali ever, even if the father is freed, he does not draw his wala' to the father's mawali. 'If she gives birth' etc.: meaning if a man freed a pregnant slave-woman whose husband is a qinn, and she gives birth after six months or at six months, her child's wala' is for the mother's mawali; because the child is a part of her, so it follows her in shari'a attributes; do you not see that he follows her in freedom? So too with wala' when making him follow the father is prevented due to the father's slavery. (Mukhtasar from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 130/8) And if the author had not been satisfied with his statement 'more than six months' but said 'six months or more' it would have been better. And know that this scenario is exactly the first scenario except that in the first she gave birth in less than six months, and here she gave birth at six months or more, and the difference between their rulings after wala' is established for the mother's mawali in both is that in the first it is not possible to draw the wala' to the father's mawali, while in this scenario it is possible to draw it as the author explained. 'Draws wala' etc.: meaning in the mentioned scenario, when she gives birth at six months or more, if her husband is freed, he draws the wala' of his son to his mawali; because wala' is like lineage, and the principle is that it belongs to the father, but it was prevented due to his slavery; when the father is freed, it becomes possible to attribute the child to him, so making the child follow him is more appropriate than making him follow the mother. 'Ali said: 'Wala' is a bond like the bond of lineage.' And lineage is to the fathers, so too wala' transfers to the father's mawali when the impediment is removed, like the child of li'an: its lineage is established from the mother's family, and if the father retracts his accusation, the lineage transfers to the father due to the removal of the impediment. If it is said: wala' is like lineage, and it cannot be rescinded after being established, we say: it is not rescinded; rather, a stronger wala' occurs and takes precedence over it, as it is said: the brother is an 'asaba, and if someone more entitled to inheritance appears, his ta'sib is not nullified but he is given precedence. This is when the slave-woman is not in 'idda; if she is in 'idda and gives birth at more than six months from the time of freeing and less than two years from the separation, his wala' does not transfer to the father's mawali. We have indicated this in the gloss on the author's statement 'and the wala' of the pregnancy does not transfer,' so remember it. The basis for establishing the drawing of wala' from the mother's mawali to the father's mawali is that it is narrated from 'Ali, 'Umar, 'Abd, and Zayd ibn Thabit, and no opposition to them is known. And know that the drawing of wala' in this scenario is conditioned upon the father being freed before the son's death; after his death there is no drawing. (Mukhtasar of commentaries and glosses)
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the wala' of a child born to a freed pregnant slave woman whose husband is a slave. The Hanafi ruling distinguishes based on the timing of birth relative to the freeing. If the child is born within less than six months of the master freeing the mother, the child's wala' remains permanently with the mother's master (the freed person's master), and even if the father is later freed, the wala' does not transfer. This is because the mother's freedom is the direct cause, and the hadith 'wala' is for the one who frees' applies. If the child is born exactly six months or more after the freeing, initially the wala' is also with the mother's master, but if the father is subsequently freed before the child dies, the child's wala' transfers to the father's master. The reasoning is that wala' is analogous to lineage, and lineage is through the father; the father's slavery prevented attachment to his side, but when he is freed, the impediment is removed, and it is more appropriate to attach the child to the father's wala'. This is supported by the statement of 'Ali that wala' is like lineage, and the analogy to a child of li'an. The passage also addresses an objection that wala' cannot be transferred once established: the answer is that the original wala' is not nullified but a stronger wala' takes precedence. Finally, the passage notes that the father must be freed before the child's death for the transfer to occur.

Key Terms
قن (qinn): A full slave owned by someone else.
جر الولاء (jarr al-wala'): The transfer of wala' from one set of mawali to another due to a change in legal status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pregnant slave woman is freed and gives birth exactly six months later, and the slave father is freed afterward, what happens to the child's wala'?
A) Remains with mother's master permanently
B) Transfers to father's master if father freed before child dies
C) Goes to the child's choice
D) Divided equally between both masters

Key Takeaway
The wala' of a child born to a freed pregnant slave can transfer to the father's master if the child is born six months or more after the freeing and the father is freed before the child's death, based on analogy to lineage and removal of the impediment of slavery.

Free 'Ajami Man Marries Freedwoman: Dispute on Child's Wala'
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wala' of child when free 'ajami marries freedwoman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the wala' of a child born to a free 'ajami man and a freedwoman, identify the proofs of each side, and determine the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When a free 'ajami marries a freedwoman, the child's wala' goes to the mother's master—because emancipation wala' cannot be rescinded.

This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute about the wala' of a child born to a free non-Arab (ajami) man and a freedwoman (mu'taqa). The disagreement centers on whether the child's wala' follows the mother's emancipation or the father's potential alliance (muwalat). By studying this dispute, you will learn to weigh competing proofs within the Hanafi school and understand the principle that stronger legal ties prevail over weaker ones.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the issue
The husband is a free 'ajami (non-Arab) who was never a slave; the wife is a freedwoman (mu'taqa) with a master. They have a child. The dispute: to whom belongs the child's wala'?
Note that 'ajami means non-Arab, regardless of religion.
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
According to the two imams, the child's wala' goes to the mother's master, irrespective of whether the father has muwalat or not.
This is the position presented first in the text.
3
State the position of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf holds that the child's wala' follows the father's side, just as lineage (nasab) follows the father.
Abu Yusuf considers wala' analogous to lineage.
4
Analyse the proofs
The two argue that wala' of emancipation is stronger because it is irrevocable (cannot be rescinded), unlike muwalat which can be rescinded. Abu Yusuf analogizes wala' to nasab, which is patrilineal.
The strength of proof determines tarjih.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practically, under the majority view the child's wala' belongs to the mother's master; under Abu Yusuf it belongs to the father's mawali. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) view is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
If the father is Arab, the dispute does not arise as the child's nasab follows the father's tribe.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عجمي تزوج إلخ [ أي حر عجمي لم يعتقه أحد صورة المسألة: أن رجلا من غير العرب حر لم يمسه رق، تزوج معتقة لرجل سواء كانت معتقة لعجمي أو عربي، وسواء كانت عربية أو عجمية، فولدت المعتقة منه ولدا، فولاء الولد لموالي الأم، سواء كان للعجمي ولاء الموالاة بأن كان أبوه كافرا فأسلم فتزوج بمعتقة ثم والى رجلا، أو لم يكن له ولاء، وهذا عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف حكم الولد حكم أبيه في الوجهين، ولا يكون ولاء الولد لموالي الأم؛ لأنه كالنسب والنسب إلى الأب، وإن كانت الأم أشرف؛ لكونه أقوى، فكذا الولاء، ولهما: أن ولاء العتق أقوى من ولاء الموالاة؛ لأن ولاء العتق لا يحتمل الفسخ، وولاء الموالاة يحتمل الفسخ، فرجح الأكد الأقوى على الأضعف قيد بكون الزوج عجميا؛ العربي إذا تزوج معتقة، فإن ولده منها ينسب إلى قومه دونها،
An 'ajami man married a freedwoman: [the commentary] i.e., a free 'ajami man who was never freed by anyone. The image of the issue: a man from non-Arabs, free, never touched by slavery, married a woman freed by a man, whether the freedwoman is freed by an 'ajami or an Arab, and whether she is Arab or 'ajami. Then the freedwoman gives birth to a child from him. The wala' of the child belongs to the mother's master, whether the 'ajami has wala' of muwalat (because his father was a kafir, he embraced Islam, married a mu'taqa, and then made a wala' with a man) or he has no wala'. This is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). According to Abu Yusuf, the child's ruling follows the father in both cases, and the child's wala' is not for the mother's master, because it is like lineage, and lineage is to the father, even if the mother is of higher standing, because it is stronger. So too with wala'. And their (the two's) argument: wala' of emancipation is stronger than wala' of muwalat, because wala' of emancipation cannot be rescinded, while wala' of muwalat can be rescinded. Therefore the stronger and more firmly established outweighs the weaker. The restriction is that the husband is 'ajami; if an Arab marries a mu'taqa, his child is attributed to his own tribe, not hers.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the wala' of a child born to a free 'ajami man (a non-Arab who has no Arab lineage and has never been a slave) and a freedwoman (mu'taqa) who has a master. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the child's wala' goes to the mother's master regardless of whether the father has wala' of muwalat (clientage by alliance) or not. Their reasoning is that the mother's wala' is by emancipation, which is stronger and cannot be rescinded, whereas the father's potential wala' by muwalat can be rescinded, so the stronger wala' takes priority. Abu Yusuf disagrees, arguing that wala' is like lineage, and lineage follows the father; therefore the child's wala' should follow the father's side, even if the mother is of higher social standing. The text notes that this dispute applies only when the father is 'ajami; if the father is Arab, his child automatically belongs to his tribe and the question of wala' from the mother does not arise.

Key Terms
عجمي ('ajami): A non-Arab, free man who has never been a slave or been freed.
ولاء الموالاة (wala' al-muwalat): Clientage established by a contract of alliance (not by emancipation), can be rescinded.
معتقة (mu'taqa): A woman who has been freed by someone (she has a master).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, what is the wala' of a child born to a free 'ajami man and a freedwoman?
A) Goes to the father's tribe
B) Goes to the mother's master
C) Goes to the child's own choice
D) Goes to both equally

Key Takeaway
When a free 'ajami man marries a freedwoman, the child's wala' goes to the mother's master, as the stronger emancipation wala' overrides the father's weaker muwalat.

Transfer of Wala' from Mother's Master to Father's Master
Ruling with proof on wala' transfer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which the wala' of a child born to a freedwoman transfers to the father's master, and explain the legal reasoning (ijma of Companions) that supports this transfer.

Core Idea
A child's wala' transfers from mother's master to father's master when the father is freed and the child is born at six months or more after emancipation.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains a nuanced ruling in the Hanafi school: the transfer (jarr) of wala' from the mother's masters to the father's masters. While the general rule is that the child's wala' follows the mother, an exception arises when the father is later freed. The passage establishes the conditions and proofs for this transfer, including a consensus of major Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
The base rule is that the wala' of a child born to a pregnant freedwoman belongs to the mother's master forever. This is established because the child was part of the mother at the time of emancipation.
This default is from the principle that the child follows the mother in legal attributes like freedom.
2
Recognize the exception
If the child is born at six months or more after the mother's emancipation, and the father (a slave at birth) is subsequently freed, the wala' can be pulled (jarr) to the father's master. The transfer occurs only if the father is freed before the child's death.
The six-month condition indicates a viable pregnancy at the time of emancipation.
3
Understand the legal reasoning
The child's wala' is analogous to lineage (nasab). Lineage ideally traces to the father, but the father's slavery at the child's birth prevented this. Once the obstacle of slavery is removed, the wala' follows the father as lineage would.
The passage likens this to the retraction of li'an accusation, where lineage transfers from mother to father.
4
Examine the proof: Ijma of Companions
The practice of transferring wala' from mother's master to father's master is reported from Ali, Umar, Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, and Zayd ibn Thabit, with no known dissenter. This consensus (ijma) serves as the primary daleel.
The ijma is considered zanni in transmission but authoritative in the Hanafi school.
5
Note the special case of iddah
If the mother is in her waiting period (iddah) from a previous marriage and gives birth after more than six months from emancipation but before two years from separation, the wala' does not transfer to the father's master. This exception preserves the original rule.
This is based on an annotation in the author's own work, indicating careful boundary drawing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حق الولاء
الأمة ولاء الحمل عن موالي الأم أبدا، فإن ولدت بعد عتقها لأكثر من ستة أشهر، فولاؤه إلى موالي الأب أي الولد لمولى الأم، فإن عتق العبد جرّ ولاء ابنه إلى مواليه. عجمي تزوّج معتقة، في هذه المسألة المذكورة
أي موالي الأب
أبدا حتى لو أعتق الأب لا يجر ولاؤه إلى موالي الأب. فإن ولدت إلخ يعني إذا أعتق رجل أمة حاملا من زوجها القن، وولدت لأكثر من ستة أشهر أو لستة أشهر فولاؤه لموالي الأم؛ لأن الولد جزؤها، فيتبعها في الصفات الشرعية، ألا تری أنه يتبعها في الحرية، فكذا الولاء عند تعذر جعله تبعا للأب لرقه تكملة البحر الرائق: ۱۳۰/۸] ولو لم يكتف المصنف على قوله: "الأكثر من ستة أشهر بل قال: لستة أشهر أو أكثر منها" لكان أولى. واعلم أن هذه الصورة هي الصورة الأولى بعينها إلا أنها في الأولى جاءت بالولد لأقل من ستة أشهر، وههنا جاءت لستة أشهر أو أكثر منها، والفرق بين حكمهما بعد أن تثبت الولاء فيهما لموالي الأم أن في الأولى لم يمكن . جر الولاء إلى موالي الأب، وفي هذه الصورة يمكن الجر كما بينه المصنف. التكملة والفتح مع زيادة من المحشي) جر ولاء إلخ يعني في الصورة المذكورة، وهي أن جاءت بالولد لستة أشهر أو أكثر منها إن عتق زوجها جر ولاء ابنه إلى مواليه؛ لأن الولاء كالنسب والأصل فيه: أن يكون للأب إلا أنه تعذر ،لرقه، فإذا أعتق الأب أمكن نسبته إليه، فجعل الولد تبعا له أولى من جعله تبعا للأم، قال علي: "الولاء لحمة كلحمة النسب"، والنسب إلى الآباء، فكذا الولاء ينتقل إلى موالي الأب إذا زال المانع كولد الملاعنة يثبت نسبه من قوم الأم، فإذا أكذب نفسه ينتقل إلى الأب؛ لزوال المانع.
فإن قيل: الولاء كالنسب، وهو لا يحتمل الفسخ بعد ثبوته، قلنا: لم ينفسخ بل حدث ولاء أقوى منه فقدم عليه كما قيل: الأخ عصبة، فإذا حدث من هو أولى منه بالإرث لا يبطل تعصيبه ولكنه يقدم، وهذا إذا لم تكن الأمة معتدة، وإن كانت معتدة فجاءت بولد لأكثر من ستة أشهر من وقت العتق ولأقل من سنتين من وقت الفراق لا ينتقل ولاؤه إلى موالي الأب، وقد أشرنا إلى هذا في حاشية قول المصنف: ولا ينتقل ولاء الحمل فتذكره، والأصل في ثبوت جر الولاء من موالي الأم إلى موالي الأب أنه مروي عن علي وعمر وعبد وزيد بن ثابت له ولا يعرف لهم مخالف، واعلم أن جر الولاء في هذه الصورة مقيد بما إذا أعتق العبد قبل موت الابن، وأما بعد موته فلا جر. (ملخص الشروح والحواشي)
Right of patronage: The patronage of a fetus belongs to the mother's masters forever. If she gives birth after her emancipation after more than six months, his patronage belongs to the father's masters, i.e., the child belongs to the mother's master. If the slave (father) is freed, he pulls the patronage of his son to his masters. (Commentary: meaning the father's masters forever; even if the father is freed, he does not pull his patronage to the father's masters. 'Then if she gives birth' etc. means if a man frees a pregnant slave woman from her slave husband, and she gives birth after more than six months or at six months, his patronage belongs to the mother's masters because the child is part of her, so it follows her in legal attributes. Do you not see that it follows her in freedom? So too is patronage when it is impossible to make it follow the father due to his slavery. Completion of Bahr al-Raiq: 8/130. It would have been better if the author did not restrict his statement to 'more than six months' but said 'six months or more'. Know that this scenario is exactly the first scenario except that in the first the child came at less than six months, and here at six months or more. The difference between their rulings, after establishing patronage for the mother's masters in both, is that in the first it was not possible to pull patronage to the father's masters, but in this scenario it is possible as the author explained. (Completion and al-Fath with addition from the annotator) 'He pulls the patronage' etc. means in the mentioned scenario, which is that she gives birth at six months or more, if her husband is freed, he pulls the patronage of his son to his masters because patronage is like lineage, and in principle it should belong to the father, but it was impossible due to his slavery. When the father is freed, it becomes possible to attribute him to him, so making the child follow him is more appropriate than making him follow the mother. Ali said: 'Patronage is a bond like the bond of lineage.' Lineage goes to fathers, so too patronage transfers to the father's masters when the obstacle is removed, like the child of a woman condemned by li'an: his lineage is established from the mother's tribe, but if he retracts his accusation, it transfers to the father due to removal of the obstacle. If it is said: Patronage is like lineage, and it does not permit dissolution after its establishment, we say: It is not dissolved; rather a stronger patronage arises and is given precedence, just as it is said: A brother is an asaba, and if someone more entitled to inheritance appears, his being an asaba is not nullified but he is given precedence. This is when the slave woman is not in her waiting period. If she is in her waiting period and gives birth to a child after more than six months from the time of emancipation and less than two years from the time of separation, his patronage does not transfer to the father's masters. We have alluded to this in the annotation of the author's statement: 'The patronage of the fetus does not transfer.' So remember it. The basis for the establishment of pulling patronage from the mother's masters to the father's masters is that it is narrated from Ali, Umar, Abdullah, and Zayd ibn Thabit, may Allah be pleased with them, and no dissenter is known among them. Know that pulling patronage in this scenario is conditioned upon the slave being freed before the son's death. As for after his death, there is no pulling. (Summary of commentaries and glosses)
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the transfer of wala' (patronage) of a child born to a pregnant slave woman who is freed before delivery. The author states the general principle: the wala' of such a child belongs to the mother's masters forever. However, there is an exception: if the child is born after six months or more from the time of emancipation, and the father is later freed, the father's master can pull the wala' to himself. This is because the child is part of the mother, so it follows her in legal attributes like freedom. But the wala' is like lineage, which should ideally go to the father, but due to the father's slavery at birth, it is impossible. When the father is freed, the obstacle is removed, and the child's wala' follows the father. This is analogous to the case of a child of a woman condemned by li'an: the child's lineage is initially established from the mother's tribe, but if the father retracts his accusation, the lineage transfers to him. The proof for this transfer is a consensus of the Companions: Ali, Umar, Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, and Zayd ibn Thabit, with no known dissenter. The passage also discusses a scenario where the woman is in her waiting period: if she gives birth after more than six months from emancipation but less than two years from separation, the wala' does not transfer. This condition is derived from a note in the author's own work.

Key Terms
ولاء الحمل (wala' al-haml): The patronage (freedman relationship) of a fetus/unborn child, specifically the child of a pregnant slave woman who is freed before birth.
جر الولاء (jarr al-wala'): The act of transferring/pulling the wala' from the mother's master to the father's master when the father is later freed.
موالي الأم/الأب (mawali al-umm/al-ab): The masters (emancipators) of the mother or father respectively, who hold the wala' over the freedperson.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition can the wala' of a child born to a freedwoman be transferred to the father's master?
A) If the child is born within six months of emancipation.
B) If the father is freed before the child's death and the child is born at six months or more after emancipation.
C) If the mother is in her waiting period and the child is born after two years.
D) The wala' never transfers from the mother's master.

Key Takeaway
The wala' of a child born to a freedwoman can transfer to the father's master if the father is freed before the child's death and the child was born at six months or more after emancipation, based on the consensus of major Companions.

intermediate
8 min
Wala' of a Child from a Non-Arab Father and Freedwoman Mother
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on wala' attribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on the wala' of a child born to a free non-Arab father and a freedwoman mother, explain the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and identify the practical difference between their view and that of Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
When a free non-Arab marries a freedwoman, the child's wala' belongs to the mother's master because emancipation's bond cannot be dissolved.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the wala' of a child born to a free non-Arab man and a freedwoman. The majority of the school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani) holds that the wala' goes to the mother's master (mu'tiq), while Abu Yusuf argues it follows the father. Their disagreement hinges on whether wala' is more like lineage or whether the strength of emancipation overrides analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the Case
Identify the parties: a free non-Arab man (ajami) who has never been enslaved marries a freedwoman (of any background). She gives birth to a child. The question: Where does the wala' of this child belong?
The father is free, so he has no wala' of emancipation (only possible wala' of allegiance). The mother's wala' is from emancipation.
2
Identify the Majority Position
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the child's wala' belongs to the mother's master (or his agnates) regardless of whether the father has a wala' of allegiance or not.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Analyze the Majority's Proof
Their reasoning is that wala' of emancipation (wala' al-itiq) is stronger than wala' of allegiance (wala' al-muwalah) because the former cannot be dissolved while the latter can. Since the stronger prevails, the child's wala' attaches to the mother's emancipator.
This is a reasoning based on the inherent strength of the bond.
4
State Abu Yusuf's Position and Proof
Abu Yusuf holds that the child's wala' follows the father, because wala' is analogous to lineage (nasab), and lineage is traced to the father. Therefore, the child's wala' should be on the father's side even if the mother is freed.
He uses qiyas on nasab, not on the strength of bonds.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence appears when the child dies. According to the majority, inheritance from the child goes to the mother's master (or his agnates). According to Abu Yusuf, it goes to the child's dhawi al-arham (uterine relatives) because the father's side does not have a valid wala' holder.
This difference directly impacts estate distribution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عجمي تزوج إلخ [ أي حر عجمي لم يعتقه أحد صورة المسألة: أن رجلا من غير العرب حر لم يمسه رق، تزوج معتقة لرجل سواء كانت معتقة لعجمي أو عربي، وسواء كانت عربية أو عجمية، فولدت المعتقة منه ولدا، فولاء الولد لموالي الأم، سواء كان للعجمي ولاء الموالاة بأن كان أبوه كافرا فأسلم فتزوج بمعتقة ثم والى رجلا، أو لم يكن له ولاء، وهذا عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف حكم الولد حكم أبيه في الوجهين، ولا يكون ولاء الولد لموالي الأم؛ لأنه كالنسب والنسب إلى الأب، وإن كانت الأم أشرف؛ لكونه أقوى، فكذا الولاء، ولهما: أن ولاء العتق أقوى من ولاء الموالاة؛ لأن ولاء العتق لا يحتمل الفسخ، وولاء الموالاة يحتمل الفسخ، فرجح الأكد الأقوى على الأضعف قيد بكون الزوج عجميا؛ العربي إذا تزوج معتقة، فإن ولده منها ينسب إلى قومه دونها،

(عيني، تكملة وغيرها)
A non-Arab marries a freedwoman, etc. [i.e., a free non-Arab who has never been enslaved. The case: A free man from non-Arabs who has never been enslaved marries a freedwoman of a man, whether she is a freedwoman of a non-Arab or an Arab, and whether she is Arab or non-Arab. She gives birth to a child. The wala' of the child belongs to the mother's masters, whether the non-Arab has wala' of allegiance (his father was a disbeliever and he became Muslim and married a freedwoman then made an allegiance contract) or he has no wala'. This is according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). According to Abu Yusuf, the child follows his father in both cases, and the child's wala' does not go to the mother's masters because it is like lineage, and lineage is to the father, even if the mother is nobler due to being stronger. So too is wala'. Their (the two's) argument: The wala' of emancipation is stronger than the wala' of allegiance because wala' of emancipation cannot be dissolved, while wala' of allegiance can be dissolved. So the stronger outweighs the weaker. The restriction that the husband is non-Arab is because if an Arab man marries a freedwoman, his child is attributed to his tribe, not hers. [PAGE_220]... The child's wala' is to her masters, even if he (the father) has wala' of allegiance. And the emancipator (mu'tiq) is given precedence over dhawi al-arham (uterine relatives) in inheritance, but is behind the agnates by lineage. So if the client (the freedperson) dies, then the emancipator dies, his inheritance goes to the nearest (agnate of the emancipator). The restriction that she is a freedwoman is because if a non-Arab marries a free Arab woman, her child is attributed to his tribe, not hers. The author sufficed with saying 'freedwoman' and did not say 'freedwoman of the Arabs' as al-Quduri said, because the difference is absolute regarding freedwomen, and al-Quduri's restriction to Arabs is incidental. Know that the fruit of this difference appears if this child dies, leaving his aunt and other dhawi al-arham, and the emancipator of his mother or his agnates. The wealth goes to the mother's emancipator or his agnates according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). According to Abu Yusuf, it goes to dhawi al-arham. We only intend a free non-Arab because if he were a slave, the child would be attributed to the mother's masters by consensus. (Ayni, Completion, etc.)
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the wala' of a child born to a free non-Arab (ajami) man and a freedwoman. The majority view of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani is that the child's wala' belongs to the mother's master (mu'tiq). This holds true whether or not the father has a wala' of allegiance (wala' al-muwalah) with someone. Their reasoning is that wala' of emancipation (wala' al-itiq) is stronger than wala' of allegiance because the former cannot be dissolved, while the latter can. Thus, the stronger prevails. In contrast, Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the child's wala' follows the father, because wala' is like lineage, and lineage is traced through the father, even if the mother is of higher status due to freedom. The practical consequence (thamarah) of this difference: if the child dies leaving his aunt (or other dhawi al-arham) and the mother's master (or his agnates), Abu Hanifa and Muhammad give the inheritance to the mother's master or his agnates, while Abu Yusuf gives it to the dhawi al-arham. The restriction that the father is non-Arab is because if the father were Arab, the child would be attributed to his tribe in lineage, which affects the wala' ruling. Al-Quduri had restricted the case to 'freedwoman of the Arabs,' but the author (Kanz al-Daqaiq) does not, because the ruling applies generally to any freedwoman.

Key Terms
عجمي (ajami): A non-Arab person, specifically a free man who is not of Arab lineage.
ولاء الموالاة (wala' al-muwalah): A patronage relationship established by contract (between a Muslim and another) of mutual inheritance, not by emancipation. It is weaker and can be dissolved.
ولاء العتق (wala' al-itiq): The patronage relationship that arises from emancipation (manumission). It is a strong bond that cannot be dissolved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, when a free non-Arab man marries a freedwoman, whose master holds the wala' of their child?
A) The father's master, because wala' follows lineage.
B) The mother's master, because wala' of emancipation is stronger.
C) The father's master if he has wala' of allegiance, otherwise the mother's.
D) The child has no wala' because both parents are free.

Key Takeaway
In an intra-Hanafi dispute, the majority view that wala' of emancipation overrides wala' of allegiance is the mufta bihi, determining that the child's wala' goes to the mother's master.
